I. MAIN CAMPAIGN | MNCM |
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
001) HE CAN'T BE FAR                                                     [M001]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Flashback: nighttime in Farewell, Oregon. Chaos ensues everywhere. Near an
 alleyway, main character Deacon, his wife Sarah, and his riding buddy Boozer
 are contemplating escape.]

PA: Get to the nearest rooftop and stay there. Help will come. This is the
    National Emergency Response Organization. Repeat — All evacuees get off
    the streets. Remain indoors.

Deacon: Uh, she's burnin' up, the, uh, knife must have — nicked her kidney or
        somethin'. She's turning septic.

Boozer: How you doin'¹ little sister.

Sarah: So stupid. It was this little — this little kid, this — this Goddamn
       little kid.

Boozer: With a big Goddamn knife.
Deacon: Hey, help me. C'mon.

[They try lifting the wounded up Sarah up.]

Boozer: Ah, c'mon. Hey —
Sarah: Shit —

[They stop and listen for yelling nearby.]

Boozer: Another mob. We don't wanna be here when they come through.
Deacon: We gotta get to the roof. Flag down one of those choppers.
Boozer: Alright.

[Later, on a rooftop. A chopper is waiting there.]

Deacon: Wait, we need help — she's been wounded.
O'Brian: Wh — wh — what's wrong with her?

Deacon: Well she's not — whatever the hell's going on out there. She's been
        stabbed.

O'Brian: I can't take anymore.

[Deacon looks at his nametag.]

Deacon: Okay, listen. O'Brian? If we don't get her to a hospital, she's going
        to die.

O'Brian: There are no more hospitals.

Deacon: Oh c'mon, no more hospitals? You got, uh, doctors, you got triage, you
        got a MASH unit?

O'Brian: Uh, look I'm just a grad student, okay? I — I got volunteered for
         this, I'm not even supposed to be out here —

[Deacon waves a pistol in his face.]

Deacon: O'Brian.

O'Brian: Okay. Shit. I've only got room for two of you, okay? Two.

Deacon: What do you mean you've only got room for two of us, what do —

O'Brian: We're overweight, okay? I can only take two of you. Two.

Deacon: Okay. C'mon. Help me. C'mon. Alright¹ sweetheart. It's okay. You're
        gonna be alright.

[They lift her into the chopper.]

O'Brian: I got her.

Deacon: Hey, I'm gonna be right back.

[He walks over to Boozer, who's leaning near the rooftop door.]

Deacon: Okay, Boozer, let's go. We gotta get on that —

Boozer: Hold on. Hold on.

Deacon: We gotta get on that chopper.

Boozer: I heard what he said. There's only room for two on that chopper. Go.
        Go with her. I'll be okay.

[Deacon sees Boozer's lag is gashed open.]

Boozer: Look, I've been through worse shit than this before, yeah?

Deacon: Yeah, we have.

[He walks back to the heli.]

Deacon: Where are you going?
O'Brian: What?
Deacon: Where? Where?
O'Brian: Refugee camp, west of Three Fingered Jack.
Sarah: No.
Deacon: Boozer is never gonna make it without me.

[He takes off his Mongrels ring and slides it onto her finger.]

Deacon: I want this back.
O'Brian: You coming?
Sarah: No.

[The chopper lifts off.]

Boozer: Deek! Oh, shit. What did you do?

[Flashback ends. Scene: two years later, Boozer and Deacon are riding down a
 highway on O'Leary Mountain. They stop at the Old Pioneer Cemetery.]

Deacon: We lost 'im.
Boozer: He can't be far.
Deacon: Wait, hold on. Cut your engine.

[Nearby, an mortally injured woman is slumped near a monument.]

Boozer: Shit, she's alive. Alvarez. Alvarez, hey. Alvarez, what happened here?
        I mean, who did this? Was it — was it Rippers?

Alvarez: Leon — did this.

[Alvarez succumbs to her wounds.]

Deacon: Fucking Leon.

[Leon rides by on his bike.]

Boozer: C'mon.

[The two friends start their pursuit. Leon fires blindly behind him.]

Deacon: Oh shit!
Boozer: He's got ammo!
Deacon: No shit — he can't have much —

[Even as Leon slings molotovs, they're still hot on his heels.]

Boozer: You like that? Yeah? You sonofabitch!
Deacon: You hit him —
Boozer: Yeah, I think so — Whoa, whoa! Hold up, hold up! He laid his bike down.

[As they stop riding, they hit the deck when shots ring from the forest.]

Deacon: Cover me.
Boozer: Right behind ya.
Deacon: He went that way.
Boozer: C'mon.

_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
002) WE'LL MAKE IT QUICK                                                 [M002]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Boozer and Deacon head into the forest, following Leon's tracks.]

Deacon: Where the hell's he goin'? There isn't shit out here but a buncha
        Freaks —

Boozer: Well maybe I was wrong — about him — havin' a deal with Copeland —

Deacon: No — Leon's been fencing shit to Copeland for a long time — finally
        caught up with him.

Boozer: Hey, hey — wait, wait, hold up. Hold up.

Deacon: Shit — alright — lemme see —

[He scours the tracks in the dirt.]

Deacon: Wait, wait, wait — here. Down this way — Tracks are fresh. So where
        the hell'd you learn to track shit anyway —

Boozer: Used to go elk huntin' with my old man when I was a kid — ended up
        tracking shit for miles — 

[They reach a small wilderness campground. Leon's bullet grazes Deacon.]

Boozer: Holy shit — get down!

[Leon realizes he's run out of ammo.]

Leon: Fuck.
Boozer: C'mon.

[They follow on foot.]

Boozer: You okay, brother?
Deacon: Yeah, yeah, yeah. Just a graze. Sonofabitch can't aim worth a damn.
Boozer: Sonofabitch — 
Deacon: I'm fine, Boozer —

[The path bends near a small waterfall.]

Deacon: He must be heading down there, toward the falls.
Boozer: He's losing a lot of blood — he's not getting far. Come on.

[They find Leon nearby, bleeding from Boozer's shotgun blast earlier.]

Deacon: Search him. Bleeding out. That's a helluva way to go. It's slow. Lotta
        pain. But I suppose you'd know all about that, right¹ Leon?

Boozer: She was breathin' when we found her, you piece of shit.

Leon: I wasn't going to waste a bullet, not on her.

Deacon: Hold on a second, hold on a second. Now, where's the stash, Leon.¹ If
        you tell us, well, unlike you, I can promise you we'll make it quick.

[A Freaker's cry rings in the distance.]

Deacon: Doesn't look like you'd be suffering for too long. Leon, you got a
        little problem here, see — They can smell your blood, from all the way
        down there. What do you suppose that feels like, huh? Torn apart, eaten
        alive?

Boozer: Guess he's gonna find out.
Leon: Fuck you.
Deacon: Goodbye Leon.
Leon: No. Wait. Alright, alright, don't, don't — I got it right here, take it.

[He hands Deacon a piece of paper.]

Deacon: Where?
Leon: In the cemetery. It's in the old cemetery.
Deacon: Thank you.
Leon: No, you said —

[Deacon whirls around with his gun pointed at Leon's head.]

Leon: Do it. Don't leave me out here, man. Do it. Do it! Ya goddamned liar.
      Do it.

[He pulls the trigger. Boozer picks up his camo baseball cap.]

Boozer: Tuck's gonna need somethin' for the bounty.

[They start heading back to the road.]

Boozer: You did the right thing¹ bro — we don't want to leave anyone to the
        Freaks — not even a piece of shit like Leon —

Deacon: Hey, hold up — I wanna search this camp, see if I can't find something
        to fix up this scratch.

[He finds ingredients 

Deacon: Now I just gotta — put 'em together — and — yes — There — yeah, that
        ought to do it — Guess I — won't be losin' the arm anytime soon —

[They continue onwards.]

Deacon: Thought we were going huntin' tonight. Take some bounties in to Tucker
        —

Boozer: Well not if it's pissing down rain.
Deacon: Nah¹ man — we need the camp credits — gotta stock up on supplies.
Boozer: Yeah, okay. I don't want to be out all night though.
Deacon: Jesus — I gotta get in shape —

[They reach their bikes again.]

Boozer: Gonna see if there's anything we can salvage on Leon's bike.
Deacon: No. Goddammit.
Boozer: What?
Deacon: Sonofabitch.

[A pool of gas is underneath Deacon's ride.]

Boozer: I'm guessing that's the fuel line, unless you just pissed yourself.
Deacon: It's the fuel pump. Leon, yeah, shot out my damn fuel pump. Can we get
        anything off Leon's bike?

Boozer: Nah, it's done. Look, let's just go back to O'Leary Mountain. We'll
        head out in the morning, find some parts, and come back and get your
        bike.

[Deacon looks up at an old billboard for Crazy Willie's.]

Deacon: No. I think I got a better idea. Why don't we just get it while we're
        out here?

Boozer: What?
Deacon: Well — Crazy Willie's isn't far from here. Let's just head over there.
Boozer: What're ya thinking?
Deacon: We were goin' out hunting tonight anyway. Crazy Willie's is as good a
        place as any.

Boozer: Yeah. Okay.

003) I SAY WE HEAD NORTH                                                 [M003]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon hops on Boozer's ride and they set off.]

Boozer: Hey, what did Leon give you?

Deacon: Map of some kind? Once we get my bike back, let's head up to the
        cemetery — look around.

Boozer: Yeah. Okay. So tomorrow, we get the drugs, take 'em to Tucker, collect
        on Leon's bounty. Then I say we head north.

Deacon: And you think shit's any different up north?

Boozer: Don't matter. I think it'd do us good, get the hell away from here.
        Hold on, something's blocking the road.

Deacon: Careful. I — saw a setup like this couple days ago — a bunch of Rippers
        blocked the road with an old truck.

Boozer: C'mon, help me move it. Ready?
Deacon: Yeah.
Boozer: Push —

[Drifters attack, catching them unawares as they push the vehicle out of the
 way. They're quickly dispatched.]

Deacon: C'mon. We're almost there.

[They hit the open road again.]

Boozer: Huh — we're comin' up on the old NERO checkpoint.
Deacon: We're almost there.

_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
004) BAD WAY TO GO OUT                                                   [M004]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[The duo stops at a vehicle-choked tunnel —— a prime ambush site.]

Boozer: Shit, how you wanna do this?

Deacon: Loan me your shotgun. I'll walk point. Looks like that checkpoint had
        'em backed up pretty good.

Boozer: Yeah, a lot of good it did 'em. Hell, I'd rather be buried back with
        the Goddamned pioneers.

Deacon: Yeah.

Boozer: Shit. Look at 'em all. Bunch of Goddamned dumbasses, the lot of 'em.
        What were they thinkin'.¹ "Hey, Mr. Fed, can we — sit here and wait
        'til a Goddamned horde comes through and just kills us all?"

Deacon: Bad way to go out, trapped in a shithole like this.

[They advance a ways, stopping near a smelly Freaker nest.]

Deacon: You smell that?
Boozer: Oh Jesus. There. C'mon, let's go.
Deacon: Wait, hold up. How many Molotovs you got left back there?
Boozer: Let's hit it on the way back. Leave it.
Deacon: Yeah. Leave it my ass.
Boozer: Sonofabitch, you're hopin' someone's home.

[Deacon throws a molotov into the nest, hearing an anguished cry within.]

Boozer: Sounds like you got your wish.

[After killing the Freakers, Deacon starts mashing one corpse's head in.]

Boozer: Deek? DEEK! Hey Deek, Deek, Deek, Deek. Bro, bro. I think it's dead.
        You're gonna break my shotgun.

Deacon: Yeah. Okay.
Boozer: Alright —

[Boozer gets back on the bike.]

Boozer: You're going up there again.
Deacon: What're you talking about?

Boozer: The Goddamned refugee camp. You only act like this when you're thinkin'
        about goin' up there.

Deacon: Act like what?
Boozer: It's not your fault that she's dead.
Deacon: Drop it.

Boozer: If you'd gotten on that chopper with Sarah, all that would've changed
        is you'd be dead too.

Deacon: Look, just drop it.

[Ahead, some Freakers show themselves and set off a car alarm.]

Deacon: Damn alarm. You're not getting your bike through there.

Boozer: Try that service tunnel — see if you can clear us a path from the other
        side.

Deacon: I got it. Just keep your headlight pointed that way —

[He enters the service tunnel and is soon startled by a Freaker.]

Deacon: Jesus!

[Deke clears the path but triggers another alarm.]

Deacon: Damn alarm.
Boozer: Jesus — Deek!?
Deacon: I didn't plan on this, Goddamnit!

[They slay the Freakers attracted to the location.]

Deacon: Another nest.
Boozer: Ugh, yeah — I smell it —
Deacon: How many Molotovs you got left?
Boozer: You just used the last one.
Deacon: You got any shit to make more?
Boozer: Yeah, yeah —
Deacon: This'll just take a sec —

[He gets some supplies from Boozer's saddlebag and torches another nest.]

Deacon: Ready?
Boozer: Shit — Here they come!

[They make it through the tunnel unscathed.]

Boozer: Hey, c'mon, get on.
Deacon: Yeah, okay. Gimme a sec.

[The pair blazes down the highway.]

Deacon: I've been thinking about what you said, about riding north.

Boozer: Just sayin' — you need to get away from here. Clear your head, you
        know?

Deacon: In the morning, let's turn in the bounties and we'll hit the road.

Boozer: Hell yeah, brother. Now you're talkin'.

[They reach Crazy Willie's and it's teeming with enemies.]

Boozer: You wanted a Freakshow.
Deacon: Shit.

Boozer: Place is crawlin'. Shit, we're gonna need more ammo. What're you
        thinkin'? And I already know it's a bad idea.

Deacon: You just — ride on through. You pull as many of 'em off as you can.
        And I just, I go in through the back, down that hill, find the garage.

Boozer: Shit.
Deacon: Alright, you just give me a few minutes to find the part that I need
        — You ride back, we ride the hell out. After I kill a few of the
        bastards.

Boozer: I swear to God, you got a death wish.
Deacon: Like I said, not tonight.

[Boozer rides off as loudly as possible.]

Boozer: C'mon, you stinkin' sonsofbitches! Come on! That's right! Here I am,
        motherfuckers! Ol' Bill's right here!

005) YOU GOT A DEATH WISH                                                [M005]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After continuing through the motel area, Deacon nears the garage. Boozer
 radios in.]

Boozer: Deek, how's it goin'¹ brother? You ready?
Deacon: Not yet. Still gotta find a way into Willie's garage. Gotta be a fuel
        pump inside.

Boozer: Well hurry your ass up. I rode past one of those — uh — what the hell
        do you call 'em? The — the shit that Rippers put up —

Deacon: Sigils —
Boozer: Yeah — and it means they're up here somewhere —

[Deek nears the garage.]

Deacon: Shit. Boarded up. Gotta find another way in. Maybe there's a — way in
        through the roof.

[He climbs an old shed to ascend higher.]

Deacon: Yeah — that's what I thought —

[A hole in the roof leads towards the garage.]

Deacon: Gotta be a fuel pump in here somewhere.

[He strips the part off an old chopper.]

Deacon: Boozer, you there? I found the part. I'm heading out to the highway —
Boozer: Deek. Rippers. Rippers! No, no, no, no — ah! Ah, shit!
Deacon: Rippers? Boozer? Boozeman? Goddammit. Oh Goddammit Boozer — where are
        you —

[Deacon heads up the road.]

Deacon: I hear 'em —

[Nearby, two Ripper cultists are a knocked-down Boozer with a blowtorch.]

Ripper: These tats are dead symbols of a dead man. Dead symbols of the Lost.
Boozer: Get off me! You sonsofbitches!
Ripper: Biker man. You must be brought low, biker man. For you are Lost, and
        we are Found.

Ripper 2: Teach him the Path, brother, the Path.

[He burns Boozer's right arm repeatedly with the torch.]

Ripper: We will show you! Get low. Get low! Low!
Deacon: Rippers — sonofabitch — Hey! Over here! You sonsofbitches — Get off
        him! Ripper assholes! Come on!

[He guns the three Rippers down.]

Boozer: Those Goddamn sonsofbitches, I'm gonna kill them all. Every fucking
        one of 'em!

Deacon: Boozer. Boozer, come on —

[He sees how burned Boozer's forearm is.]

Deacon: Oh my god.
Boozer: Oh shit!
Deacon: Uh, let me help you up.
Boozer: No, I got this.
Deacon: No, no, no, you don't. C'mon. Get up.
Boozer: Fuckin' Rippers.
Deacon: We gotta go, pal.

Boozer: It was like they were waitin' for me or something. Fuck! I didn't see
        'em and then — then they were on me.

Deacon: Okay.
Boozer: My arm.
Deacon: Don't look at it.
Boozer: My Goddamn arm. No, I — God!
Deacon: I'm serious, don't look at it. Don't look at it. Get on the bike!
Boozer: Oh, shit! C'mon, go, go!

[They ride off just as a giant horde comes down the road.]

Boozer: Fuckin' Rippers!

006) DRIFTERS ON THE MOUNTAIN                                            [M006]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[The bikers ride back to their base at O'Leary Mountain's forest watchtower.]

Boozer: Shit. Thought we'd never make it.
Deacon: Hey, uh — Why don't you wait out here, let me make sure it's all clear.
Boozer: Screw that. There's a bunk callin' my name.

[Deek helps Boozer upstairs.]

Deacon: Alright, pretty much like we left it.
Boozer: What? Not like there's much to steal. Just gonna — reintroduce myself.

[He collapses on a bunk.]

Boozer: Oh thank God.
Deacon: I'm gonna go out, find some shit for your arm and get my bike. You
        gonna be okay?

Boozer: Yeah.
Deacon: Good.
Boozer: Yeah.

Deacon: I'll head over to that NERO checkpoint. They gotta have sterile
        bandages or painkillers.

Boozer: Oh, wait. Don't — don't leave my bike there.
Deacon: No. No, no, no, I'm gonna be, uh, going out on foot while it's still
        light out.

Boozer: Hey, I got some ammo if you need it. In the footlocker by the door.
Deacon: Thanks.
Boozer: And, hey. Don't take my shotgun.
Deacon: Uh, Boozer — Alright. Here you go.
Boozer: Thanks¹ brother. Just — feel kinda naked without it.

[Deacon walks downstairs.]

Boozer: Dammit — Boozer. Your arm's not gonna be fine. Sonofabitch. I gotta
        find something for his arm.

[Deacon exits the grounds through an automatic gate.]

Deacon: I'm not taking Boozer's bike — I gotta get to mine before it gets dark.

[Down the embankment, a shadowy figure runs off.]

Deacon: What the hell — Boozer — are you awake?
Boozer: Yeah Deek — what's up?
Deacon: I just saw someone sneakin' around the safe house —
Boozer: What the hell — what's he doin'?
Deacon: No idea. I'm gonna follow him — see if there's some more where he came
        from. Deacon out.

[Deacon stalks the man until he returns to his camp.]

Marauder: So what'd you find?
Marauder 2: It's just like I said — those Drifters we saw, ridin' on the same
            bike? They're holed up, just up the road.

Marauder: Yeah? No shit.
Marauder 2: Helluva set up¹ — some kinda lookout tower, got a fence and
            everything. Ours for the taking.

Marauder: Sounds pretty sweet — I say when it gets dark, we go in — kill the
          sonsofbitches and then make ourselves at home —

Marauder 2: Uh, you know they're gonna have guns —
Marauder: Looked like one of 'em was pretty gimped up — we can take 'em.
Deacon: Yeah? Fuck you guys.

[Deacon kills the entire six-man marauder camp.]

Deacon: That's the last of them — Musta followed us here — Sonsofbitches —
        Stay the hell off O'Leary Mountain. Boozer — I found their camp. Just
        a few Drifters looking to move in on our safe house.

Boozer: Like we were sayin' before — it's time to start thinkin' about headin'
        north —

Deacon: Let's get your arm fixed up — and then worry about hitting the road.
        I'm gonna be heading to my bike. Deacon out.

[Deek starts walking through the nighttime wilderness towards his camouflaged
 bike.]

Deacon: Ah, damn Freakers —

[If Deacon strays from the path too much:]

Deacon: Where the hell am I¹ — I gotta be getting close — Gotta get to my
        bike — getting closer —

[He runs through the stormy weather.]

Deacon: Oh, damn rain — If it's not the Freaks — it's the Goddamn rain — Why
        is it always raining —

[He nears the highway.]

Deacon: Gotta get close — come on¹ baby — where the fuck are you? This is it
        — this is where we left it —

[Nearby, he finds the branches he camouflaged his bike with strewn about.]

Deacon: My bike's gone. Fuck! Dammit, Copeland!

[He sees a forager nearby.]

Deacon: Hey, you're from Copeland's Camp! Where the hell is my bike!? Hey,
        stop! Wait! Goddamnit!

Survivor: I didn't take your bike, man — I swear —
Deacon: I'm not gonna kill ya — stop runnin' — Jesus Christ —
Survivor: You gotta ask Copeland — I don't know nothin' —
Deacon: Hey! I just want my bike —
Survivor: I didn't do nothin' —
Deacon: Oh, Goddamnit. Alright — now I'm gonna kill you —

[The survivor sprints like a marathon runner, never letting Deacon close.]

Deacon: Boozer, you there?
Boozer: Yeah Deek — you get your bike?
Deacon: Nope. Copeland's men got to it before I did — I'm heading to his camp —
        Deacon out.

[He chases the survivor all the way back to Copeland's town.]

Survivor: Open the gate — open up! It's me — Reynolds — open up —
Deacon: Open the gate.
Guard: St. John — is that you?
Deacon: Some sonofabitch stole my bike —
Guard: Don't know nothin' about that — you gotta go talk to Manny.
Deacon: Okay — yeah, that's where I'm headed —

[Deek walks over to Manny, the local bike mechanic.]

Deacon: Hey Manny.
Manny: Hey, I haven't seen you around lately. Or been too busy to notice. Nose
       down. Work hard, they feed you.

Deacon: Yeah, camper's life.
Manny: Yeah, camper's life. I read a book once — "Zen and the Art of Bike
       Repair" — you ever read it?

Deacon: Nah, I didn't have a lot of time for books back in the day.
Manny: Yeah, I ran a shop, in Farewell. Made all the grease monkeys read it.
       "Bein' a mechanic requires great peace a' mind," it said. Try workin'
       on an empty stomach. That'll focus your mind.

Deacon: Manny, I'm looking for a bike.
Manny: Oh yeah?

[Deacon walks over to a frame stripped of most its parts.]

Manny: Oh, whoa, whoa, whoa. You don't want that one.
Deacon: Why not?
Manny: Well, it just came off the truck. I mean, some dumb sonofabitch left it
       out in the shit, rusted up good. Been rode hard too, the fool that rode
       it didn't know shit 'bout bikes.

Deacon: Is that right?

Manny: Yeah, that's right. Shot to hell, this one. I mean, we just parted it
       out. It didn't even have a fuel pump, we coulda used that.

Deacon: Oh man, fuel pump. Like this one?
Manny: O-okay.
Deacon: Like this one, Manny?
Manny: Okay, okay. See now, when I said "fool," what I meant was — The fools
       that brought that bike in, see, they didn't tie that shit down properly
       — So they left it like, rattlin' around back there and —

Copeland: Deek? Let's talk.
Deacon: Looks like you had some trouble.
Copeland: Got hit hard last night — Rippers again. Twice now they've been up
          here. Some say looking for you and Boozer.

Deacon: Out in the shit, folks say a lot of things.
Copeland: Folks 'round here take care of their own — but go enough days without
          food — well, you see how it is.

Deacon: Lake not holding out?
Copeland: We get a fair amount of trout. Lake's fed by snowmelt. No one left
          to stock it with fish, gonna run out sooner or later.

Deacon: Like everything else.
Copeland: Used to go hunting out here with the old man. We'd build deer blinds
          out here, put down salt licks below us, pick 'em off clean. Some
          winters, had so much venison, we couldn't eat it all.

Deacon: I didn't think that was legal — deer baitin' — back in the day.
Copeland: My old man had only one law — the United States Constitution. If he
          could only see us now. America — Land of the Free!

Deacon: We are that.
Copeland: Saw Leon the other day.
Deacon: Yeah?
Copeland: He was bringing me something.
Deacon: Is that right?
Copeland: Folks here in a lotta pain, Deek.
Deacon: Oh, Leon. Tuck said that he took off. No one's seen him.
Copeland: Tell you what. You find his stash, you bring it to me. To me, Deek.
          You do that, well, we'll see what we can do for you.

Deacon: The bike. That your men stole. That you men parted out.
Copeland: Salvage, Deek. Salvage.
Deacon: Alright. I'll try to keep that in mind.
Copeland: By the way, nice hat.
Deacon: What?
Copeland: No, this one.

[He picks up Leon's hat — the bounty — from where it hangs on his belt.]

Deacon: Oh no, don't you ever touch me —
Copeland: Now, hold on. Leon wore a hat like this, didn't he?
Deacon: Oh Cope, I swear to God —
Copeland: Don't — You wanna do business in my camp? You start doing some runs
          for me.

Deacon: Cope — shit. Okay. I'm here anyway. Whaddya got?
Copeland: Now that's more like it. A group of Drifters has been harassing my
          supply runs. They've moved into the radio tower west of O'Leary
          Mountain. Isn't that your backyard?

Deacon: No, it's not. But I'll take care of 'em.
Copeland: I thought you might.

[Deacon returns to the mechanic shed near the entrance.]

Manny: Yo, Deek, Deek! Hold up. I just want to say how sorry I am. I — I didn't
       know, I swear!

Deacon: Do you have any idea how much time I put into that bike? It was a
        Drifter bike, Manny!

Manny: I know, I know. I'll make it up to you, I swear. I put together a new
       one.

Deacon: You call this piece of shit a bike?
Manny: I know, it's not — Look, I'll keep an eye out. For — for more parts.
       I'll hook you up. I swear.

Deacon: Okay, what about my custom gas tank, Manny — y'know, the one that I got
        from my dead wife? You gonna keep an eye out for that one too?

Manny: Jesus, Deek. I'm sorry.
Deacon: Just get the fuck outta my way.

[Deacon returns to the safehouse watchtower.]

[Boozer lays lifeless on his bed, slumped to one side.]

[Boozer suddenly bolts upright with his shotgun.]

Boozer: Shit, Deek.
Deacon: Holy —
Boozer: I coulda blown your Goddamn head off.

Boozer: No. Nope. I got this.
Deacon: C'mon, lemme see that arm —
Boozer: Look, I Got it.
Deacon: Alright! Fuck.
Boozer: Just — Deek? Thanks, brother. Look, I — I'll be better, okay? I'm gonna
        be fine.

          just took off — Manny said his bike's got a red tank on it and he

Deacon: Okay. If I go now, I might be able to catch up to him.

Copeland: I want him alive¹ Deek —

Deacon: Alive?

Copeland: Alive. You catch this man, then radio me. We'll fetch him and hang
          the bastard, right from that limb. It's time we start showin' these
          Drifter sonsofbitches that we have law and order in this camp. No
          offense meant to yourself.

Deacon: None taken. I'll find him. Hey Cope — this man I'm tracking down —
        who'd he kill?

Copeland: Why do you care? It's just another bounty job, isn't it?

Deacon: No look, I don't care, I just wanna know their names. Who, Cope?

Copeland: One of 'em was a man named Randall, been with the camp almost a year.
          I didn't know the other two. You want me to ask?

Deacon: No. I guess not.

Copeland: You find that sonofabitch, you radio me. Copeland out.

[Deacon looks at the biker's last known whereabouts: a pond near a blockade.]

Deacon: This is it — Okay, let's see — what's going on here. You're mine now.
        There he is —

[Deacon pursues the biker when he rides by and shoots at his enemy's ride.]

Moto Rider: Oh shit — the hell —
Deacon: Silver helmet. Red gas tank, that's him — So you thought you'd ride
        into Copeland's Camp — shoot the place up — that about right? Kill a 
        few folks, take some shit, and just ride out, like you were just —
        going shopping at the mall —

Moto Rider: Go to hell, Drifter — Copeland can suck on it — you hear me?

Moto Rider: Dammit. No — no, no, no, no! Not my bike — no, no!

[Deacon shoots his way through the bike until it flips and he captures Moto.]

Moto Rider: What — did you — do — you sonofa — bitch — hey — no — no — no, no,
            no, no — no —

Copeland: Yeah well, Copeland kinda frowns on that. Not a fan of it myself, if
          you wanna know the truth. Gives Drifters a bad name. And what if you
          had shot Manny, you know? Who'd fix my bike then? Stupid piece of
          shit.

Moto Rider: Screw you — you're one of Copeland's toadies — you little bitch —
            that's what you are — you little bitch!

Deacon: Cope, it's done. I got him. Write down these coordinates and send your
        men out here.

Copeland: Is he alive?

Deacon: Yeah, he's alive. But I won't promise ya how long he's gonna stay that
        way. Deacon out.

014) CLEAR OUT THOSE NESTS                                               [M014]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Shortly after finishing the railroad ambush camp, Boozer radios in.]

Boozer: Hey Deek, you there? I was thinkin' about heading down to that logging
        camp — clear out those nests. I've been seeing more Freaks up here.

Deacon: Boozer — no — no, you're gonna get yourself killed. Uh — you gotta
        wait 'til you're whole, brother. Uh — I'm over here anyway, so — I'll
        take care of the nests — okay?

Boozer: Yeah, okay. Thanks Deek.

Deacon: Nah, Deek — wait 'til tonight. Be fewer Freaks inside those nests —
        Or — take 'em out while it's still light out — there'll be more of 'em,
        but they won't be as strong —

Deacon: Okay, this is it — yeah, oh — this camp is gonna be crawlin'. Uh —
        yeah, nah — nah, ya gotta leave the bike out here, Deek or — it'll
        pull all of 'em down on ya. Okay — oh, there's gotta be a nest in this
        shack — Alright — fire in the hole — Come on boys and girls — let's do
        this — 

[He burns one out.]

Deacon: Okay — one nest done. How many more ya got? More in here? Yup — How'd
        ya like that? Huh? C'mon ya sonsofbitches — come on —

[He burns another and turns towards the large building nearby.]

Deacon: Oh — warehouse — yeah, it looks like the kinda place you wanna call
        home — yeah? Goddammit — what, did you all shit yourselves at once?
       Jesus Christ — Oh, Goddamn Freaks — what the hell are ya doin' in here,
       huh?

[He burns a third nest.]

Deacon: Getting kinda cold out here — thought I'd help ya out — This place is
        a deathtrap —

[He burns a fourth nest.]

Deacon: That'll warm you up — Okay — gotta be careful — gotta be careful —

[He burns a fifth.]

Deacon: Come on fellas —

[He burns the sixth.]

Deacon: Is that the last of 'em? Finally — Boozer — it's done. I cleared those
        nests. Should be less Freaks on the mountain from now on.

Boozer: Hey Deek — how'd it go? Were there — were there a lot of 'em?

Deacon: Yeah — but I wanted to clear 'em while it was still light out — you
        know how the sunlight bothers 'em —

Boozer: Yeah — that's — that's probably the — way to do it. Alright anyway,
        well — thanks for — thanks for doin' that — Deek.

Deacon: Get some shut-eye, Boozer. Deacon out.

015) PRICE ON OUR HEAD                                                   [M015]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

Deacon: Boozer, you there? I'm just callin' to check up on ya.
Boozer: Yeah Deek, I'm here.
Deacon: You hang in there¹ buddy. As soon as we get that arm patched up, we're
        ridin' north. Just like you said.

Boozer: I hope so. God, I miss the open road.
Deacon: You just work on gettin' better. I still got some work to do on the
        bike, and we gotta stock up on some gear. But once you're patched up?
        We're outta here. Deacon out.

[Deacon rides two kilometers to Salome's hot springs — Tucker's stronghold.
 If he does, he'll fight a few Rippers on the bridge leading in.]

Gate Guard: St. John! It's okay.
Deacon: Where's Tucker? Alkai?
Guard: Over at the dig site.
Deacon: Well, which one, Goddammit.¹
Guard: North one. Back there.
Deacon: Anyone touches this bike, or anything on it, I break your fingers.
Guard: Whatever¹ man. Jesus.

[Deacon strolls over to a dig site for irrigated crops.]

Alkai: I keep telling you, everywhere you look, it's all one giant lava field.
       Twenty-five feet solid rock. It'll take jackhammers to —

Tucker: I don't need a lecture, Goddammit. I get it.

Alkai: No you don't. But these people are hungry. Even if they had all their
       strength — it'll take 'em months to finish this job with picks and
       shovels.

Tucker: I don't give a shit! We're all hungry, Al, but this job's gotta get
        done whether it takes all Goddamn year. It's not like we got somewhere
        else to be, now do we?

Alkai: Wait. I'm not finished.

Tucker: Well make it quick, will ya¹ Al? I got things to do.

Alkai: Rippers. This morning. One of my men spotted a large group of them
       coming over the pass.

Tucker: And no one stopped them?

Alkai: How the fu— Tucker, you know we're already spread thin.

Tucker: Are — are they headed north? Al, are they headed towards us? Yes or no?

Alkai: I — I don't know. Maybe he knows.

Deacon: What the hell² are you up to now, huh? What's this about, huh?

Tucker: Dammit¹ Alkai, it's not his job to know. It's your Goddamn job to know.

Alkai: I can't be in two places at one time. You either want me here running
       your dig — Or you want me out there in the shit, chasing the Rippers.

Tucker: Go check the stores, see how much ammo we got left. I'll tell Wheeler
        to watch the dig.

Alkai: What're you lookin' at?

Deacon: Oh, I dunno, just waiting for you to smarten the fuck up.

Tucker: Don't.

[Alkai walks off.]

Tucker: Did you track down Leon?

[He hands Leon's bloody baseball cap to her.]

Tucker: Good thing someone around here knows how to make things happen. Ride
        with me.

[He rides shotgun in her golf cart as they patrol the encampment.]

Tucker: How long's it been since you found someone, brought 'em in?

Deacon: The kind of people left out in the shit, aren't the kind of people you
        want me bringing in.

Tucker: We lost two more to the fever.

Deacon: It's not my problem.

Tucker: You want our food? I'm making it your problem.

Deacon: I told you. We'll do runs for you, but we're not joining your Goddamned
        camp.

Tucker: Remind me again — my old woman's memory — why is that?

Deacon: Because it's a waste of time, Tuck.

Tucker: Well aren't you the optimist. Where's Boozer?

Deacon: He said he was gonna — head over to Copeland's Camp. See about —
        tradin' for some fish.

Tucker: You're not in bed with Cope now, are you? His camp near yours?

Deacon: It's not closer, or further. Look, I'm not Boozer's old lady. He goes
        where he wants.

[They drive past a large trash fire.]

Deacon: Jesus, you keep this shit burning all day and night?

Tucker: Got a lot of Freak corpses piling up out here, with men like you,
        doing your jobs. Damn right we keep it burning.

Deacon: Try using more gasoline. Burns faster. Less fumes.

Tucker: Like we got so much to spare? When it's all gone, what're you gonna put
        in that bike of yours? Spit 'n' sweat? Now what the hell is going on
        here?

Phillips: The count's off. Storage is missing food, and some ammo.

Tucker: Jesus. Who was on watch last night?

Phillips: Wheeler.

Tucker: Tonight, double the watch. This shit's starting to piss me off.

Phillips: You got it.

Deacon: Trouble in paradise?

Tucker: It's like I was sayin' — camp's like a prison. Buncha Goddamned lazy,
        liars, thieves, rapists, and murderers. You know why that is?

Deacon: No idea.

Tucker: 'Cause that's who we are. The Freakshow. Only folks survived were those
        mean enough, nasty enough, to out-freak the Freaks. The rest are here,
        hopin' I feed 'em, protect 'em, keep 'em nice and cozy an' warm so they
        can sit on their asses and watch the world end. You — get your ass back
        to work. Don't make me go get Cyrus. Lazy sonsofbitches — can screw
        around all they like on their time. Daytime, is my time. Runnin' this
        camp's no different than runnin' a prison.

Deacon: I can't remember what you said — you were — you were what, a warden or
        somethin'?

Tucker: Nothing so high and mighty. I was matron of the women's ward. You look
        like the sort who mighta spend some time in the pen — back in the day.
        You ever do time?

Deacon: I had my share of trouble, but never landed in K-state.

Tucker: I got a job for you. Larsen was on a run yesterday — passed through
        Marion Forks¹ said he saw someone. Young woman, looked like, but he
        only caught a glance. He stopped to look around, but he never found
        her.

Deacon: Is he sure?

Tucker: Larsen's been doin' this long as you. He knows a person from a Freak.
        But you got a knack for this. You head over and find her before the
        Freaks do.

Deacon: I'll see what I can do. But, look — Tuck, I want the rest of my
        credits — for Leon.

Tucker: You bring me warm bodies, I'll give you all the credits you can spend.
        I gotta go find Wheeler. Someone's lookin' at a night in the shack.

[Deacon walks over to Alkai's merchant stall.]

Deacon: Alkai.
Alkai: What do you want, Drifter?
Deacon: What's your problem? Hm?

Alkai: One of my men escaped a Ripper camp, over by Iron Butte. Got tortured,
       like they always do. But this time they kept asking him if he knew
       about two bikers, two men — Asking if he'd ever seen of 'em and heard

Deacon: Lotta bikes around here. What's it — what's it got to do with me?

Alkai: The Ripper called 'em "Mongrels". How many Drifters still flying colors
       around here, as if that shit matters.¹ You ask me? You got a price on
       your head. How's it feel to be on the other side?

Deacon: Al, why don't you just show me what you got because I don't have time
        for your bullshit.

Alkai: Whatever you say, Deek.

[Back at his bike, he stares at the drug-filled cooler.]

Deacon: Now I just gotta figure out who I'm gonna give this to.

[If Deek chooses to give Leon's stash to Tucker:]

Deacon: We can't head north until I get better gear. Tucker it is. Hey Tuck.
Tucker: You got my drugs, from Leon?

Deacon: Yeah. Yeah, Cope wanted me to sell to him, but uh, I know who my
        friends are.

Tucker: You got that right. Go see Alkai. I heard Larsen brought in a stash of
        shotguns and rifles. Maybe he's got something you can use.

[If Deacon doesn't pick Tucker:]

Deacon: We can't head north until we get this bike fixed up. Copeland it is.

017) WHAT DID YOU DO?                                                    [M017]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

Boozer: Deek, you there?

Sarah: Hey. Hey, are you okay? C'mon¹ we gotta find your parents, okay?

Scared Man: You did it. You did it.

Deacon: Give me the gun! Oh, God.

018) SEARCHING FOR SOMETHING                                             [M018]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After reminiscing at the gravesite, a heli flies overhead and disappears.]

[As Deek heads for Marion Forks, he listens to another truther broadcast.]

          thinking about where it all began. The roots go deep, back to the
          big dub-ya dub-ya two. 1947, the Feds passed — what they call it?

Boozer: You went up there again, didn't you — after I told you not to.

Deacon: Look — would you just leave it, alright? I'm just out hunting Freaks
        — Boozer, you got that? Bounties — that is the only reason I go up
        there.

[Deacon continues pursuing the helicopter. Mutated wolves appear nearby.]

Deacon: Shit — runners — dammit.

[He shoots the wolves and continues until the heli hovers over a crossroads.]

Deacon: Whoa, whoa, whoa — hold on, hold on — they're slowing down — looks like
        they're stopping —

[When he approaches, they open fire, causing him to crash.]

Deacon: Motherfucker —
Boozer: Deek? Deek, what's going on?
Deacon: Sonofabitch —
Boozer: What happened? You okay?

Deacon: No no no I'm fine — I'm fine, I think they were just uh — warning
        shots — I mean, if they were trying to hit me, I would be dead —

Boozer: Deek — Remember me telling you about that death wish of yours?
Deacon: Yeah, yeah, yeah. I got this. Deacon out.

[From a hilltop, Deacon spies on the copter crew. They have a semi-sedate Newt
 with a device around its neck, like what animal control personnel would use
 to corral large pests.]

Cpl. Franklin: Tranq isn't working.

Lt. Booth: Oh, it's working, or this little shit would've torn your head off
           by now.

Cpl. Franklin: C'mon Doc, hurry it up!
Lt. Booth: Sonofabitch, calm the hell down.
Cpl. Franklin: Incoming!
Lt. Booth: Gimme a minute!

[He executes the wrangled Newt as a large horde starts to swarm.]

Lt. Booth: What are you doing?
Cpl. Franklin: Pack it up, we're out! Shit, let's go — go! Hell.
Lt. Booth: Abort mission — abort!
Cpl. Franklin: Go, go, go! Shit! Goddammit, let's go!
Lt. Booth: Load up! Load up! Go!

Deacon: Oh Jesus — is that a Horde?

[The horde follows the heli into the distance. A green light flickers nearby.]

Deacon: Hello — what did you assholes leave behind? Yeah, okay — it's a radio
        alright.

[As he goes to pick it up, a Newt pushes him down and snatches it.]

Deacon: Hey — Goddammit! Get back here with that! You little shit — that's
        mine!

[He guns it down.]

Deacon: Oh finally — Jesus Christ, those shits can run fast.
Boozer: So, what the hell are they doin'?

Deacon: It looks like they were out here — shit, wrangling Freaks — I don't
        know. They had a Newt in some kinda noose, like they were putting a
        tracking device on it or somethin'.

Boozer: What? Wrangling? Whaddya mean?

Deacon: You know, like tying it up, taking samples from it or something — like
        those guys used to do on that wildlife show. Pretty fucked up. They got
        chased off by Swarmers. Bugged the hell out. And they left some gear
        behind. A radio.

Boozer: Wait — you don't — you don't think that — Sarah —

Deacon: No — no — not — I — I — I — I don't know. I'm just — and he's alive,
        Boozer, he's alive. O'Brian — one of them, NERO — I'm gonna track him
        down, if I can. I — I'm gonna — I'm gonna get some answers.

Boozer: Dammit — okay. Look, I'll be able to ride soon — I'll help you, Deek.
        If he's alive, we'll find the bastard.

Deacon: You're Goddamn right. I'm gonna check in later. Deacon out. Okay,
        O'Brian — where the hell are you?

019) WHAT'S A NICE GIRL                                                  [M019]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Back at his bike, Deacon's mind drifts back to the first time he met Sarah,
 on a country road with her car broken down. He pulls up as she works under
 the hood.]

Sarah: Oh, God.
Deacon: Hey.
Sarah: Hey.
Deacon: So, I'm sorta lost. I was hopin' you could help me out?
Sarah: I'm sorry, you're lost?

        lotta signs around here.

Sarah: Oh, c'mon, you gotta be kidding me.
Deacon: Nope.
Sarah: What? What is it? What —

[He turns his mirror to show she has an oil smudge on her face.]

Sarah: Oh, that's great.

[The car makes a deflated wheezing noise.]

Sarah: Oh, that's just perfect. That — that is great. That is great.

       Belknee, Bell —

       help you. I'm sorry.

Deacon: So, no, then?
Sarah: Nope.
Deacon: Okay. Well — thanks anyway.
Sarah: Hey!

[He rides off a little, but then stops, pretending to ignore her plight.]

Sarah: Alright.
Deacon: Could you use a ride?
Sarah: Yes I could, thank you for finally offering. I'm Sarah.
Deacon: I'm Deacon.

[They shake hands; she gets oil on his.]

Sarah: Oh, well, sorry about the mess. Uh, um — I don't know — how do I, uh
       — this contraption —

Deacon: Pretty much what you think, just throw you — leg over, yeah.
Sarah: I just — Okay. Ummm, just — on there — whoa — okay. Ready. Hey — hey!
Deacon: Hold on tight.
Sarah: Thank you so much.
Deacon: No problem.
Sarah: It's just — there are no bars out here, so —

Deacon: Well sure there is — there's — place called Crazy Willie's up the road
        — there's, uh —

Sarah: No, I meant cell phone reception —
Deacon: I knew what you meant —
Sarah: Right¹ of course — anyway —
Deacon: So what's a nice girl like you doing in a place like this?

Sarah: You know, I ask myself that all the time. I do research, um, you know,
       I study things.

Deacon: Thanks, I had no idea what research was —

Sarah: Sorry, um — I do plants.
Deacon: You study plants!
Sarah: Yeah —

[Ahead, some hicks' wildly driving truck nearly knocks 'em off the road.]

Sarah: Hey! Hey, look out! Oh my God.
Deacon: Shit! Hold on!
Redneck: Woo hoo!
Deacon: Assholes!
Sarah: Oh my God!
Deacon: Are you okay?
Sarah: Yeah, I'm just — Oh lordy that was close.
Deacon: Hey, you sure you're okay?
Sarah: Yeah I'm fine. I just — Oh my God.

[Her phone rings.]

Sarah: Hey. Hey. I've got cellphone reception. Hey. Yeah, I'm fine, I just —
       The car you gave me? It's a real piece of shit. I need a tow. I'm on,
       uh, um, some — I dunno where I am —

Deacon: Road 42.

Sarah: Road 42. Yeah, I'm — I'm about a mile up. Okay, I'll see you when you
       get here.

Deacon: C'mon, I'll take you back to your car. We can wait for the tow truck.
Sarah: I don't know.

Deacon: Well alright. I'm sure when those boys come back, they'd be happy to
        give you a ride, so —

Sarah: Okay, alright. Alright! I just — Just give me a second.
Deacon: They'll be any minute now, so —

Sarah: Alright, alright, alright! Screw it, let's go. Just drive a little
       careful this time, okay?

[They start driving back to her car.]

Sarah: You weren't really lost, were you?

Deacon: Well that all depends on who you ask. My ex would say I've been lost
        for years.

Sarah: Well you certainly know your way around here.
Deacon: So you're not from around here.

Sarah: No, I'm from Seattle. The company that I work for, they just — they
       opened this lab here. So, here I came, to the middle of nowhere.

Deacon: To research plants.

Sarah: That's right. I already told you, I forgot. Um, yeah so — the company
       that I work for, they — they do work for this bioengineering firm, and
       um, some of the plants that I — I look at are pretty rare — and they
       just happen to grow here.

Deacon: That — has gotta be the best thing I've ever heard.

[As they approach her car, they can see the hicks from before standing near.]

Deacon: Oh — what the hell —
Redneck: Clete! We got company.
Sarah: Oh shit.
Deacon: Alright, gentlemen.

[Deacon quickly loses the fistfight and they start wailing on him.]

Redneck: Who's smart now, huh? That's what I thought.
Redneck 2: So what do we have here? Big bad biker, huh?
Redneck: Yeah! Yes, hit him again!
Redneck 2: How do you like that, biker boy? Not so tough now, are you?
Redneck: Work of art, it's lovely, do it, come on, hit him! Hit him!
Redneck 2: You don't learn, do you, biker boy?
Redneck: I could watch this all day. Oh yes. Yes!
Redneck 2: I'll teach him. I'll teach him good,¹ yeah you like that? How 'bout
           that —
Redneck: C'mon —

[Sarah, who was digging in Deacon's bag, fires his pistol.]

Redneck: Shit! The hell?
Redneck 2: Oh screw this¹ man, I'm out!
Redneck 3: Hold on, hold on, wait, wait, hold up, hold up!
Redneck: Roll¹ Goddammit! Roll!

[They scramble to their truck and flee.]

Sarah: Oh Jesus. Oh my God. Oh no, no. Oh, oh my God.
Deacon: Uh. Hey.

Sarah: I'm so sorry, I — I don't even know. I was just looking in your bag and
       I — I saw that and I —

Deacon: No, no, no. No, it's alright. Oh —
Sarah: Oh my God, I could have killed somebody. Oh shit —
Deacon: Well, yeah, but you gotta kinda aim it at them first.
Sarah: I've never done anything like that before. I saw —
Deacon: Hey, hey, hey, it's okay, it's okay. They're gone. They're gone.

Sarah: I saw it in your bag and I just — I tried to call the police but there
       were —

Deacon: You did good. You know what we're gonna do — what we're gonna do?
Sarah: There were no bars. There was no reception.
Deacon: I'm gonna wait right here until your guy comes.
Sarah: Okay.
Deacon: Thank you.
Sarah: I've never done anything like that.
Deacon: Huh. Coulda fooled me.
Sarah: Yeah?

[The flashback ends and Deacon snaps back to reality.]

Deacon: House is sealed up — how's she get in and out? Ladder — this is it.
        Come on — Just gotta — set it — here. Alright¹ kid — where ya hiding?

[He finds a silent girl in a bedroom, cradling a stuffed animal.]

021) LOTS OF SICK PEOPLE                                                 [M021]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

Deacon: Don't be afraid, uh, I'm not gonna hurt you. Are you alone? Is there,
        uh, anyone else with you? Oh, man. Okay, uh — Is — is this your room?
        These are really great. Uh, are — are these yours? Uh — Lisa —

[Deacon goes to touch her trophy.]

Lisa: No!
Deacon: Alright, hold — hold —

Lisa: That's mine! This one's for gymnastics — I should have won first place
      but Missy King, she cheated —

Deacon: Lisa! Lisa, you hear gunshots outside? It's not safe here. Now if we —

Lisa: I was at school. And my mom called me and told me to come home right
      away and not stop and — They would be here waiting for me and we would
      leave together and — I got here and there was — a note that said they
      left with some men and — I didn't know what to do. So — so I hid and —
      I — I didn't know what to do —

Deacon: Uh — It's alright, it's okay, it's okay. Uh — Lisa, not far from here
        there's a camp — And you really oughta let me take you there —

Lisa: No —

Deacon: Uh, there are people there — there are people there, I know them —
        it's — I'm not gonna lie to you, it's a work camp and to eat, you have
        to work. Life is gonna be hard, but at least you ain't gonna starve,
        uh —

Lisa: What? No! No, my mom's coming here for me!

Deacon: Uh, okay — is this your mommy? Well, you said she didn't come home,
        right? So, maybe she's at the camp.

Lisa: Mom is at the camp? She is. I know she is.
Deacon: Okay. Stay close.

[They prepare to leave together. Freakers screech in the yard below.]

Lisa: The men with the guns — are they still out there?
Deacon: No. We don't gotta worry about them.
Lisa: No, no — lots of Sick People —
Deacon: Lisa, stay behind me.
Lisa: We shouldn't be out here — We — we should go —
Deacon: Come on — Lisa, stay behind me —

[He kills a large bear feeding near his bike.]

Deacon: C'mon, get on. We have to move.
Lisa: I don't know about this —
Deacon: C'mon, kid — we gotta go.
Lisa: Okay — Hey — what's your name?

Deacon: Uh, Deacon. My name's — Deacon. Uh, Lisa — Lisa, how did you live out
        here — alone — for all this time? You don't talk much, do you?

Lisa: My dad's a rock hound. He used to take me out here looking for thunder
      eggs.

Deacon: Thunder eggs? Uh — what is —
Lisa: They're rocks, but — when you cut them open they're really pretty inside.
Deacon: Okay — that sounds great —

Lisa: We used to go all over — Belknap Crater, the Lava Flow, and Black Crater
      — everywhere. Do you think he's at the camp too?

Deacon: Uh — I dunno, kid.

[As they ride back toward Salome, the tunnel they're in has flashlights ahead.]

Deacon: Shit, someone's in the tunnel —
Lisa: What?
Deacon: Here — hop off.
Lisa: What are we doing?

Deacon: Listen to me — the gunshots that you heard? Those were — really bad
        men. Do you understand?

Lisa: Yes.
Deacon: Stay here, find someplace to hide. Don't come out until I say so. Okay?
Lisa: Yeah, okay.
Deacon: Alright¹ you sonsofbitches, let's get this started.

[He slays the would-be ambushers.]

Deacon: Lisa? Kid? Come on out, it's safe — You okay?
Lisa: Yeah, yeah. I — I think I want to go home.

Lisa: No. Men came and took everything.

Deacon: Did they have anyone with them? Women? Children?
Lisa: I don't remember —
Deacon: Okay —
Lisa: Tommy would remember.
Deacon: Tommy?

Deacon: Hide? I don't —

Deacon: Okay — okay, do you know where that is?

Lisa: No. They wanted me to come with them, but I knew my mom and dad would

Deacon: Alright — this it is, we're here. So just — stay with me.
Lisa: Okay.
Tucker: Well, who do we have here?
Lisa: Mrs. Tucker!
Tucker: Oh my God. Lisa, honey. It's okay. You're safe now.

Lisa: Mom and dad and everyone got sick, and I didn't know what to do and —

Tucker: Shh, shh, shh. It's okay. You're safe now. It's a miracle. It's a

        down the block. I knew her parents.

Lisa: Are they here, Mrs. Tucker?

Tucker: Honey, you know the answer to that.

Lisa: No, they're not here.

Tucker: Let's go in. Get you cleaned up. Something to eat. And then I'll find

Deacon: Hey, hey, listen, listen, she's — she's been through a lot, can we

022) IT'S A RIFLE, NOT A GUN                                             [M022]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[One sunny day, Deacon meets up with Copeland in the wilderness.]

Copeland: So, you wanna learn how to hunt, that what I'm hearin'?
Deacon: I know how to shoot a gun.
Copeland: It' s a rifle, not a gun.

Deacon: I was in the 10th Mountain, Cope. Don't give me any of your Marine
        Corp bullshit.

Copeland: Killin' a buck's a little different than killin' a man, or a Freak.
          Best way to hunt an animal is to track it. You gotta focus, and see
          what nature's tryin' to tell ya. If you look hard enough, you'll see
          the signs.

[Deacon starts following the buck's trail.]

Copeland: Well, okay then. Look hard. See this pile of deer scat? It's fresh.
Deacon: Yeah, I see it.
Copeland: They lead this way.
Deacon: Yeah, I can see that.
Copeland: Well, come on then. Quick — there's your buck.
Deacon: I see him.

Copeland: Now here, use my rifle. If you were in the 10th Mountain, you know
          how to use a scope.

Deacon: Yeah, Cope. I know how to use a scope.
Copeland: Easy — easy —
Deacon: I got this —

[Deacon fires. If he misses:]

Copeland: Thought you knew how to shoot a gun.
Deacon: I'm — outta practice.
Copeland: Hurry, try again.
Deacon: Well maybe if someone would shut the hell up.

[Either way, Deacon has to hit it to continue the mission.]

Copeland: You got him — nice shot —
Deacon: Oh, Goddammit — it wasn't a kill shot — he got away —

Copeland: No, no — that's okay. You wounded him. He'll bleed out soon enough.
          We just gotta track him.

Deacon: Okay —
Copeland: See the blood spots? Look close —
Deacon: Yeah, I see 'em —
Copeland: Then follow 'em —
Deacon: On it —

Copeland: He'll be slowin' down about now. Losin' too much blood. We should
          be coming across his carcass anytime now. Okay, you know how to gut
          an animal?

Deacon: Yeah, look — Cope, Boozer and I have been hunting before. He used to —
        go elk hunting — with his old man and, yeah — he, uh — showed me how
        to gut a deer.

Copeland: Well, let's just say, no disrespect to Boozer, but — you got a lot
          to learn. You're wasting a lot of meat there. Overall, not bad — for
          a beginner.

Deacon: Yeah, thanks.
Copeland: Now, I'll take back that rifle.
Deacon: Here, thanks.

Copeland: Like I said, Deek. We can always use more venison at the camp. Still
          got some folks tryin' to heal up from that Ripper attack.

Deacon: Okay, Cope. Yeah, I'll see if I can — remember that.

[A new broadcast plays later.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. I grew up
          in these here woods. My grandfather taught me all about huntin'.
          Funny how it still works in a world he never would've dreamed of. I
          built my first tree house to work as a deer blind. Gettin' height on
          your target helps your aim and keeps you safe. Back then, I took out
          my first doe from up top. Today, my camp's up in the trees. You wanna
          survive and can contribute, you come to me, we got you covered.
          Grandfather also taught me, to catch a doe, sometimes you gotta lay
          an ambush. Hide where they need to go — like a watering hole. Today,
          you're as likely to be prey as hunter, so you gotta keep your eyes
          peeled when you're hittin' up places we all need to go. But
          Grandfather always said the easiest way to a good meal was to lay a
          trap. Put a snare by a tree, and you could have dinner next time you
          come round. But careful. A headless snake can still bite, 'specially
          when it ain't really dead — my grandfather would've outlived us all,
          let me tell you. This is Mark Copeland for Radio Free Oregon. Don't
          believe the lies.

Deacon: Oh that's great, Cope. So you and your grandaddy set traps for 'em,
        and you and your old man used to lay down salt licks — yeah¹ that's
        really sporting. I guess none of that shit matters now.

023) MAKING CONTACT                                                      [M023]

Cpl. Franklin: Yeah, it's clear.

[Deacon infiltrates the LZ and shadows O'Brian and his NERO escort.]

O'Brian: Lieutenant O'Brian, Field Note Two Zero Zero Six. On approach to the
         landing site, I observed a large swarm of insects, probably Tabanus
         atratus, or Diptera, in a clearing well away from our designated
         target. From that distance, I could not discern what was attracting
         the insects, but from the size of the swarm, recent carrion is
         indicated. Should be just over here — Dammit, where is it — Ah, here
         it is. Speculation to Tabanus atratus is confirmed. Lots of horse
         flies here, glad to have the suit on, let me tell you. Carrion is
         still mostly intact and appears to be Odocoileus hermionus, or mule
         deer — as if anybody could check that. Striation of the large muscle
         masses indicate infection of Hooligan strain Hb, will take sample to
         confirm. Well, look at it this way, you poor sonofabitch, at least
         you weren't torn apart by Freaks. If you lived a few more weeks, you
         would've become one yourself. Now wouldn't that've been something.

[Deacon reaches over and unplugs O'Brian's comm unit. He contemplates fleeing,
 but Deek has him at gunpoint.]

Deacon: Uh-huh.
O'Brian: What do you want? Stay back.
Deacon: I just want to talk.

O'Brian: Uh — NERO protocol Two Dash Seven states clearly — That if —
         conducting operations in quarantine zones — That if I encounter any
         civilians, er — subj — Drift — civilians! — That I am forbidden from
         making contact —

[He taps the gun against the man's hazmat suit visor.]

Deacon: Really? See that sounded to me like — making contact.
O'Brian: Yes, yes it did.
Deacon: You're alive.
O'Brian: Yes — I am.
Deacon: How? How are you alive, O'Brian?
O'Brian? What? I — I — I don't understand —

Deacon: Okay, you were there, that night, Farewell — The next night, the
        refugee camp — The choppers were burning, everyone was dead.

O'Brian: NERO Protocol Two Dash Seven — states that I — Two Dash Seven —
Deacon: They were slaughtered — torn limb from Goddamned limb —
O'Brian: NERO — Protocol Two Dash —

Deacon: Alright, listen up. We're gonna do this the easy way or the hard way.
        The easy way, we have a little chat, you give me the information that
        I need — And you go back to digging your way through Freaker shit —
        Or whatever the hell else you're doin' out here. The hard way — I
        crack open that little space suit — And then we see what your friends
        out there have to say — About you breathing in all this "contaminated"

O'Brian: Yes. Okay — okay.

Deacon: You remember the rooftop of the old brewery. I put a woman on your

O'Brian: Yes — I remember, uh — a — a knife wound, she was — she was cut pretty

O'Brian: Oh — wait, wait, wait — I, I, I — I can find out. I, I can check — I

[He wraps an arm around O'Brian and prepares to use him as a hostage.]

O'Brian: Okay look, if you're going to fucking kill me, do it! Okay? I did my

Sarah: Yep. And bring me three plants — and don't crush them.

Sarah: Come on —
Deacon: Uh — got one —
Sarah: Good for you!
Deacon: This one?
Sarah: Yep. Keep going.
Deacon: Last one —

Sarah: Oh!
Deacon: For you.

Deacon: I'll bet.

Deacon: Alright, great.

Deacon: Hey¹ Boozer, uh —

Deacon: Uh, it's a funny thing, I — I was remembering how — Uh, a few summers
        back Sarah took me out to Bear Creek. We were picking lavender, and uh
        — she taught — 

Boozer: Pussy.
Deacon: She taught me how to make this salve for burns and um —

Boozer: Look, I got out today. Okay? I actually had a look around the mountain,
        I cleared some traps. Look, arm's almost as good as new.

Deacon: Alright. Okay. I'm just gonna leave it right here.

Boozer: Hey, just gimme a couple days. Okay? Just — We'll ride up north, like
        you said, and get out of this shithole.

Deacon: Sure. Yeah.
Boozer: What? You —
Deacon: Nothin'.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
031) WHAT HAVE THEY DONE                                                 [M031]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After handing over the salve, Deacon rides out from O'Leary Mountain.]

Tucker: Deek — you there?
Deacon: Yeah, I'm here. What's up?
Tucker: We got hit — and hard. Rippers, a coupla dozen, maybe more.
Deacon: Goddamn Rippers.
Tucker: That little gal you were so worried about?
Deacon: Yeah, Lisa? Wait, hold on — what happened — where's Lisa?

Tucker: Gone. They took her and three others. Alkai followed 'em as far as he
        could, but they're holed up at Belknap Crater. He came back to round
        up more men, but —

Deacon: Goddammit. Okay, look — I've seen what those sonsofbitches do to
        hostages. I'm not waiting.

[He makes for Belknap Crater in the next-door region.]

Deacon: Goddamn Rippers, where the hell is the girl? If you've hurt her, I
        swear to God — Who am I kidding, I'm gonna fuckin' kill you all whether
        you hurt her or not. Hang on¹ Lisa. I'm comin'. What's this — Lisa's?
        Sure as hell don't belong to a Goddamn Ripper.

[He examines the backpack.]

Deacon: Small foot prints — girl's size it's — gotta be Lisa — she was dragged
        through here — If you've hurt her — you sonsofbitches — I'm gonna kill
        every last one of you —

[He kills a Ripper using a dead body for boxing practice.]

Deacon: Yeah — why don't you find the Path? They're dead, asshole — they won't
        be joining your Goddamn cult.

[Deek follows the trail to some scenic caves. Another dead captive's nearby.]

Deacon: In here — they dragged her in here? Jesus — what the hell is wrong
        with you freaks? The Free — rule the world, huh? Not if they're all
        dead — No, she's not in here — where are you, Lisa? She's gotta be
        out here somewhere —

[Outside, more Rippers soon meet their end.]

Deacon: No one — is joining you — Hey look — now you're "found" — yeah? Hang
        on¹ Lisa — no matter what they do to you, just — just hang on — Lisa —
        I'm comin' for ya —

[He continues on Lisa's trail.]

Deacon: Place is a Goddamn maze — Up here — they dragged her up here — Lisa's
        gotta be up there —

[The Rippers start attacking as he approaches the fortified end of the place.]

Deacon: There she is — Lisa? Alright, Lisa. Oh Jesus, what have they done to
        you? Lisa? Lisa? Hey. Sweetheart —

Lisa: No! No!

Deacon: Hey, sweetheart — hey, hey, hey! Shut up, shut up, shut up! Lisa, it's
        me, it's Deacon. Remember? Deacon?

Lisa: Deacon?

Deacon: Okay. Alright. That's alright, it's alright. C'mon. You okay? Goddammit
        — can you run? Do you know where the visitor's center is? Alright,
        that's where my bike is — I need you to run there as fast as you can —
        don't stop.

Lisa: Don't stop.

Deacon: Right, don't stop, no matter what. You ready? Huh? Go!

[They prepare to leave, but more Rippers start showing up.]

Lisa: No — no — Rippers —
Deacon: Lisa, get down — hide!

[They kill the first wave.]

Deacon: Lisa — run!
Lisa: Rippers —
Deacon: Get down, get down!

[They kill a second wave.]

Deacon: Go, go!
Lisa: Oh, no — Rippers —
Deacon: Get to the Visitor's Center now — go!

[They finally make it through the last wave.]

Deacon: Get to my bike! Run! We're safe now. Are you okay?
Lisa: No.

Deacon: Listen to me, to the south of here there's a camp at Lost Lake, it's
        nothing like the Hot Springs. Iron Mike, he's not like Mrs. Tucker.

Lisa: I hated Mrs. Tucker.

Deacon: Well, you wouldn't be alone there. This is a nice camp, and it's a
        safe place.

Lisa: Okay. Hold on.

[Deacon tries haling his contact at Lost Lake, Rikki.]

Deacon: Rikki — Rikki, come back. Rikki, you still on this channel? Lost Lake
        Camp, come in.

Rikki: Deacon? Long time no hear. What do you want?

Deacon: Just — oh dammit — meet me, okay? On the Cascade Highway, where it
        intersects with the Old Belknap Road. I'm heading there now.

Rikki: You know what Iron Mike said — the night you and Boozer rode out of
       here?

Deacon: Oh yeah — that. Listen, that's why I radioed you and not Skizzo — Iron
        Mike doesn't even have to know about this — I've got a kid here.

Rikki: What?
Deacon: I mean, not a kid — a survivor — she's been out here a long time —
Rikki: You've got a survivor — and you're bringing her to Lost Lake —

Deacon: No, you're bringing her to Lost Lake. I'm bringing her to you. Rikki?
        You there?

Rikki: Yeah — yeah. Okay. I'm on my way. Lost Lake out.

Deacon: Rikki? Yeah, okay — you're welcome. Uh — you're — you're gonna like it
        there¹ kid. It's like I said, Iron Mike, he's, um — Uh, he likes to
        yell a lot — look, don't let him bother you — you got that? Uh, anyway
        — there's this guy named Skizzo — if he bothers you, at all — well,
        just tell Rikki. Or, uh, tell Addy — she's the camp's doctor, you tell
        her. And — Addy's — she's good, she's got medicine — if, you know, to
        clean up those, uh — to clean up those cuts — I mean, you don't want
        to get infected. They're gonna help you out, kid, you can count on 'em
        — even if you, uh — you know, even if you — screw up. Alright.

[The old pals rendezvous at the given place. Note: this part may not have any
 subtitles, even though older versions of the game do. Not sure why this is.]

Deacon: Hey¹ Rikki.
Rikki: Hey, Deek. I'm surprised. What, did Tucker give up the slave trade?

Deacon: Uh — Lisa, this is, uh, Rikki. She's gonna, uh, take you to a safe
        place.

Rikki: Nothing has changed, Deek. Iron Mike is not gonna pay you for this.

Deacon: Pay me for — oh, c'mon, that's not — excuse me — that's not what this
        is about. It's not about collecting a bounty or anything. Can you just
        please take her? Huh?

Rikki: Mm-hmm. What's wrong with her, Deek?

Deacon: What's wrong with her? She was — had a run-in with some Rippers, I had
        to —

Rikki: Oh my God. Hey, Lisa. Hi. I'm Rikki. Listen, do you like to go fishing?
       I love fishing, it's — it's my favorite thing in the whole wide world.
       Would you wanna go fishing with me? Yeah? C'mon, I'm gonna tell you
       about Lost Lake. It has the clearest water you have ever seen. And the
       fish — oh my God — the fish in the morning? They jump this high. I'll
       show you. When we go, we're gona have such a good time. Make sure you
       hold on tight, 'kay? Ready?

Deacon: I really appreciate —

[They speed off, leaving Deacon without a second thought.]

Tucker: Deek. You there? Hot Springs to Deacon St. John.
Deacon: Tucker — I'm here.
Tucker: I expected you back by now. Did you find the girl, Lisa?

Deacon: No, Tuck, no — the — the uh — Rippers cut her up pretty bad. And she
        — uh — She didn't make it.

Tucker: Goddammit. We needed her — now the digging's going to get even further
        behind.

Deacon: Well, look on the bright side, Tuck — one less mouth to feed, yeah?

Tucker: You get out there and find me some warm bodies or there won't be any
        mouths left to feed. Tucker out.

Deacon: Yeah, okay, I'm gonna get right on that.

032) NO ONE SAW IT COMING                                                [M032]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon returns to the safehouse for some sleep. He awakens to Boozer standing
 with his shotgun pointed at the doorway, clearly in a hallucinating state.]

Boozer: Oh they're comin', they're comin¹, oh they're gonna — They wanna, no
        — I mean they're on me, they're gonna —

[He puts Deacon in his crosshairs.]

Deacon: Oh shit, Boozer, what's going on?
Boozer: No! How'd you get in here?
Deacon: Whoa, whoa, whoa, whoa —
Boozer: You stay right there! You stay there.
Deacon: Boozer, it's me. It's Deek. Let's just calm down.
Boozer: Don't you come any closer. I will kill you.
Deacon: Let's just talk. It's alright.
Deacon: C'mon, give me the gun! Give me the gun, buddy! C'mon. C'mon!
Boozer: No! No — No, I will not —

[The gun discharges upwards and Boozer falls down, seemingly sobered.]

Deacon: Oh shit. Oh Jesus Christ. Boozer, what the fuck —
Boozer: I, heard — I heard 'em. I heard voices —
Deacon: Oh shit. Oh shit. Oh shit. Shit.
Boozer: I mean, Deek, you — you heard 'em, right?
Deacon: No, I didn't hear shit! Boozer, you've got blood poisoning.
Boozer: No, I — I do not.
Deacon: Yes you do, Boozer. Just take a look.
Boozer: I don't need to take a look, I'm —
Deacon: C'mon, we gotta get you some help.
Boozer: Look, I don't need some —
Deacon: C'mon.

Boozer: Dammit, I don't need help.

[They start walking to Deacon's bike.]

Boozer: Sorry 'bout that — 'bout tryin' to blow your head off — I mean — I
        thought I saw somethin' — ya know?

Deacon: Easy. Hey, watch the steps.
Boozer: I got this. But it — it was — it was in my head — ya know?
Deacon: Yeah, yeah. I know. I know.

Boozer: I could hear 'em, Deek. I — I could hear 'em — Deek. Footsteps — just
        — poundin' in my head — boots —

Deacon: Just a few more steps.
Boozer: I don't need any help. I can Goddamn walk. I can — walk.
Deacon: Okay. Okay.

Boozer: I — I just — I don't — I don't know — what happened — I — I saw 'em —
        so many of 'em, just — all comin', ya know?

Deacon: Yeah. Now, c'mon, c'mon. Get on. We gotta go.
Boozer: Wait — wait, wait — what? Where're we goin'? I — I don't —
Deacon: It's just a short ride. Boozer, it'll help clear your head.
Boozer: Ride? Uh, yeah, yeah. Okay — that'd be — good. Air. Okay —

[Boozer rides on Deacon's bike as they set off from O'Leary Mountain.]

Boozer: Where — we goin' — Deek?
Deacon: Do you remember when we first rode outta Farewell? What that was like?
Boozer: Yeah — I — remember.

Deacon: The highways were — they were all choked up with cars, there were so
        many people — all on the move. Thinkin' that — if they could only go
        fast enough, that they'd outrun what was coming.

Boozer: Yeah —

Deacon: No one could move fast enough, Boozer. No one saw it comin' the way I
        did. So by the time they said, "fuck it," you know¹ and started
        walking, and then running — it was too late.

Boozer: Yeah — too — late.

Deacon: And I remember — watchin' the Freaks — watchin' them all come —
        thousands of 'em — and all those — all those dumbshits — just got
        swallowed up.

Boozer: Yeah — I remember.

Deacon: When you see a thing like that — you know it's only a matter of time —
        before it's our turn. And nothing's gonna stop it, Boozer. Not a
        Goddamn thing. But — but do you know why we keep going?

Boozer: No.
Deacon: Because what the hell else are we gonna do?
Boozer: Yeah.
