¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
033) NOT GONNA KILL ANYONE                                               [M033]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon drives to a small campsite overlooking Iron Mike's Lost Lake resort.
 They make camp and Deacon sets to work chopping off his beard.]

Boozer: What are you doin'?
Deacon: Nothin'.
Boozer: Uh-huh. Figured you'd get all prettied up before headin' in.

Deacon: Well, you know. Yeah, I figured I'd — Stop in the lodge, have a few
        beers, and then just stroll into the infirmary. No, no, no, man¹ I'm
        just — Just sick of it.

Boozer: Okay. I'm just fuckin' with you. Hey, Deek. Iron Mike said — he'd kill
        ya if he ever saw you again. And if he said it —

Deacon: That old man doesn't remember his name half the time.
Boozer: No, no, no. He'll remember —

Deacon: Hey — Hey. You gotta stay awake. We're off the open road, but if a
        Freaker wanders by —

Boozer: Yeah, yeah, yeah. I know. Alright. Hey Deek?
Deacon: Yeah?
Boozer: Don't you kill anyone in the camp, okay?
Deacon: I'm not gonna kill anyone. You good?
Boozer: Never better.

[Deacon sets out to infiltrate the large township. There are guards patrolling
 all over, including two near the campsite.]

LJ: What the hell, man? Let's go back. There's nothing here.
Tommy: You heard the bike, same as me.

LJ: Prob'ly some Drifter. Not worth draggin' me out here. Shit, we're supposed
    to guard the camp, not wander around jerkin' off.

Tommy: Coulda been Rippers.
LJ: Oh, against the two of us? Really.
Tommy: We could get 'em before they —

LJ: No, no, no, no. See, that's what we thought, too. Me and this guy, Addy's
    brother, we went out on patrol — you know, not far from here really. We
    kept to the shadows. It was night, but the moon was out. And you know
    Rippers love the night. We heard 'em coming, first. Shriekin' like
    Freakers, they were comin' straight outta hell. God, that sound. There
    were maybe four we could see. So we open up on 'em. They don't — they
    don't even try not to get shot. Thing is, they weren't goin' down. They
    just kept runnin' at us. My boy got one of 'em down, pulled his knife to
    finish the job. Shit, I should've told him to forget it. Two others climbed
    right on him, and I — fired.

Tommy: You fired?

LJ: Yeah, I killed him. They were tearin' him apart like Goddamn Freakers. I
    fired and got the hell outta there. So, you go after Rippers, you better
    have backup.

[Deacon stalks the patrolmen as they return through the marsh. Other sentries
 stand near a campfire.]

Ace: Nice 'n' boring guard duty. The way it should be. What're you gonna do
     later?

Kincade: Gonna try to get some sleep, that's what. That girl — Lisa, whatever.
         The new one? She cries all the damn time. First few days, she kept me
         up all night — what's her deal?

Ace: She just came in from the shit, whaddya want?
Kincade: Shit, even money, we kick her to the curb before a month's out.
Ace: Iron Mike won't go for that.
Kincade: He doesn't pay that much attention. Does he even know she's here?
Ace: Think she's hard to miss. She does cry all the time.

Kincade: But she has been quiet lately. Maybe she got wise that that wasn't
         gonna help.

Ace: Yeah, actually, I haven't seen her in awhile.

[Under cover of darkness, Deacon slips further into the camp.]

Slim: Have a little faith. Iron Mike says we got nothin' to worry about now.
      The truce with the Rippers will hold.

Jim: How the hell you gonna keep the peace with a bunch of crazy-ass lunatics,
     who cut themselves? How can you trust anything like that?

Slim: Any thing¹? These are people, not Freakers.

Jim: That's debatable. Skizzo's right. The only thing these assholes understand
     is force. We sign a peace treaty like we're the goddamn UN, we show 'em
     we're weak.

[Even further in, Skizzo and Iron Mike are discussing and wandering around.]

Deacon: Oh shit. Iron Mike, Skizzo — sonofabitch.

Skizzo: Mike, the men in there, they weren't just attacked — they were
        tortured. Joe's got scars all along his head, like they were trying to
        scalp him.

Iron Mike: Raymond?

Skizzo: And the men we buried? They were butchered, Mike, butchered. Christ,
        it took us three hours to rake up all the body parts. I didn't want to
        leave 'em for the Freaks.

Iron Mike: Raymond?

Skizzo: It's Carlos and you know it. We gotta hit 'em back or the Rippers are
        gonna —

Iron Mike: Raymond — Skizzo! Leave it be. Just leave it — be.

Skizzo: And what about the next group, Mike? And the next? Hell, Carlos is
        already pushing into Rogue Camp, Camp Pioneer.

Iron Mike: There's no proof of that.

Skizzo: They're moving up north. I heard one of those Radio Free Oregon
        broadcasts — claims they got hit by Rippers.

Iron Mike: Oh, so now you're listening to that nut job Copeland.

Skizzo: Well he may be a nut job, but I think he'd know a Ripper if one was
        comin' at him with a butcher knife.

[Deacon trails the two until they finish walking near the infirmary.]

Skizzo: They're not here. But you can go in, an' see for yourself.

Iron Mike: We'll come back. You know Addy don't like it, you snooping around
           in her business.

Skizzo: Hey, you said it, not me.

Iron Mike: I'm not laughing. Now c'mon — come back later when Addy's here. I
           wanna talk to those men myself.

Skizzo: Well let's just hope they're still breathing.

Iron Mike: Addy'll take care of 'em.

[The two walk uphill towards the lodge, leaving the infirmary's grounds.]

Deacon: There it is. I just gotta find a way inside.

[Other nighttime guards are nearby with the latest camp scuttlebutt.]

Mark: You think, uh — Addy and Rikki are a thing?
Nader: Why, you tryna get with them, or is this thing goin' into your bank?

Mark: Nah, man, I'm just curious. I was on kitchen duty, and I saw Rikki
      lookin' — fine, just — just great. She came outta her cabin, and two
      seconds later, out comes Addy. Think she had a smile on.

Nader: Well, that's gonna end in shit.
Mark: Why you say that?
Nader: Skizzo's taken a shine to her.
Mark: To — Addy?
Nader: Hell no. She'd take his head off. Rikki.
Mark: Really?
Nader: Can't imagine Rikki's go for him. If she goes for guys.

034) NO PLACE ELSE TO GO                                                 [M034]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon finally finds a moment to surreptitiously jimmy the clinic's latch. As
 he's about to steal some antibiotics, Rikki and Addy come in.]

Deacon: Ah, dammit. Hi, Rikki. Hi, Addy. Uh — I don't want any trouble, so if
        you ladies just step aside, I'll show my way out —

Addy: No, no, what the hell are you doing in my infirmary?
Deacon: What the hell — what're you doing — nuh-uh.

Rikki: Oh, are you going to shoot me now? Oh wait, wait, there's a code, right?
       You can't shoot a woman unless you have to.

[She quickly draws on him.]

Rikki: Well, now you have to.

[Deacon thinks about it and holsters his weapon.]

Deacon: Ah shit. Okay, look, why don't you just let me explain.

Rikki: Check what's in the cooler. What, are you selling narcotics for Tucker
       now? Y'know, when you brought me that girl, I thought you had changed.
       But clearly you haven't.

Addy: No, it's not narcotics. It's antibiotics.
Rikki: What?
Deacon: Boozer's — sick. He's got blood poisoning. I had no place else to go.
Rikki: Blood poisoning? What happened?
Addy: Does it matter?
Deacon: I fucked up.
Addy: Bring him in. Go and get him. Bring him here.
Rikki: No, we can't do that —

Addy: Yes, we can. Look, I don't care who he is, and I don't care what Iron
      Mike thinks. When a man is sick, a man is sick. We have to look after
      each other. Baby, it's all we got.

[She lowers her weapon and heads out the door.]

Rikki: C'mon, I'll give you a ride. Which way we headed?

Deacon: You remember there was a small camp, when we first rode into the
        valley?

Rikki: Yeah, I remember.

Deacon: You call this a bike?

Rikki: It may not be a fancy "Drifter" bike, but it gets the job done. Get on.

[They leave camp.]

Deacon: So how's she doing? The girl that I brought in, Lisa. Are you — are
        you gonna take me to see her?

Rikki: No.

Deacon: Goddammit Rikki — what the hell — why not?

Rikki: I can't. She's not here.

Deacon: Wait, wait — hold on a second, what? Where is she?

Rikki: A few days ago, Skizzo assigned her to a scavenge run. She and three
       others headed over to the Rogue Camp to look for supplies. They came
       back without her.

Deacon: You're telling me they left her — they left her out in the shit?

Rikki: They didn't leave anyone. They said she ran off.

Deacon: Jesus!

Rikki: It could have been anything. Wolves, Freaks, Rippers — choose your
       poison.

Deacon: And what — what was Skizzo thinking, sending her out on a supply run?

Rikki: Everyone's gotta work, Deek — that's the deal — and you know it.

Deacon: I don't believe this shit, look — she'd been surviving in Marion Forks
        for years when I found her.

Rikki: Yeah? Then maybe you should've left her there.

[They pull into Boozer's campsite.]

Boozer: Who's there? Get back — don't make me blow you Goddamn head off.
Deacon: Hey Boozer — it's me.
Boozer: No, get back!

Rikki: Oh. Hey — Hey, it's uh, it's Rikki. You remember me? I rode with you
       guys a year ago.

Boozer: Rikki — Tumalo?
Rikki: Yeah.
Boozer: That's, uh — Tumalo to — to Lost Lake?
Rikki: Yeah — yeah, man.
Deacon: Hold — hold up — hold up.
Rikki: That's right. How — how you doin' there — Boozer? You doin' alright?
Boozer: Oh — just peachy.
Rikki: It still didn't give you the right to steal our shit.
Deacon: Are you kidding me? Look at his arm, what was I supposed to do? Huh?

Rikki: I — I don't know — maybe ask. Jesus. Look at you guys, the biker boys.
       The most badass Drifters in the shit, right? And now you come back
       crawling to Iron Mike — Oh wait — if he'll let you. C'mon. Just help me
       get him back to Addy. Let's go.

Deacon: C'mon, pal. Let's —
Boozer: Don't need your help. Rikki.
Rikki: Yeah, Boozer. Rikki.

[Boozer hops on back of Deacon's bike as they ride back.]

Boozer: Wait, where — where are we goin'?

Deacon: Addy said — she's agreed to — to take a look at your arm, and — and
        see what she can do —

Boozer: What — no! No, you're not taking me to some Goddamn camp. I can ride,
        dammit —

Deacon: We're not — dammit, Boozer, it's just for a few days. Get some shit for
        your arm and then —

Boozer: No — you know what it's like there, Deek.

Deacon: No, you're not thinkin' straight — this isn't the Hot Springs, this is
        Lost Lake — Iron Mike, remember him?

Boozer: Iron Mike? He's gonna get us killed. You said —

Deacon: That was a long time ago, they built the place up — they — they got
        more people —

Boozer: We're all gonna fuckin' die —

Deacon: We'll be long gone before anything like that happens — Camp's got the
        only doc in a hundred miles. Now, Addy — look, she'll take care of it —

Boozer: Just — just a couple'a days. Yeah, then we ride the hell outta here —
        Ride north, like you said — get the hell away from all this —

Deacon: Yeah. Yeah — we ride north. Leave all this shit behind.

035) WE'VE ALL DONE THINGS                                               [M035]

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Later, after Boozer gets situated in the clinic...]

Addy: Okay, so — I'm gonna go back and check on him and — Make sure he's okay.

Rikki: Coward.

Addy: Yeah, you got that right.

Deacon: Uh, how long? Um — until he can ride, I mean.

Addy: You mean, "How long do you have to be here?" Look, we have antibiotics,
      but — it's not enough. If Iron Mike lets you stay — your friend will have
      a chance.

[Deek walks with Rikki up to Iron Mike's lodge.]

Rikki: So what happened? How'd he burn his arm like that?

Deacon: We ran into some Rippers, south of Belknap — Guess they didn't like
        his tattoos.

Rikki: Jesus — I've heard about 'em doing shit like that to themselves, but
       not to people they're trying to recruit —

Deacon: Boozer wasn't any Goddamn recruit.

Rikki: Uh, guess Tucker shoulda made a deal with them like Iron Mike —

Deacon: C'mon, Rikki, just — he doesn't get it. Carlos isn't going to honor
        some deal with Lost Lake — not for long anyway, and Mike — he just
        doesn't see it.

Rikki: He sees more than you think. You've always had your good side, Deek —
       you've just been doing your best to kill it.

Deacon: Thanks for the vote of confidence.

[They enter the lodge; Skizzo is already there, discussing something.]

Skizzo: You cannot believe a word he's going to say. Addy is soft. Mike, we
        do not have enough for those that pull their own weight, let alone a
        Goddamn cripple.

Deacon: He's not a cripple. He can work. He —
Iron Mike: Oh, hold on.
Skizzo: I say we throw them out on their asses.
Rikki: Mike, that is not who we are —

Skizzo: Jesus. Listen to you. And you — You tired of bein' Tucker's little
        bitch, finally? Huh?

Rikki: Raymond, stop it —
Skizzo: Don't call me that.
Deacon: I'm pretty tired alright —

[Deacon draws on him and Skizzo does the same.]

Iron Mike: Alright, enough!
Skizzo: See? See?! You know who the fuck this guy is and you know what he's —
Iron Mike: You hold on! And you? You put that shit away.
Rikki: Mike — Deacon was the one that brought me the girl —

Iron Mike: I know. I know. And I know what kind of man he is, what he's done.
           He done any worse than you? Rikki? How 'bout me? We've all been out
           in the shit, Skizzo. We've all done things we're not proud of.

Rikki: We need another rider.
Deacon: Oh now wait a minute — I just need a few days and some antibiotics.

[Rikki, who was just sticking up for him, gets exasperated and turns away.]

Deacon: I'll do whatever it takes.
Skizzo: Sure, Mike. Whatever you say. I'm on board.
Iron Mike: Walk with me.

[They leave and let the other two fight amongst themselves. Some of this chat
 lacks subtitles, so I winged it.]

Rikki: I don't trust you —
Skizzo: Don't start with me. So, you're the one who brought him in?
Rikki: I didn't "bring" him in. Boozer needed help.
Skizzo: But he broke into the infirmary!

Rikki: The tackle shop isn't exactly secure. You were supposed to fix that
       weeks ago.

Skizzo: Oh, so what, you're hooked up with Addy, so now I gotta go over and
        fix her locks?

Rikki: Isn't that your job?

Skizzo: No, it's not my job. My job is keeping the camp safe. Addy's job is
        keeping the drugs safe.

Rikki: Sure, whatever.
Skizzo: Don't tell me how to do my job.

[Outside...]

Iron Mike: Rikki told me you stopped runnin' for Tucker. Sent that little girl
           here instead.

Deacon: I'm sorry I lied to you, before, about doing runs for Tucker.
Iron Mike: How long you been driftin'? You and Bill?
Deacon: I don't know. Like I said, time gets lost.

Iron Mike: If folks don't put down some roots, figure this shit out, grow some
           food, come next spring? Won't be none of us left.

Deacon: If you give Boozer what he needs, let us hole up here 'til he can
        ride — like I said, I'll do whatever you need. I just, I — I want you
        to know that as soon as he's patched up — we're gonna put together some
        gear, we're gonna ride north.

Iron Mike: North, huh?

Deacon: There's a camp up there, near Smith Rock — Boozer's never been there,
        anyway. Got a lot of ghosts down here. It's time we move on.

Iron Mike: Fresh start, eh? Yeah, I can respect that. Alright — don't make me
           regret this, Deek. Now go on, leave me be. I got some thinkin' to
           do.

Deacon: Sure¹ Mike, yeah, whatever you say — just — have Rikki radio me if you
        need something.

[Later, if Deacon wanders toward Blair's merchant stall:]

Blair: Deek, Deek, Deek — what's been keeping you away so long?
Deacon: Blair — how ya doing?

Blair: Hey, I gotta ask you. I heard you riding in last night, with Rikki and
       uh — who's that guy?

Deacon: Boozer, or his name is William or Bill — I've always just called him
        Boozer. Don't ask why.

Blair: I wasn't — I mean — is he gonna be okay? I stopped by to say hi to Addy
       — he didn't look so good.

Deacon: Yeah, he's gonna be fine. Soon as he's patched up, we're riding north,
        you got that? So just drop it. Okay?

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
036) SHERMAN'S CAMP IS CRAWLING                                          [M036]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon heads over to Addy's infirmary.]

Addy: Deacon — hey. Is everything okay? What's wrong?
Deacon: Uh — actually, that's not why I'm here.
Addy: Okay.
Deacon: Came by to see if there's anything you need. For the uh, infirmary.

Addy: Actually, we're running low on everything. I mean, we could always — use
      more meds, sterile bandages, instruments. Uh, here.

[He looks at her list.]

Deacon: Hmm, a Liston knife?

Addy: Yeah, it was used by doctors in the Civil War to perform operations in
      the field.

Deacon: Operations?

Addy: Yeah, y'know, when they didn't have anesthesia or laudanum. I wrote down
      where you might be able to find one. It's the brochure for — the
      visitor's center at Sherman's Camp, yeah.

Deacon: Sherman's Camp. Yeah, the place crawling with all the Freakers. I'll
        see what I can do.

Addy: Yeah — I — Deacon — Thank you.

[He leaves the clinic.]

Deacon: I gotta find a Liston knife — Head to — Sherman's Camp — place is gonna
        be crawlin'.

[He can see the Freaker-infested hellhole from a high road.]

Deacon: Sherman's Camp — gettin' close — Here it is —

[He finds the boarded-up destination.]

Deacon: Visitor's center. Gotta find a way inside.

[He shoots the latch off the fire escape and enters.]

Deacon: Gotta be in here somewhere. Down here — Not much left — this place has
        been picked over clean —

[He smashes an exhibit to find the knife.]

Deacon: Liston knife. This is it. Gotta get it back to Addy.

[Deek rides back.]

Deacon: Addy, I got that knife you were lookin' for.
Addy: Thank you¹ Deacon. You have no idea how badly we need this.
Deacon: No problem. Glad to help.

[He makes it back to Lost Lake.]

Addy: Hey.
Deacon: Oh. Here's that knife you were looking for.
Addy: Thank you so much.
Deacon: Yeah, no problem.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
037) I NEED YOUR HELP                                                    [M037]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[While doing "Sherman's Camp is Crawling," the NERO radio springs to life.]

O'Brian: Hello? Is anyone on this channel?
Deacon: O'Brian? Is that you?

O'Brian: Yes — yeah. It's — it's O'Brian. You still have one of our radios.
         Good. Okay. Look. I'm gonna try and help you — find out about the
         woman —

Deacon: Sarah Whitaker. I put her on your chopper that night —

O'Brian: Yeah, yeah, yeah. I know. Okay. But first, you gotta do something for
         me.

Deacon: Wait, what? You need something from me.

O'Brian: Look, there's a digital display on your radio. I'm going to send you
         a coded message. Coordinates. Meet me at that location.

Deacon: O'Brian — what the hell's this all about?

O'Brian: Just meet me there. There will be NERO soldiers all around me, like
         before,¹ don't let them see you. O'Brian out.

[Deacon heads for the NERO site.]

Deacon: Alright — I'm here.
O'Brian: Jesus — don't — don't sneak up on me like that.

Deacon: Did you find out anything about Sarah — about the woman I put on your
        chopper?

O'Brian: Nothing.
Deacon: Nothing?

O'Brian: Hey, hey — wait, wait, wait, wait. It's gonna take some time, okay?
         I'm risking my neck here. If anyone back — back at HQ finds out?
         Those — those guys with the guns over there? They follow orders
         without question.

Deacon: You're all — on the same team, O'Brian.

O'Brian: Look — it just looks that way. Look, I don't have time to explain it
         right now, but — It's why I need your help.

Deacon: My help —

O'Brian: Look, just take it. It's a — it's a — Wavelength recorder and some
         GPS trackers. I just need you to — We're outta time. Look — shit, I
         don't even know your name.

Deacon: Deacon — Deacon St. John.

O'Brian: Yeah, well look — Deacon St. John — If you want me to risk my neck
         helping you find whatever-her-name — uh, Sarah? Then yeah, I'm gonna
         need you to do something for me. Okay. Keep that radio close. I'll
         contact you in a couple minutes.

[O'Brian leaves the package with Deacon and amscrays.]

Deacon: You don't even know my name — well you're gonna know it before we're
        done, O'Brian. And keep the radio close — it's been right here the
        whole time, you sonofabitch. Jesus Christ — how long do I have to wait
        now —

O'Brian: Hello, you there? Deacon?
Deacon: Yeah, I'm here. Now what's this all about? What do you want?
O'Brian: Alright, I put a blocker on this channel. It's secure.
Deacon: What do you want?

O'Brian: I've sent a series of coordinates to your radio. I need you to go to
         those locations and —

Deacon: What? Why?

O'Brian: Just listen to me. There are several NERO task groups doing work in
         the field. I need to know what they're doing.

Deacon: Then why don't you ask them?

O'Brian: I can't. Look. I said it's a long story and I don't have time to get
         into it right now. Let's just say, the men above me, way above me,
         are running a lot of field missions, all separate from each other.
         Nobody knows what anybody else is doing.

Deacon: So the world ends and you assholes carry on like nothing's changed.
        Where?

O'Brian: I sent you the coordinates.
Deacon: Okay, Jesus — O'Brian — alright, I will see what I can do.

O'Brian: Just — get to as many of them as you can. There are active LZs,
         landing sites, sample drop off locations —

Deacon: Yeah, yeah, I got it. But you better have something for me, O'Brian.

O'Brian: Yeah, yeah — I got it too. Hold on — Drifter — One of our helos is
         heading toward your position now. You have to follow it.

Deacon: Follow it? Why?
O'Brian: Just — go. Don't lose it.

Deacon: Jesus — okay, alright. What's going on, O'Brian? Why am I out here in
        the shit chasing choppers down for you?

O'Brian: The destination is classified, I'm locked out of their files — so I
         can't give you the coordinates to their LZ. You have to follow them
         in.

Deacon: Jesus, don't you guys have, uh — spy satellites, shit like that?
O'Brian: Not that I have access to, no. I told you, I'm —
Deacon: — locked out, yeah, I heard you.
O'Brian: Don't lose them.
Deacon: Huh, slowing down. O'Brian. They're landing.

O'Brian: Good. I have their coordinates now via your radio. You better go in
         on foot.

Deacon: On foot.
O'Brian: Remember, you can't let them see you.
Deacon: O'Brian — I'm here. What do you want me to do?

O'Brian: Each of these research units have a science guy like me guarded by a
         bunch of goons. I need you to get close to the researcher. The
         wavelength recorder is set to the channel we use to record data.
         It'll record everything they're doing.

Deacon: Okay, so you want me to sneak into an LZ, filled with heavily armed,
        Kevlar wearing¹ soldiers who shoot on sight, so you can spy on some
        asshole wearing a pocket protector?

O'Brian: Pocket protector? Really? I have a fucking PhD, asshole.
Deacon: Yeah, which stands for piled high and deep.
O'Brian: Do you still have the tracking devices I gave you?

Deacon: Oh, I was gonna sell 'em, but most of us don't have access to shit
        like — you know, satellites.

O'Brian: Place one of them on their helo. Almost all of these filed missions
         include stops that aren't on the books. I want to find out where
         they're going next.

Deacon: O'Brian —

O'Brian: You don't need to ask. I'm already looking into what records we have
         about where evacuees were taken. O'Brian out.

Deacon: This has gotta be it. What the hell are you guys doing out here?

[Deacon sneaks in closer, puts a tracking device on the chopper, then sneaks
 closer to a researcher with a pinned-down Freaker subject.]

Lt. Chavez: Field Note Two Zero Seven One. Checking the traps at site Fourteen
            Alpha have confirmed a large, male subject, with the confirmed
            albinism mutation. Subject has expected lack of skin pigmentation
            and reddish eyes. Muscle mass appears to be forty percent greater
            than normal infected subjects. What was it you called them?
            "Bleachers?" Well, they're real. While this is only the third
            subject we've been able to study — as noted, their strength and
            ability to absorb damage make them extremely dangerous to approach
            — we've noted in other field reports that over a thousand have been
            spotted in this area. Whatever is causing the mutation, it's
            spreading rapidly.

Deacon: What the hell, O'Brian.¹

O'Brian: What's wrong?

Deacon: I'll tell ya what's wrong. Your boys were carving out the guts of a
        Freak while it was still alive.

O'Brian: They're not "my boys." And what do you care? Aren't you a — what do
         you guys like to call yourselves? Drifters? Don't you kill the
         infected for money, or whatever shit you barter with?

Deacon: Yeah, I kill Freaks, but I don't carve them open while they're still
        alive and listen to 'em scream.

O'Brian: Did you get my data?
Deacon: Yeah. I got your data.
O'Brian: Okay, I'm uploading it now. I'll be in touch. O'Brian out.

Deacon: O'Brian? O'Brian? Ah, Goddammit, he did it again. O'Brian? Talk to me —
        Shit. You better be in touch, O'Brian.

[Afterwards, another truther message plays.

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. It's with a
          heavy heart that I report six deaths and two injuries from my camp
          this week. And not from the usual shit — no, it was those damn black
          choppers. Let me tell you, everything I been warning you about¹ it,
          is absolutely comin' true. Heard those choppers touched down and
          wiped out an entire group of men and women who were screamin' and
          beggin' for mercy. Citizens of this country, and they cut 'em down.
          My men returned fire, but — shit. This won't be the last we hear of
          'em, either. They're hunting us down, those of us who dared to
          survive and mess with their plans. They're killin' us off, so they
          can finally emerge from their gopher holes. Stay vigilant, people,
          and keeps your eyes on the sky. This is Mark Copeland for Radio Free
          Oregon. Don't believe the lies.

038) SEARCHING FOR LISA                                                  [M038]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After hearing how Lisa went missing, Deacon rides to Rogue Camp, an wintry,
 overrun suburb a ways away from Lost Lake.]

Deacon: Okay, this has gotta be it. Lisa? I'm coming for you. She's gotta be
        out here somewhere. Alright, where are you, kid? Ah, Goddammit, you
        gotta be around here somewhere. No, no. Not in here.

[After searching around, Deacon finds a house he can't enter easily.]

Deacon: Now, how the hell am I going to get in? Locked. Nope.

[He pushes a car away from a cracked garage door.]

Deacon: Through here, yeah — this'll do it. Inside here —

[He finds some scribbles on a shelf in a girl's bedroom.]

Deacon: Is this Lisa's handwriting? "I Want to Forget" — that sounds like
        something she would write.

039) NOW YOU SEE IT                                                      [M039]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon returns back to Lost Lake's infirmary to check on Boozer.]

Deacon: Hey, I came by to see how the lazy bastard's doing. How you doin',
        Boozeman? Are you — you tired of layin' around — yet —

[He sees Boozer in a bad way, moaning and groaning.]

Deacon: Boozer? Hey —
Addy: You can't be in here, Deacon. C'mon — Deacon.
Deacon: C'mon, c'mon — hey, what's going on? How's he doing?
Addy: He needs his rest.
Deacon: Don't mess around with me, Addy. I asked you — how is he doin'?
Boozer: I'm good, I'm good.
Addy: Not good.
Boozer: Damn, it's cold —
Deacon: But, the antibiotics —
Addy: They're not enough. They're never enough.
Deacon: No, wait a second, you said that if I —
Addy: I said — that we would try. Look, all we can do is wait.
Deacon: Wait. Okay. Alright.
Boozer: Deek — Deek —
Deacon: No, there's — You know what, there's something I can do about this —
Addy: Deacon — Deacon. Deacon — Deacon, stop. Stop!
Deacon: I can get — What?!

Addy: I know you wanna smash something — I see that look in your eyes. But you
      know what? You go right ahead, but you do it out there —

Deacon: Addy, I can —

Addy: Go. Look — there is nothing else you can do. Please — just go home. Go.
      Home. Deacon.

Boozer: Deek — Deek —

[Addy shuts the door as a delirious Boozer calls out for him. Skizzo nears.]

Skizzo: So, he gonna make it?
Deacon: Yeah, Skizzo, he'll be fine. I just — he needs a few days.
Skizzo: Come with me to the lodge. I wanna show you something.
Deacon: I got shit to do.

Skizzo: I'm stickin' my neck out here. Trust me, you're gonna want to see this.
        Just — just listen. Coupla months back, this Drifter comes into camp,
        tellin' all kind of crazy stories. Said he worked at the airport, was
        on the ground, back in Farewell, when shit went down. One night they
        were expecting a flight in from Portland — only it never shows up. The
        plane? Was doing a haul for the Red Cross.

Deacon: The Red Cross?

Skizzo: Yeah, you getting it? Medicine, doctor shit, cargo hold full of it.
        Maybe even some of those uh, anti-whateverthefucks —

Deacon: Antibiotics.
Skizzo: Yeah, yeah, yeah, shit like that. Just like that.
Deacon: Where?
Skizzo: Hey, keep your voice down¹ willya? Let's talk inside.

[They enter Iron Mike's lodge and walk to a map.]

Skizzo: So this Drifter. He's working in the control tower when the plane
        disappears off the radar — Poof. Now you see it, now you don't. Right
        about — here.

Deacon: South of Mount Washington.

Skizzo: That's what he said. It came down intact. A controlled crash or
        whatever. Guy's got to listen to the pilot bleeding out from a broken
        pelvis on the ground.

Deacon: Okay, so you haven't sent anyone to find this.

Skizzo: Nope.

Deacon: Why not?

Skizzo: 'Cause the old man won't have it.

Deacon: Iron Mike? What the — oh, right. Rippers.

Skizzo: You catch on quick. Everything west of the Iron Ridge here — Belongs
        to Carlos and his merry band a' bald-headed freak-a-likes.

Deacon: Shit.

Skizzo: So, you go over there and get caught? You head north, brother.
        Otherwise, Iron Mike's treaty with Rest in Peace goes — just like that.

Deacon: Okay, yeah, no, yeah — I get it, I get it. Let me ask you a question.
        Why are you tellin' me this?

Skizzo: Oh, wait a minute — first off, I'm not telling you shit. You remember
        that. Second off, you're a Goddamn Drifter. What am I supposed to do,
        follow you around like I'm your little bitch? Keep your ass outta
        trouble?

Deacon: Alright.

Skizzo: I have things to do.

Deacon: I get it. You're just a regular stand-up guy, right¹ Skizzo?

Skizzo: Just tryin' to stay alive, like everybody else. Hey. You do what you
        gotta do. The end a' the day? That's all we got. Do you know what I'm
        saying?

Deacon: I know what you're saying, Skizzo.

Skizzo: Keep your radio close. I'll be in touch.

[Skizzo leaves.]

Deacon: Yeah, Skizzo, we can always count on you. Shit — now what? Anything's
        better than standing around this shithole.

[Later, as Deek rides outside of town:]

Skizzo: Hey, St. John. You there?

Deacon: Yeah, Skizzo. I'm here.

Skizzo: Yeah, that business we were talkin' about? It's gonna take me a bit —
        I gotta go check on security at the border with Iron Butte — check on
        the Rippers there, if you know what I mean.

Deacon: Uh — no, Skizzo, I don't got a clue. Why don't ya spell it out for me?

Skizzo: Nice try, smart ass¹. Remember, I'm goin' out on a limb here. Don't
        make me regret it. Anyway, I'll be in touch real soon. In the meantime,
        make yourself useful around camp. Prove Iron Mike was right for a
        change.

Deacon: Yeah, sure, whatever you say, whatever you say. St. John out.

[Even later still...]

Skizzo: Hey, St. John. Where you at¹ brother?

Deacon: I'm here, Skizzo, but I'm not your Goddamn brother.

Skizzo: Hey, no skin off my nose. Just doin' what I can to help your bro. That
        business we discussed? Let's just say, uh — you should head out that
        way now.

Deacon: Oh, you mean the border with the Rippers.

Skizzo: Very funny. I meant no such thing. Huh — all I said was, if you were
        thinkin' about takin' a ride — what do you Drifters like to call it?
        Ridin' the open road — now would be a good time to do it. You got me?

Deacon: Yeah, Skizzo, like always, I got you. St. John out.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
040) PLAYING ALL NIGHT                                                   [M040]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon heads to the deserted border bridge at Camp Pioneer.]

Deacon: Skizzo, it's St. John. I'm at the border.
Skizzo: You see any of my men around?
Deacon: No, Skizzo, it's clear. Look, how much time do I got?

Skizzo: Time? Time for what? All I know is I got a card game going on with a
        few of my guys — Couple of 'em, maybe they should be out on guard duty,
        but I'm lettin' that slide. If I had to guess, I'd say we'd be playin'
        all night.

Deacon: So until morning. Got it. Deacon out. Yeah, this is it —

[He creeps into Ripper territory and eventually finds the downed plane.]

Deacon: Oh Jesus — hell of a mess —

[From behind some wreckage, a gigantic musclebound Freaker rips another apart.
 This is a new type -- a Breaker -- and it's killed only with much effort.]

Deacon: That it? Jesus H. Christ — One — tough — sonofabitch — Antibiotics.
        Gotta find me some antibiotics — Let's see — Yes — this'll work —
        Gotta get 'em back to my bike.

[Deacon returns to his ride and secures the medical cooler.]

Deacon: These'll fix him up — an' then we ride outta here. Head north, like he
        said.

Rikki: Deacon St. John, you there? Deek, this is Rikki, over.

Deacon: Dammit, I can't let her know I'm out here — Uh, hey, Rikki? This is
        Deek, uh — you're breakin' up, I can't hear ya —

Rikki: Deek, where are you? I need to get —

[He shuts off his radio.]

Deacon: Yeah, sorry¹ Rikki — I don't have time for this right now.

[Deacon returns back to Lost Lake territory in the morning.]

044) FLOW LIKE BURIED RIVERS                                             [M044]

Deacon: This is how.

        Freaks do.

Deacon: Few days ago, I was riding north of Belknap Crater, when a chopper flew

Iron Mike: A chopper. What the hell?

Deacon: Just listen to me. It was a black chopper — one of those NERO choppers
        that used to fly all over the Goddamn place, when the shit was going
        down.

Iron Mike: And you saw one — still flying.

Deacon: I followed them, I stole one of their radios. I've been tryin' to track

Iron Mike: They got resources to do that, while we're out here starving,

Deacon: I followed 'em up to the Grotto Caves, you know the ones?
Iron Mike: Yeah.

Deacon: They had motion sensors set up, measuring how many Freaks used the cave

Iron Mike: That right.

Deacon: They said Freaks all up and down the Cascade range, south of Crater

Iron Mike: Hey — this idea of yours — it's got some merit. But — Job like that,

Deacon: You said you wanted help making Lost Lake safer? This is how we do it.

Iron Mike: Alright. Alright, look. There's some things I gotta do. Okay? But
           you meet me at the bridge in a couple of minutes. I know where we
           can find some.

045) YOU SEE WHAT THEY DID                                               [M045]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

        you brought me here because you wanted me to see this.

Iron Mike: Not true. Alright, you got the key? We're gonna go get the maps to
           those mines, just like I said, and we're gonna get more'n enough
           TNT to seal every cave in the valley.

Deacon: Bullshit.
Iron Mike: You are right about one thing — I'm not sorry you've seen it.

Iron Mike: I am talking about the war that's coming! With the Rippers — the one

Iron Mike: Almost no one, point of fact — but I tolerate most, even smartass
           Drifters — C'mon —

046) DO YOU HAVE MY BACK?                                                [M046]
_______________________________________________________________________________

        not anymore.

Lt. Booth: Field Note Two Zero Six Zero — We've now completed the survey of
           twenty-four nesting sites, including those at Marion Forks, the
           Pioneer Cemetery, the Cascade Highway lumber site, the truck stop
           on the Old Belknap Road — what was that called again?

Cpl. Franklin: Ah, Crazy Willie's —

           don't miss — Crazy Willie's, south of the Belknap Crater.

Cpl. Franklin: I got a question¹ doc.

Cpl. Franklin: The nests — why do they build 'em?
Lt. Booth: We don't know.

Lt. Booth: We have a theory that —

Cpl. Franklin: I mean, we never see 'em where wild animals build them, in

Lt. Booth: — you finished?
Cpl. Franklin: Sorry.

Lt. Booth: The guys back at the lab have a theory. I'm sure when they're ready

Cpl. Franklin: Jesus — just asking. I see things too, you know. I wasn't always

Lt. Booth: Can I continue?
Cpl. Franklin: Sure.

Lt. Booth: — south of Belknap Crater. Some areas of the Belknap Wilderness

Cpl. Franklin: Salome Hot Springs —

Lt. Booth: Ah yes — "Salome." "On Herod's birthday, she danced before them,

       just a good way to stay alive.

Rikki: That's why I'm at the camp. You know — chance to live a normal life
       again.

Deacon: Good luck with that.
Rikki: It's nothing serious — me and Addy.
Deacon: Didn't look that way to me.
Rikki: Yeah well, things happen fast these days. You know what I mean?
Deacon: Didn't ask. I wanted to tell you something.
Rikki: Shoot.

Deacon: I, uh — look, I appreciate you going to bat for me, for me and Boozer.
        With Iron Mike I mean.

Rikki: Wow, you are gettin' soft.
Deacon: Fuck off.
Rikki: You've never thanked me for anything.
Deacon: Yeah, well, maybe I never had any reason to.
Rikki: Okay. So where'd you and Iron Mike go the other day?
Deacon: Wait, you said that he already told you about it.

Rikki: He was pretty tight-lipped. I've known Iron Mike a long time, and to be
       honest, I — I don't think I've ever seen him so — I don't know —
       depressed. Where'd you go?

Deacon: Sherman's Camp.

Rikki: I heard that place was a Freakshow.

Deacon: It is. But we didn't have much of a choice. I¹ uh — I had an idea about
        sealing the caves, keep the Hordes from coming through. He knew where
        the mining claims office was. We picked up some maps. He's gonna track
        down some explosives.

Rikki: Your radio must be broken. Almost sounded like you volunteered for some
       shit.

Deacon: I'm riding with you now¹ aren't I? Jesus.
Rikki: You just wanted out of marsh duty.
Deacon: Okay. You got me.
Rikki: So what happened? Something happened.
Deacon: Nothing, Rikki. Nothing happened.
Rikki: He didn't say anything?

Deacon: Just — no. No. Nothing happened. And no, Iron Mike didn't say anything.
        Like you said, he's a pretty tight-lipped guy.

051) IT COULDN'T BE THAT EASY                                            [M051]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Eventually, the pair comes to the hydroelectric dam in Cascade territory.]

Deacon: Alright, dam's coming up. Take it slow near the gate. No idea who or
        what may be living there.

Rikki: Got it.
Deacon: Well, it looks clear.
Rikki: What, are you expecting trouble?
Deacon: Yeah, always. And if we run into any, we're gone.
Rikki: Alright, come on. I wanna check the outflow.
Deacon: Where are you going?
Rikki: Down here.

[They walk down to the outflow and see the stream is barely moving.]

Rikki: Oh no, no, no. Hey this isn't right. There should be more water flowing
       out. Right there.

Deacon: Yeah?
Rikki: Yeah. And you hear that?
Deacon: What — what?

Rikki: Exactly. If the turbines were running, you'd be able to hear the hum of
       the lines from here.

[She looks up at a broken bridge.]

Rikki: Oh, what happened there?

Deacon: What? Oh, same thing that happened to all the bridges. Smart men in
        uniforms decided blowing 'em up would keep the Hordes from coming in.

Rikki: Hordes of refugees or Hordes of Freaks?
Deacon: Well you figure men like Copeland? Probably both.
Rikki: Alright, c'mon, I wanna check something out.

[They walk to the center of the outdoor complex. Rikki leans against a door.]

Rikki: C'mere, touch this. C'mon.
Deacon: Whaddya —
Rikki: 'Kay. You feel anything?
Deacon: No.

Rikki: Exactly. If more water was flowing, the turbines would be vibrating.
       C'mon. Up this way. We're going all the way up to the top, up there.

Deacon: Following you.

Rikki: See these pipes? They're called the penstock. Water pressure builds up
       from the reservoir and is pushed down through those pipes, concentrating
       the force of the flow, which goes right through to the turbines.

Deacon: How the hell do you know all this stuff?

Rikki: I had two older brothers who were always fixing cars and shit, with my
       dad. He got me a job at Boeing when I was only seventeen. I was going
       to school part time, to become a mechanical engineer, when shit went
       down.

Deacon: You ever see 'em again? Your dad, brothers?
Rikki: No. C'mon. Over here.

[They climb to the top and look out over the dam reservoir.]

Rikki: Alright. Well, let's figure this out. Well, this is gonna be fun.
Deacon: So now what — hold —

[He sees she's stripping.]

Deacon: Wait, what's — what's going on, what're you doin'?

Rikki: We only rode together a few months but in all that time, I never saw
       you volunteer for anything. One of us has to jump down there and clear
       the intake. So — I'm up. Oh but you can stand and — watch. Okay. Well,
       it's now or never. Let's go.

[She jumps in.]

Rikki: Yeah, it's — it's pretty mucked up. I think I can clear it though. Run
       back down to the turbine. See if it's vibrating at all.

[He does.]

Deacon: Hmmm, nothing. Wait a second — there it is. Yep, that did it.

[By the time he climbs back up, Rikki's already up and changed.]

Rikki: Ha, ha, ha! You feel that vibration?
Deacon: Yeah, but the power lines are still dead.

Rikki: What? Man, well it couldn't be that easy, right? Alright, c'mon — let's
       check out the transformers.

Deacon: So, uh — your dad and your brothers, what happened to 'em?

Rikki: I don't know. On my way back, I tried calling over and over — always
       got a busy signal — By the time I reached the house, it was deserted.
       The entire neighborhood was deserted. There were flyers everywhere,
       evacuation orders. I went to the closest refugee camp but — it was
       overrun. Everyone was dead. Freaks were everywhere.

Deacon: Jesus, Rikki. I'm real sorry.
Rikki: Yeah, it was a long time ago.

[They walk over to some machinery.]

Rikki: Hm, these are the ones feeding the lines going south.
Deacon: Alright, any idea what's wrong with 'em? —

Rikki: No, not a clue. Okay. Well, it might be a short in the turbine junction
       boxes. So let's just go down and check it out. Okay?

Deacon: Oh, alright. So, uh — what's with you and Skizzo? I mean it seems like
        you're always on the verge of ripping his throat out.

Rikki: A few months back, Addy and I caught him hiding outside our cabin while
       we were — bathing.

Deacon: What? Oh God, he's a peeping Tom?

Rikki: I told him if it happened again, he'd find out that my gun is bigger
       than his.

Deacon: Jesus. You know, if Addy was there — Skizzo probably wasn't looking at
        you.

Rikki: Ha, it was all I could do to stop her from neutering the bastard.
Deacon: Ouch.
Rikki: Right? Never piss off a woman who knows how to use a scalpel.

[They reach a locked gate.]

Rikki: Here, boost me up.
Deacon: Okay — okay, got it.

Rikki: There. Here, I got the gate. Come on. Junction room's right around here
       — Oh God — what is that smell?

Deacon: Freaker nests. From the smell of it, more than a couple. Stay close.
        How many Molotovs you got with you?

Rikki: Enough.
Deacon: Okay — remember the drill? You light 'em up, I knock 'em down.
Rikki: God, it's been awhile, but I remember.
Deacon: Time to burn — Here they come!
Rikki: Ready —

[They destroy a nest and its inhabitants.]

Rikki: It's over —
Deacon: Burn it down — You ready?
Rikki: Oh yeah.

[They destroy the final nest.]

Deacon: You good?
Rikki: Yeah. They really don't like visitors much, do they?
Deacon: Well, can you blame 'em?

Rikki: Well, they better get used to this shit. Y'know, as of today, I'm
       claiming this for Lost Lake Camp.

Deacon: Power to the people.

Rikki: Alright. Let's check the junction boxes and get the hell outta here.
       This is it. You ready?

Deacon: Yep.

Rikki: Okay — Down.

[The lever switches on the lights.]

Rikki: Yes! Houston, we have power.

Deacon: Nice work.

Rikki: I couldn't have done it without you.

Deacon: Come on. Let's find something to block the door with. I don't wanna
        have to come back up here every month to clean this shit out.

Rikki: Wait, wait, wait — you're gonna be here in a month?

Deacon: What? No. I — I don't know. Would you just — Jesus Christ.
Rikki: I'm just fuckin' with ya¹ Deek. C'mon. So why'd you ask about my dad
       and my brothers?

Deacon: Uh — I don't know. You just, um — you never mentioned 'em before. So
        I'm — you know I'm sorry if I — if it's something you didn't want to
        talk about.

Rikki: No it's fine. In fact, it reminded me of something I wanted to ask you —
       back when we were riding together —

Deacon: Okay, Rikki — Rikki — not now — you can ask me later.

Rikki: What¹ no — hey — hey —

Deacon: Come on — we gotta get moving —

052) THAT'S WHEN I KNEW                                                  [M052]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[They walk back outside.]

Rikki: Hey, you never asked — uh — why I stopped riding with you and Boozer.

Deacon: Was I supposed to ask? I already knew why. Iron Mike's bullshit. God —
        Rikki. Do we gotta do this now?

Rikki: We had been riding together for I — I don't remember, a couple months —

[He interrupts with fake laughter.]

Deacon: Where is this — okay.

Rikki: Deek, c'mon. Okay. There was this one night, and I remember it really
       clearly. It was snowing outside and — Boozer was snoring. You remember
       how he used to snore? I swear, I thought — he was gonna bring a Horde
       down on us, right?

Deacon: Yeah, well, that — pretty much hasn't changed.

Rikki: Anyway, you thought everyone was asleep and you were — Sitting outside

[He hands her his photo of Sarah.]

Rikki: That I didn't want to end up — Like so many of us here — we're — trapped
       in the past, or running from it, I — I just — I wanna look forward.
       Okay? Not back.

Deacon: This isn't what you think it is. Okay?
Ripper: Get low!
Deacon: Come on — get down —
Ripper: Stay on the Path!

[They duck down to avoid being seen by noisy Rippers nearby.]

Ripper: Find them.

Rikki: A camper? Shit —

Deacon: Why don't ya drag your asses back to Iron Butte and find the shithole
        ya crawled out from —

Rikki: No, no, no, no — Listen to me — we're from Lost Lake — We have a treaty!

Deacon: Little far north — aren't ya? Huh, ya don't wanna get too far away from
        Carlos — do ya? How 'bout we just leave ya here to bleed out, huh? Make
        all the Freaks out here happy, yeah? Huh? Isn't that what ya want? Oh,
        you can all just — go — straight to hell — oh yeah, nice and low down
        there for ya, huh?

[They kill all the Ripper ambushers.]

Deacon: Okay, I think that's the last of 'em.

Rikki: Oh, Jesus. Maybe you're right. I've seen Rippers before, but not like
       that. What the hell are they amped up on?

Deacon: No idea. Back in the day, dealt with a few tweakers who acted like
        that — I think they're on PCP, or whatever that other shit is —

Rikki: Oh, uh — bath salts. Remember? That was becoming a thing before
       everything went down.

Deacon: Right, yeah¹ c'mon, let's — see if they messed up our bikes.

053) IT'S A LONG STORY                                                   [M053]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

Deacon: Really think Iron Mike's treaty with these bastards is gonna hold?
Rikki: I dunno —

       have a run-in? You and Boozer, with — with the Rippers — Before you

Rikki: Okay, we have to follow the lines south. Check the transformers. Make
       sure they're all good.

Deacon: Okay. I'm following you.
Rikki: Hey, I gotta ask you something.
Deacon: Could I stop you?
Rikki: How'd you end up in the MC?
Deacon: It's a long story —
Rikki: We got a long ride.

Deacon: Okay¹ I — I was a member of the 10th Mountain, part of a forward unit
        working with the Northern Alliance —

Rikki: Shit, I didn't know you were in the army. Why were —
Deacon: You wanna hear this or not?
Rikki: Sorry.

Deacon: We were advancing on Mazar-i-Sharif. We got ambushed by a group of
        Taliban heading the other way. And they were in flatbed trucks decked
        out with ZU-23s, modified anti-aircraft guns —

Rikki: Big guns.

Deacon: Yeah. Really big fucking guns. Our Humvee exploded, went over a cliff,
        right into the Hari. You know how hard it is to drown in Afghanistan?
        It's hard. Place is one giant Goddamn desert. Anyway, I was thrown
        clear. And when I came to — the — the Humvee was upside down in the
        river. I swam out to see if anyone survived. I¹ uh — I pulled a body
        back to shore. And I did that seven more times. And by the — by the
        time I pulled in Tanner, my sarge — I was done. And when I came home,
        I dunno — I, um — I bought a bike, spent a couple'a years on the road,
        just moving from place to place, and um —

Rikki: To Farewell? You grew up around here, right?

Deacon: Yeah — yeah. Okay, so by the time I finally settled down, I got a job
        at a bike shop run by this — by this old guy named Jack, and, uh — he
        ran the club — the, uh — well, the Prez, that's what we used to call
        him. He patched me in himself.

Rikki: Wait, Jack — I remember Boozer talking about him. He was in prison or
       something.

Deacon: Some bad shit went down and — and he ended up taking the rap, for the
        club.

Rikki: Sounds like you guys were pretty tight.

[Outside Lost Lake, they find a gas station with a shorted-out transformer.]

Rikki: Oh shit. There had to be one, right?

Deacon: Let's come back in the morning. You can get whatever tools you need
        and — We'll finish it up then. There'll be fewer Freaks out.

Rikki: So, no hot shower tonight? Okay. But I wanna show you something first.

Deacon: No — Rikki, it's been a long day —

Rikki: C'mon, you know a lot about the Freaks. I just wanna show you something
       you might not know. C'mon. We're out here anyway.

Deacon: Shit. Okay.

Rikki: Let's go.

[They start riding.]

Rikki: Can I ask you something?

Deacon: Oh God — like I said before — could I stop you?

Rikki: Why are you still flying colors?

Deacon: I don't know what you mean.

Rikki: I mean — why do you still wear the cuts? You and Boozer? It's — it's not
       like you're trying to recruit anymore, or — or staking out territory.

Deacon: No.

Rikki: A couple of guys I worked with at the plant wore colors on the weekend.
       I asked 'em about it once, an' they said they wore 'em as a way of
       saying "fuck you" to, I don't know, cops, authority, the government? So
       what are you rebelling against?

Deacon: Whatever's left. Look, we wear 'em because we wear 'em. What do you
        want? I mean, no idea about Boozer, but I ain't trying to say shit.
        It's just — the cut — that's who I am. I done a lotta stupid shit in
        my life, but joining the MC, well — let's just say that it's one of the
        few things² I don't regret.

[They drive out to an abandoned lumber mill and hop onto an outbuilding roof.]

Deacon: Rikki, what are we doin' here? I've seen the NERO death trains before,
        and Hordes —

Rikki: I know — not like this.

[A superhorde pours forth from a large factory building.]

Deacon: What the fuck?

Rikki: Watch. I've come here a few times to see them. They stay in those old
       machine buildings and they come out every night — Like someone's ringing
       a dinner bell, right? When it's morning, they go back inside and what,
       hibernate?

Deacon: You mean you never went down there to see?

Rikki: Ha ha — no. One time I got way too close and a dozen of them started
       chasing me. It's like poking a hornet's nest. C'mon, let's get outta
       here — it's getting dark.

[They quietly leave and ride for Lost Lake.]

Deacon: Okay, okay — anyway — the other day — I, uh — I saw something you won't
        believe —

Rikki: Really, you want to talk? Alright¹ let's hear it. Wait, let me guess.
       You saw a NERO helicopter.

Deacon: Wait, uh — how did you know about that?
Rikki: They've been spotted a few times. All over Lost Lake.
Deacon: Shit.

Rikki: Why do you care? It's not like they're here to help us. From the sound
       of it, they shoot on sight.

Deacon: I don't care.
Rikki: Oh. Sounded like you did.

[Around dusk, they finally pull into town.]

Addy: Hey — where the hell have you been all day?
Rikki: Nice to see you too.
Addy: Yeah, well, Skizzo said you and Deacon took off and — I — I was worried.
Rikki: Addy, I'm tired. Okay?
Addy: Oh that's rich.
Rikki: Hey, Deek — thank you.

Deacon: Yeah, well, just let me know when you're ready to tackle that
        transformer. I'll be around.

Rikki: Sure.
Addy: Bullshit.
Rikki: What is your problem?
Addy: No, no — what is your problem?
Rikki: I just said, I'm tired. That's it.

Addy: Okay. I'm sorry. Like I said, I was — I was worried. It's not like you
      to just — take off without talking to me.

Rikki: Okay.
Addy: So that's it?

[Rikki walks away and Addy storms off after her.]

Deacon: That's a day I'm never getting back. Oh, hey, look at that. Too late
        for marsh duty. Yeah, that's too bad, huh¹ Skizzo? Skizzo, Skizzo —
        speaking of Skizzo — I wonder what the hell he did all day?

054) MOMENTS OF LUCIDITY                                                 [M054]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

O'Brian: Yeah — try not to get your ass shot off. Your¹ uh — comm was still

Deacon: Well, it doesn't matter what you call it, I'm the one that's out here

[He creeps into the LZ, puts a bug on the chopper, then spies on a researcher
 investigating inside an abandoned shack.]

Deacon: Here we go —

Lt. Booth: Field Note Two Zero Six Eight — Another subject exhibiting the
           morphology of Stage Two infection. Tendons in the hands and fingers
           are less constricted, fingernails less clawlike, as if recently
           chewed. Additionally, the subject is wearing jewelry and clothing
           less tattered and worn than —

Cpl. Franklin: Hey, sorry. Couldn't help overhearing.
Lt. Booth: Ah, the gun-toting biology major.

Cpl. Franklin: Yeah. Something like that. So it's wearing jewelry — what's the
               significance of that?

Lt. Booth: These things have been out here for two years, scratching and
           clawing at us and each other.

Cpl. Franklin: Yeah?

Lt. Booth: Try putting a gold watch on a baboon for two years, set it loose in
           the wild, and see what happens to it.

Cpl. Franklin: Okay, okay — I get your point.
Lt. Booth: This watch looks new.
Cpl. Franklin: Really? So —

Lt. Booth: So that means this subject has either been taking care of it, or has
           recently —

Cpl. Franklin: — recently put it on — holy shit. I thought they were all, you
               know —

Lt. Booth: Batshit crazy? Yeah, they are. But just as some late stage dementia
           patients could still have moments of lucidity — victims of Stage Two
           virus infection see to retain some level of vestigial memory.

Cpl. Franklin: No shit.
Lt. Booth: No shit. Look at its clothes.
Cpl. Franklin: They're —

Lt. Booth: Almost clean — right? I mean, not clean, but — most Freaks are so
           caked with shit and piss —

Cpl. Franklin: Yeah, it's disgusting.
Lt. Booth: Yeah¹ well, again, put a pair of pants on a baboon for two years —
Cpl. Franklin: Jesus.

Lt. Booth: You ever wonder why there's so many more Freaks in areas where
           people used to live?

Cpl. Franklin: Never thought about it. But yeah, I guess they do —

Lt. Booth: Yeah. We think there might still be something — buried deep in their
           massively deformed heads — that remembers what they once were.

Cpl. Franklin: Jesus — you don't think they're aware of —

Lt. Booth: No, no. We've done the CT scans. They might as well be brain dead —
           in human terms.

Cpl. Franklin: What's that mean?
Lt. Booth: I don't know. That's what we're here to find out.

Deacon: Well, what it means, is that some Freaks get up in the morning, they
        shower, they get dressed, they put on their favorite gold watch, they
        kiss their wife goodbye, then they head out the door for a fun day of
        eating us — and shitting themselves. Why the hell are these guys
        wasting their time with this shit? Hope you got all that, O'Brian.
        Okay, now just gotta get the hell outta here. O'Brian, are you there?
        O'Brian?

O'Brian: Hold on — yeah, I'm here.
Deacon: I planted your tracking device and I got your data.
O'Brian: The researcher. Were they male or female?
Deacon: Wha — what? Why?
O'Brian: Was it a man or a woman?
Deacon: Uh, it was a woman, and no, I didn't catch her name.
O'Brian: Okay. I'll be in touch. O'Brian out.

055) RIDING THE OPEN ROAD                                                [M055]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After visiting the hydroelectric dam, Deacon radios in to Lost Lake.]

Deacon: Hey, Rikki, you there? I'm, uh — I'm gonna be gone for awhile, I'm
        gonna need you to cover me. Skizzo's gonna wonder why I'm not out on
        marsh duty or whatever the hell.

Rikki: Hey¹ Deek — what's up?

Deacon: Boozer's, uh — hell, I don't know. He's — he's depressed or something.
        Talk to Addy. I think I know a way to cheer him up.

Rikki: So, what are you gonna do?

Deacon: I don't know. Uh — I thought I'd maybe head to O'Leary Mountain, get
        his bike, bring it back.

Rikki: That's a long way to go on foot —
Deacon: I'll figure somethin' out. Are — are you gonna cover for me, or what?
Rikki: Yeah.
Deacon: Thanks¹ Rikki. Deacon out.

[Deek returns to the old mountain's safehouse, killing two prowlers nearby.
 He takes Boozer's bike all the way to Lost Lake afterwards.]

Deacon: Hey, I brought you something.
Boozer: Wait, what the fuck? You — you went up and got my bike?
Deacon: Well, I didn't want Cope gettin' it — partin' it out.
Boozer: Jesus, Deek —

Deacon: Hey — I mean, I mostly — did it, you know, in case I need parts — It's
        not like your gimp ass is gonna need 'em —

Boozer: Shit. Thanks, brother. That's the one thing I miss. Ridin' on the open
        road.

[Boozer sits on his hog, but missing an arm, it doesn't feel the same.]

Boozer: Oh fuck —

[Boozer gets off and walks away. Meanwhile, Rikki radios in.]

Rikki: Deek — Addy just wanted me to tell you that she paid some men to go get
       your bike and bring it back. It's over at the mechanic's shop.

Deacon: Uh — wait — what —
Rikki: You're welcome, Deek. Rikki out.

[Later on...]

Copeland: St. John. This is Mark Copeland to Deacon St. John.
Deacon: Hey, Cope — what's up?

Copeland: Just checkin' in. Couple of my men were up to the top of O'Leary
          Mountain the other day, said they found a safe house set up in an
          old Forest Service watch tower —

Deacon: Is that right?

Copeland: Yes¹ sir, that's what I'm told — they said it was abandoned, but —
          funny thing — whoever lived there, left behind a bike — in good shape
          too, by the sound of it —

Deacon: Really?

Copeland: Indeed. But that's not the funny thing — the funny thing —  is they
          went back up there today to pick it up but — the bike was gone. Now
          ain't that a head scratcher?

Deacon: Look, Cope — this is all really fascinating, but, uh —

Copeland: Now hold on — here's the fascinatin' part — they swear that old bike,
          well — it looked a lot like the one Boozer used to ride —

Deacon: Okay — so let me get this straight, Cope. You guys went up to O'Leary
        Mountain, you found — what you thought was Boozer's bike — and the
        first thing ya thought of was, "Hey, why — why don't we just go back
        and steal it?"

Copeland: Salvage, Deek, Salvage. But no, that was my second thought. My first
          was, whatever happened to ol' Boozer? Manny says he hasn't seen him
          around for some time.

Deacon: I don't know, Cope. Next time I see him, I'll let him know how much
        you miss him. St. John out.

056) THE ONLY ONE HE'S GOT                                               [M056]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After retrieving Boozer's bike, Deacon is out riding, when...]

Deacon: Anything wrong?
Addy: No. I — just need to talk to you.
Deacon: Uh — yeah, okay.

[He goes back to the Lost Lake clinic.]

Addy: Hey¹ Deacon, you got a second? How's William? I haven't seen him lately.

Addy: Yeah, well then he's doing better than most.

Addy: Well, losing an arm's a big adjustment, he's giving up the life he had.

057) I GOT WORK TO DO                                                    [M057]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon goes up to Iron Mike's farm later in the morning.]

Deacon: Hey¹ Boozer, how's the¹ uh¹ work going?
Boozer: Scuse¹ me, I ain't got time to fuckin' chit-chat.
Deacon: Alright, don't work too hard.

[Deacon leaves, hearing another truther broadcast afterwards.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. 'Bout a
          month before shit went down, I wrote in my newsletter, Farewell
          Freedom: store a year's worth of food and water, because I knew, no
          matter what was coming, we were all nine meals from anarchy. I
          figured, if I could get a few people prepared — the ones who'd really
          listen — then maybe we'd survive when it all finally collapsed down
          on our heads. But not as many listened as I'd hoped. Now, those
          supplies are runnin' out and folks are goin' hungry. Remember the
          parable of the ant and the grasshopper? Well us "ants," who prepared
          and stored for future calamity, didn't have the heart to starve out
          you "grasshoppers" who danced while the sun was shining without a
          worry in your head for what calamities the future would bring. Now
          we're all paying the price. Are we gonna starve? I don't know. Fish
          runs are thinning out. Game is getting scarce. Can't remember the
          last time I saw a buck or a doe. But I'll tell you this much, we're
          not turning on each other. No sir, we'll never do that. This is Mark
          Copeland for Radio Free Oregon. Don't believe the lies.

Deacon: Goddamn truther bullshit. You know, last I checked, the "grasshoppers"
        all armed themselves to the teeth, came in, and killed all your fucking
        ants, and took everything you owned. So — if you're gonna tell
        parables, Cope. Just — get 'em right.

[Later...]

Deacon: Hey¹ Addy, you there?

Addy: Deacon, yes, I'm here.

Deacon: Hey, so, uh — I — I don't think that — that he's doin' so well. I don't
        know. I guess — I'm really worried about him.

Addy: Yeah, me too — when he stopped by he seemed — I don't know. Angry.
      Depressed.

Deacon: Look, I'll keep an eye on him. I'll — I'm gonna make sure he do
        anything stupid. I'll see what I can do — I don't know —

Addy: You do that, Deacon. It'll mean a lot to him. Infirmary out.

058) SOME KINDA FREAK EXPERT                                             [M058]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After visiting Boozer at the farm, Deek returns to Iron Mike's lodge. Him
 and Skizzo are pouring over a map in the firelight.]

Iron Mike: Okay, that's your best bet. Right there.
Skizzo: I don't know about that, Mike. We lost people in there before.
Iron Mike: We lost — we lost — who? When?

Skizzo: A few weeks back. Torres and Evans. Lookin' for supplies. I told you
        that they —

Iron Mike: No, Goddammit — you didn't.

Skizzo: I told you. That we went after 'em — but the entrance was caved in.
        Their bikes were outside but the place was crawlin'? You remember? I
        don't even know if they made it inside.

Deacon: What's the trouble?
Iron Mike: We just — we're going over the papers, the ones from Sherman's Camp.
Deacon: Mm-hmm.
Iron Mike: There was a mine that was gettin' ready to expand.
Deacon: Sure, and there's probably explosives stored onsite¹.

Iron Mike: Yeah. Except now Skizzo tells me we may have lost two men on the
           inside.

Skizzo: Hey, I never said that, Mike.

Deacon: Well, look — I — give me the map — I'll go get the explosives and I'll
        look for your people inside —

Skizzo: Like hell you will.
Iron Mike: Hey!
Deacon: What the hell is goin' —

Skizzo: You may trust him, Mike, but I don't. Tell me, how much is Tucker
        payin' for a box a' TNT these days, huh?

Iron Mike: You know what, you hold on. He's doin' his part.

Skizzo: Oh really? He's doing what? Besides breakin' the treaty with the
        Rippers, skippin' work, stayin' out with Rikki all day — What's he
        been doin', huh?

Deacon: What you been doing, huh? Sittin' on your ass while everyone does all
        the work?

Skizzo: I keep this camp safe. From Marauders, thieves, and Drifters —

Iron Mike: Alright, you knock it off. Knock it off! Hey, you don't trust him?
           You go with him. But you remember somethin' — both of you —
           Remember — we are all part of the same camp.

Skizzo: That's fine. Fine by me. In the morning, we'll take our bikes and we'll
        go —

Deacon: We'll go right now.
Skizzo: Now.
Deacon: Yeah.
Skizzo: Now. In the middle of the night.
Deacon: Sure. You know it's dark out, there'll be less Freaks inside the mine.

Skizzo: Oh that's right. Oh, since you been skippin' work, you've been chasin'
        down black choppers — And now you're some kinda Freak expert. Is that
        it?

Deacon: You don't need to be a fucking expert to know that the Freaks come out
        at night, Skizzo —

Skizzo: Oh yeah? Okay —
Iron Mike: Okay, come on, enough already.
Skizzo: Okay. Okay. You wanna go now? We'll go now. But I'll hold onto this.

[Skizzo walks out with the mine map.]

Deacon: Jesus Christ.

Iron Mike: Hey, look, he's got his issues just like everybody else does — But
           he does his job.

Deacon: Tell that to Torres and Evans.

Iron Mike: Deek — I guess I'm just making sure he's not gonna have some kinda
           accident down in that mine.

Deacon: Jesus, Mike — who do you think I am?
Iron Mike: I'm still trying to figure that out. See you when you get back.

[Deacon goes outside.]

Deacon: Sonofabitch —

[He meets up with Skizzo at the gate.]

Deacon: Where we goin'?

Skizzo: Lucky Lad, know where it is?

Deacon: Yeah — I'll be waitin' for ya.

Skizzo: Yeah, try to keep up.

[They start racing toward the mine.]

Rikki: Deacon, you there? This is Lost Lake Camp. Over —
Deacon: Yeah¹ Rikki — what's up?
Rikki: I stopped by to see you. Obviously you're not there.

Deacon: Skizzo and I are on a run for Iron Mike — I'll be back by morning.
        What's up?

Rikki: I just wanted to see when we could get out — fix that transformer —
Deacon: That hot shower still calling your name?
Rikki: Somethin' like that.
Deacon: We'll be back by morning. Talk then. Deacon out.

[If Deacon loses the race:]

Skizzo: Thought you were gonna be waitin' for me?
Deacon: I got sidetracked.

[If Deacon wins the race:]

Deacon: What took you so long?
Skizzo: Whatever, brother. Let's get this done.
