059) LINES NOT CROSSED                                                   [M059]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[They enter the compound and see wrecked bikes.]

Deacon: So these belonged to Mike's men?

Skizzo: My men, but yeah. Torres and Evans. They weren't Drifters, but they'd
        been out in the shit a few times. I thought they could handle it.

Deacon: I guess you were wrong.
Skizzo: Shit's already been parted out. Goddamn scavengers everywhere.

Deacon: Skizzo, why wouldn't you bring their shit back with you when you were
        out here looking for 'em.

Skizzo: Because there were too many Freaks, that's why.

[Newts make noise on the roof.]

Skizzo: Like them. Only a lot more. C'mon. Now Mike said the explosives are
        kept locked in strong boxes¹. Should be a set of spare keys somewhere
        inside the office. Fuckin' Newts —  God, I hate those little suckers.

Deacon: We finally agree on something.
Skizzo: Hey, over here. I think I can boost you onto this roof. Ready?
Deacon: Yeah —
Skizzo: Up you go —
Deacon: Got it —

[He enters a second-story window and finds the foreman's spare keys.]

Deacon: There — Skizzo, I got 'em.
Skizzo: Great, great. Look around. See if you can find some flares.
Deacon: Wait a second, you didn't bring a flashlight?

Skizzo: Yeah. But the batteries are dead. Shit's getting hard to find these
        days. At least ones that have any juice left.

Deacon: Flares — Skizzo, I found a box of flares.

Skizzo: Yeah, yeah, see if you can force open the door. I'll come in and grab
        'em.

[He unlocks the front door.]

Deacon: Flares are over here.
Skizzo: Yeah — gimme the keys.
Deacon: What you mean, like these keys?
Skizzo: Yeah, hand 'em over —

Deacon: Hey, hey, hey. I got an idea. How about you lead us to the strong
        boxes¹, I'll unlock 'em. You got a problem with that?

Skizzo: No problem. Just don't lose 'em. Okay?
Deacon: Yeah. I'm gonna keep that in mind.
Skizzo: I got 'em. Let's head in.
Deacon: Right behind you.

[They go to the caved-in mine entrance.]

Skizzo: See? It's just like I said.

Deacon: Looks like we should be able to squeeze in through here. Give me a
        hand. Here — push —

Skizzo: I'm pushin', I'm pushin' —
Deacon: There — wedge it against that boulder —
Skizzo: Got it —
Deacon: There —

[The fallen beam is placed horizontally again.]

Skizzo: Look stable to you?
Deacon: Stable enough —

[They enter the mine and Skizzo pops a flare.]

Deacon: Remember, keep your gun holstered.
Skizzo: I thought you said it was gonna be clear.

Deacon: I never said that — and I mean it. If there are any Freaks in here,
        one shot will bring 'em right down on our heads.

Skizzo: I heard ya already. Jesus. Okay, first expansion area is right off
        the main shaft. C'mon, this way.

Deacon: Right behind you.
Skizzo: Ah shit. We're not gettin' under that.
Deacon: Look at the map. Is there another tunnel? A ventilation shaft?

Skizzo: Map shows they started a connecting tunnel here. Looks like it was
        unstable, so they boarded it up.

Deacon: Where?

Skizzo: Eh, back this way.

Deacon: Here?

Skizzo: Yeah.

Deacon: Yeah, looks like they boarded it up. Well, this doesn't look exactly
        stable.

Skizzo: I thought I already said that — all I got is this. You got the
        flashlight. You have the honors.

[Deacon kicks down the "do not cross" barrier for the connecting tunnel.]

Deacon: Maybe there's a reason they never completed any of this expansion work.
        I mean it seems like one stick of dynamite will bring this whole place
        down on our heads.

Skizzo: Doesn't seem so bad.

[No sooner have they crossed the path than a tunnel-sealing cave-in occurs.]

Skizzo: Go, go! Look out!
Deacon: Jesus. You alright?
Skizzo: No broken bones. Jesus — yeah.
Deacon: Oh — that was close.
Skizzo: Well, we're committed to this shit now. C'mon. This way.
Deacon: What're you doin'?
Skizzo: What's it look like? I'm droppin' flares.
Deacon: Why? You got the map.

Skizzo: This thing's a fucking maze? Gonna need help knowing which tunnels
        we've checked.

[Deacon draws his attention to a pair of corpses in a shadowed corner.]

Deacon: C'mere —
Skizzo: What?
Deacon: These your men?

Skizzo: Yeah. Every time I saw Torres, he had on this same damned vest. I kept
        tellin' him, wearin' bright orange's gonna get you killed, bro. I guess
        it didn't matter in here.

Deacon: His buddy lost the arm. Bled out and — kept Torres fed for a week.
Skizzo: You ever resort to that?
Deacon: There's a few lines I haven't crossed. That's one of 'em.
Skizzo: Yeah. Me either. Stand back. I'm not leavin' 'em for the Freaks.

[He tosses a molotov on the corpses.]

Deacon: Let's get the hell outta here.
Skizzo: Yeah. Come on, we can squeeze through here.
Deacon: Following you.
Skizzo: That's a tight squeeze — you got this?
Deacon: Who sits on his ass all day in the camp?
Skizzo: Oh, very funny — c'mon.

[They move through a rock fissure into another part of the tunnel.]

Skizzo: Okay — the first expansion area should be around this corner.
Deacon: If you're readin' the map right.
Skizzo: I'm readin' it right. See? You still got the keys?
Deacon: Yeah, right here.

[He unlocks the strongbox. Skizzo checks it afterwards.]

Deacon: Nothing. It's empty.
Skizzo: Shit.
Deacon: Oh, I'm sorry. Did you not believe me?
Skizzo: Sure. I believed you. Come on. Maybe they put 'em all in one place.
Deacon: Sonofabitch.

Skizzo: Let's go check the other one. This way. Let's double back. Make sure
        we didn't miss any side tunnels.

Deacon: Skizzo, hold up, hold up. This doesn't seem right.
Skizzo: What — what're you talking about?
Deacon: This isn't the way we came in.
Skizzo: What, you think these flares got up and moved themselves?
Deacon: Maybe I got turned around.

[They continue on.]

Deacon: Now, wait a minute Goddammit. This is the main tunnel.
Skizzo: What?

Deacon: It's the — it's the main tunnel. You see the tracks? We weren't
        following any tracks on our way in.

Skizzo: What the hell? But these are my flares, dammit. How did they — Oh,
        someone's fucking with us. C'mon, this way.

[They follow the flares into a larger chamber. Skizzo waves his piece around.]

Deacon: Hold up, hold up, wait a second —
Skizzo: Who the hell's in here? Come on out! Show yourself!
Deacon: Skizzo — put that thing away.
Skizzo: What're you talkin' about?

Deacon: What I'm talking about is one shot — one — That's all it takes to bring
        all the Freaks in these tunnels down on top of us.

Skizzo: I thought you said these tunnels would be clear this time of night.
Deacon: No, what I said —

[A newt jumps on top of Deacon, taking him unawares.]

Skizzo: What the hell! Look out! I can't get a shot —
Deacon: Oh Goddammit. Goddammit¹ it's got the keys!
Skizzo: Oh — shit! Where you goin'?
Deacon: It's got the keys! We gotta catch it.
Skizzo: Wait — come back —
Deacon: Goddammit Skizzo — it's gettin' away!

[Deacon tracks and chases the Newt, leaving Skizzo alone in the chamber.]

Deacon: Dammit¹ you little shit — get back here. C'mon, you shit. Gimme back
        those fuckin' keys. Where'd you go —

[Deacon kills the Newt and reclaims the keys. He can hear gunfire further in
 and runs to help Skizzo as he's attacked by Freakers.]

Skizzo: Goddammit. Get off me.
Deacon: Dammit, Skizzo!
Skizzo: No — no!
Deacon: What the hell was he thinking — Oh, Skizzo! Skizzo — stop shooting!
Skizzo: What?
Deacon: Dammit¹ Skizzo, you're bringing the whole mine down on us —
Skizzo: Ah dammit — okay, okay —
Deacon: Put the gun down —
Skizzo: What the hell are you talkin' about?

[They finally kill all the attackers.]

Deacon: Looks like the last of 'em —
Skizzo: So much for the tunnels bein' clear —
Deacon: I told you what would happen if you fired your weapon.
Skizzo: What was I supposed to do? Throw rocks at 'em?
Deacon: What you're supposed to do, is you're supposed to fuckin' listen to me
        — Next time — Try this.

Skizzo: Whatever.
Deacon: You're welcome.
Skizzo: For what?
Deacon: For savin' your ass.
Skizzo: If you hadn't run off, my ass wouldn't need saving.
Deacon: Well, you ready to fucking finish this?
Skizzo: Yeah, I'm ready. This way.

[They continue on past the Freaker ambush area.]

061) THAT'S HIS MISTAKE                                                  [M061]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[With some effort, they use a mine cart to get the TNT to the entrance.]

Deacon: What're you talkin' about?

[Later...]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. Today I want
          to talk about drugs. Now, I don't much care for 'em. They keep you
          numb, unreliable, and silent. In 1996, the CIA was accused of dealing
          cocaine in Central America. Used it to help them control the masses,

          they figured out how well that shit worked, well — they decided to
          set their sights here at home — make drug addicts of us good old
          American taxpayers. They brought cocaine up from South American by
          the planeload, barrels of the stuff, got us hooked on it, kept us

          very heart and soul of this good country. But thankfully, at last,
          all that is in the past. At least for my people. Stay sober¹ people.
          Stay alive. This is Mark Copeland for Radio Free Oregon. Don't
          believe the lies.

Deacon: Yeah? You ever lose an arm, Cope? Maybe when you do you'll find
        yourself wanting a bottle of whiskey — or two — or three. In the
        meantime, shut the hell up.

062) DRINKING HIMSELF TO DEATH                                           [M062]
_______________________________________________________________________________

[On his way back to town after the TNT run:]

Guard: Who? No, there's no one here. The work crew's gone home for the day.

065) YOU TWISTED MY ARM                                                  [M065]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[While walking around Lost Lake, Deacon gets a call.]

O'Brian: St. John. You there? It's O'Brian.

Deacon: Hold on. O'Brian, I'm sick of doing your dirty work. You got news for
        me or not?

O'Brian: Yeah. I — I mean — yes. I have news.
Deacon: Well then, what is it?
O'Brian: I — need you to do one last job.
Deacon: Were you listenin' to what I was just sayin'? I'm done with this.

O'Brian: Her middle name. It was "Irene," right? Sarah Irene Whitaker. It's on

O'Brian: One — last job. I sent you the coordinates. O'Brian out.

[He hurriedly walks to his bike, passing by Boozer.]

Boozer: Mm-hmm —

Boozer: Yeah — okay.

Boozer: Not bad. Uh, it's been worse, you know? I actually don't mind workin'

Deacon: Yeah.

 chopper soon arrives.]

Deacon: Okay. Stay close.

Boozer: Yeah.

           us rebuild. Now for the past coupla months, Rikki has been doin'
           just that. But she can't do it alone. She needs help. Tonight is
           gonna happen because we welcomed a Drifter into our camp. And we
           allowed him to earn our trust. Tonight we take one more step out of
           the darkness.

[Rikki flips the breaker and the town lights come on. She and Mike hug.]

Iron Mike: C'mere. C'mere. Thank you! Thank you! Oh my God! Hey, hey! Hey¹ you
           two, I gotta — I gotta — I got a bottle a' bourbon inside. C'mon,
           you wanna — c'mon with!

Deacon: That was my wife, yeah.

Deacon: Well there is.
Rikki: What?
Deacon: Stop talkin' about it.
Rikki: Okay.

[The clinic seems deserted.]

Deacon: I don't think she's here.

Rikki: Addy, you here? Okay, well — strip.

Deacon: Strip — strip what?

Rikki: Take your shirt off, sit on the table.

Deacon: Hey, look, it's nothin'.

        switches and circuits or whatever the hell you were doin'.

Deacon: Ah Jesus! okay¹ —

Rikki: Really?

Rikki: Just — shh. Hang on. There, it's done. Big baby.

Deacon: See, I told you it was nothin'.

Rikki: Yeah, you did.

[They just stare at each other, sharing a moment, before looking away.]

Rikki: Oh wow. You really have been at war.

Deacon: Yeah, more than one.

Rikki: Shit, that's right? Where was this one? Afghanistan or the MC? Or after?

Deacon: I, uh, I — I don't remember.

Rikki: What about this one?

Deacon: Rikki, uh. I'm not sure that, um — Well, I hear that Addy doesn't
        really like, um — People messing around in her business.

Rikki: Yeah, I — I heard that too. What about this one?

Deacon: Rikki.

[Skizzo can be seen eavesdropping on their convo, then leaving.]

       see Addy, and she's gonna tell you how great of a job I did.

Deacon: Rikki, um —

Rikki: Deek, it's — it's — it's fine. You're welcome. Hey, Deacon? Maybe one
       day, stop and light a candle. It can get pretty dark and cold out there.

Carlos: C'mon! Oh yeah. One down. And what? About a dozen to go. Maybe more?
        What are the odds? The three of us? You, me, Boozer, still alive.
        Brought together, here, at the end of the world?

Deacon: The fuck have you done to Boozer?
Carlos: Oh, he's not here yet. But he will be. Soon enough.

[He knocks out Deacon with a punch and leaves. Later, Lisa enters the room.]

Lisa: It is you. I saw them bring you in.
Deacon: Lisa?

Lisa: No. That is not my name. I'm on the Path. I don't have a name anymore.
      None of us do. Everyone I ever cared about — is dead.

Deacon: Lisa. Listen to me —
Lisa: Do you know why we want to be like them? Like the Freaks?
Deacon: No.

[She raises her knife —— and cuts the rope binding his arm.]

Lisa: It's because they don't remember what they've lost. Who — they've lost.

[She tosses the knife near his feet and leaves. Deacon frees himself and then
 does the same, leading right into the Rippers' temple.]

Deacon: Lisa? Lisa? She's gone — I can't let them see me — If they see me,
        they're gonna bring the whole place down on my head —

[He sneaks around, murdering Rippers he finds as quietly as possible.]

Deacon: I'll enlighten you — Oh, give me a chance — I'll help you find the
        Path — One Mind, yeah — right — Find out where they're keepin' my
        shit — Get my gear — Bonfire — where the hell is the Bonfire — It's a
        bonfire — it can't be hard to miss — How the hell am I gonna get outta
        here? There it is — now where's my shit? This is it — this has gotta
        be it —

[Deek creeps into a house near the town gate. He takes a Ripper playing with
 his hat completely by surprise, then starts collecting his weapons/gear.]

Deacon: I'll take that. Got a question for you — what's the deal? Huh? You
        just drag people in here, fuck with 'em, steal their shit — And then
        what, take it all and throw it in the bonfire out there? Is that the
        idea? Jesus Christ. Oh, hello. Yeah. Got another question for you.
        Where's my cut?

Ripper: What?

Deacon: My cut — my leather jacket — my fucking leather jacket. Who took it?

Ripper: Don't know.

Deacon: Okay —

Ripper: Wait, wait, wait! He just left! He just took it and left, not long ago!
        Join us, brother.

[Deacon slits his throat and examines tracks in the room.]

Deacon: He just left — These are fresh — There he is —

[He enters a building with the cut-wearing thief and puts a gun to his head.]

Deacon: Hey. Do me a favor. Take that shit off.

Ripper: We will cut away your soul!

[When the cut is off, Deek slashes his throat with a machete.]

Deacon: Thanks. Get low, asshole.

Boozer: Look, I got this. I'm not much good in a firefight, but I can plant
        these charges.

Deacon: I've set demo charges before, Boozer — In Afghanistan. I know exactly
        where to put 'em.

Boozer: Good. Tell me where to go when I'm down there. We doin' this?
Deacon: Yeah.
Boozer: Alright.

Deacon: Okay, I'm gonna be up in this tower, should give me a good view of the
        entire dam.

Boozer: I'll wait here until you get up there. Alright. You ready? I'm headin'
        in.

Deacon: Yeah. Stay low, move fast.

Boozer: You got it, brother.

Deacon: Boozer — never mind. Go, go!

[With Deacon sniping, Boozer heads atop the dam.]

Boozer: Where — where do I set the first charge?
Deacon: You see the second set of scaffolding? On top of the dam?

Boozer: Yeah, I see it, headin' over — Alright — I'm settin' the first charge —
        Done — Alright, I'm movin' on to the next one —

Deacon: Nice job, Boozeman — keep going —

Boozer: You got this? You gotta keep 'em off me¹ bro, or this whole thing's
        goin' up, and me with it —

Deacon: Hey, I got this — you just get the charges planted.
Boozer: And I'm — setting the second charge — Got it —

[As Boozer descends, more Rippers ride in.]

Boozer: Kinda busy here — you got 'em?
Deacon: Yeah, yeah —
Boozer: Huh — a few less Rippers — nice work —
Deacon: Keep — goin', Boozer — c'mon — c'mon —
Boozer: Deek? Deek — more Rippers —
Deacon: I see 'em —
Boozer: Where do I set the next charge?
Deacon: Rikki called it the penstock, the big pipe, at the base of the dam.
Boozer: Okay — headin' there now — Alright — third charge — In position —
Deacon: Just — move your ass —
Boozer: Okay, you try doin' this with one hand and a blade —
Deacon: Hey, c'mon¹ man, sometimes I wish I had a blade hand —
Boozer: Okay, I got it — Get 'em off me —
Deacon: I got this¹, Boozer —
Boozer: You fall asleep there? What's goin' on¹ brother —
Deacon: Okay, okay.
Boozer: Fourth charge — Alright — that's the last of 'em —
Deacon: Run! Boozer —
Boozer: I'm goin' as fast as I can —
Deacon: Come on! Come on!

[The charges go off, sending the entire lake into the Iron Butte valley. The
 Ripper compound on the golf course is mostly destroyed in the wake.]

Boozer: Holy shit.
Deacon: Are you okay?
Boozer: Yeah. Yeah, I think so. Unless, wait a minute, was this already —

[He comically points to his missing arm, causing both men to laugh.]

Deacon: Well that never gets old, does it? Let's, uh — Let's go find Jessie.
Boozer: Yeah.

[They ride for the golf course.]

Deacon: Brother, you, uh — you did a helluva job back there.
Boozer: Yeah? I thought I was done for a coupla times —
Deacon: Yeah, I'm sorry about that —

Boozer: What the hell you talkin' about? This is the most alive I've felt since
        — oh, shit — you remember when we got trapped by that Horde in Tumalo?

Deacon: We ain't done yet —
Boozer: How many you think we killed?
Deacon: I dunno — I mean, they had it comin', right?
Boozer: Yeah, they had it comin' — guess we all do.

085) TIME FOR SOME PAYBACK                                               [M085]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[They arrive at the golf course.]

        This is on Jessie. He wants some payback? I'll show him some fuckin'

Boozer: Come on, that's the last of 'em.

Deacon: These guys seem more jacked up than usual?

Boozer: Hell yeah — they musta snorted up the rest of whatever the hell drug
        they take —

[After gunning through the remaining Rippers, they enter the temple. Atop a
 broken stairwell, they can hear Carlos' ravings.]

Deacon: Yeah, there's no way you're gettin' up there.

Boozer: Yeah. Dammit. Here. Hell. I'll boost you up.

Deacon: Okay, listen. If something happens to me, there's a trail not far from
        here. You got —

Boozer: No, no, no, no, no, listen — That is not "Carlos" up there, okay? Not
        this "Founder of Rest in Peace," it's fuckin' Jessie Williamson.
        Fuckin' low-life piece a' shit scumbag who got what was comin' to him.
        Alright? Now you fuckin' go up there, and you kill that son of a bitch.

086) I'M GOOD WITH THAT                                                  [M086]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Boozer boosts Deacon upstairs. Deacon tries maintaining stealth, but he's
 soon blindsided by Carlos, who knocks him down and blows drugs in his face.
 Carlos rips away his guns in the meantime.]

Boozer: Deek! What's goin' on, dammit! Deek! Talk to me!
Carlos: Time to get low¹ brother! Time to get low!
Boozer: Dammit, Deek!

[They start having a melee fight. Sometimes Boozer interrupts with a taunt
 from where he stands in the ground floor.]

Carlos: Deacon St. John — brought low by the lowly Jessie Williamson — brought
        low — Do you remember back in the day? You and Boozer held me down
        while Jack burned the flesh from my back — Those — those memories —

        lose ourselves! We will all — become Free — I will help you find the

        you're a Goddamn wimp now —
Carlos: Oh yeah — and then I will help Boozer — Oh — and then I will forget —
        I will become one of the Found! I will finally Rest — In — Peace!

[Deacon's knife wins out over Carlos' machete. He puts Carlos in a hold and
 stabs him in the back.]

Carlos: I see it. I see it.
Boozer: Deek! What's goin' on, dammit!
Carlos: The Path is — clear to me now.
Boozer: Deek! Talk to me!
Deacon: Yeah, me too.

[He slits the psycho's throat.]

Deacon: Rest in peace, Jessie.

[Later, the bikers walk through flood wreckage back to their bike.]

Boozer: It's done?
Deacon: Yeah, it's done. And I couldn't have done it alone.

Boozer: It was good bein' out in the shit again, y'know? But I gotta say,
        shovelin' shit, pullin' weeds — Well maybe it isn't such a bad way to
        spend the day.

Deacon: Yeah.

Boozer: Well, with Jessie gone, how many you think are left? People that we
        knew from before, I mean.

Deacon: No one. Boozer, there's no one left.
Boozer: Shit. I'm sorry, man.
Deacon: Yeah. Me too. C'mon. Let's get the fuck outta here.
Boozer: Yeah. Yeah.

[Back at Lost Lake, Deek finds Mike in the Ripper-defaced chapel.]

Iron Mike: Well, like I said, I — I know we haven't talked in a few years. I —
           guess I just figured with my Elizabeth bein' there with you an' all,
           there probably — Wasn't much point in me yammerin' away at you. Oh,
           and then — what, with all hell breaking loose, I — I thought maybe
           you weren't there, or you just didn't give a shit, pardon my
           language. I guess that's why I'm here. To say I still don't know.
           I hope you're there. I hope there's — some reason for all this shit
           we're livin' through. That's all. We'll — we'll — we'll talk again
           some other time. Oh, um — amen.

[He notices Deacon nearby.]

Iron Mike: Deek.
Deacon: Uh, yeah — Rikki told me that I could find you here.

Iron Mike: Nah, it's just these knees a' mine, y'know. It's — reason I haven't
           been prayin' all these years. Yeah, I'm not a — I'm not a
           churchgoin' type, even after livin' through that shitstorm in
           Sherman's Camp. But now, after all this, I just thought, hell, I —
           maybe now it's the time.

Deacon: I, uh — I didn't have a choice, Mike.
Iron Mike: Oh, everybody's got a choice — Deek — until they're dead.
Deacon: It's either us or them.

Iron Mike: It's always us or them. Always. You know the reason we're goin' to
           hell —  Is we can't figure out that "us" is every Goddamned soul
           that ain't walkin' around in shit-stained pants tryin' to eat us.

Deacon: Alright, you know what? You may not like it, but the world is what it
        is. Yeah, it is. Prayin' ain't gonna change that. Wishin' that it was
        something else ain't gonna make it that way, Mike.

Iron Mike: Wishin' ain't got anything to do with it. We make the world what it
           is, by what we do. All of us.

[Deacon rolls his eyes and starts leaving.]

Iron Mike: I let him go. Skizzo. Ain't no way he was gettin' a fair trial.
Deacon: You let him go.
Iron Mike: Told him to ride out. Not come back.
Deacon: Jesus Christ, Mike, do you have any idea what the fuck you've done?

Iron Mike: Yeah. I stopped another killing. And you know what? I guess I'm
           good with that.

[Later, Deacon is riding around when...]

Deacon: Boozer? Boozeman — you're not gonna believe this shit.
Boozer: Deek — what's wrong?
Deacon: Iron Mike — just let him go.
Boozer: Wait, let who go?

Deacon: Skizzo. He just — let him go. He just let him ride outta here without
        a Goddamn care in the world. Did you hear what I just said?

Boozer: Yeah, Deek. I heard ya, but — Jessie — all those Rippers — maybe —
        dunno, maybe I've seen enough killin' — you know? Like I said, bein' a
        farmer — ain't so bad. Deek?

Deacon: Yeah, okay. Boozeman. You're the — second one to tell me that. I gotta
        go. Deacon out.

[Sometime after, truther drivel takes over the airwaves.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. Let me tell
          you — before this shit? We were numb and we were dumb. We were
          blindly taking in opiates of all kinds, keeping us sedated like fat,
          happy cows: candy, television, booze, heroin. And it worked. But now,
          well — We're feelin' the pain, all of it. Every cut. We are wide
          awake and we are watching. You see the truth of what I've been saying
          since the beginning. No one can get anything past us. We're the ones
          running the show now, and we're doing a damn sight better than the
          Feds ever did. Take a deep breath and hold it in. You're free men.
          No one can take that away from you again. This is Mark Copeland for
          Radio Free Oregon. Don't believe the lies.

Deacon: Yeah — Cope — I'm feelin' the pain — who fucking isn't? Well, fucking
        Jessie "Carlos" Williamson. Rest in peace.

[Flashback: Deacon pulls to Cloverfield's front gate.]

Jim: Hey, hey, hey! What're you doing? You can't park here.

Jim: This is private property¹, now turn around and get the hell outta here.
     Come on.

     asshole, this is a restricted area. I told you, get the hell outta here!

Sarah: Over to the dam. That's a nice quiet road, right?

        State — visit Jack.

Deacon: Oh my God. No, no, no, listen, listen, listen, you did great, you did

Sarah: Yeah. I mean, no, but yeah, I will. Okay.
Deacon: Thank you for saving my life.
Sarah: Well, you know. I do what I can.
Deacon: Hey, hey, the clutch, the clutch!
Sarah: I know what the clutch is!
Deacon: Okay, no, no the —
Sarah: Deacon!

[They recover and get back on the road.]

Deacon: So, uh — do you think your parents are gonna come?
Sarah: To the wedding? I don't know.
Deacon: I mean, you know, I thought if I stepped back from the MC that¹ uh —
Sarah: I don't think it's gonna matter to them, Deacon.
Deacon: But you're gonna — you're gonna at least tell 'em —

Sarah: Yeah, if you want me to. Look, it's just — I'm not gonna change who I
       am — and who you are — to make my uptight, middle-class parents happy.

Deacon: Okay. Look out.

[A squad car races by them, sirens blaring.]

Sarah: I see them.

Sarah: Oh, shit.

[They arrive back at Cloverfield. The squad car ahead is let through the gate.]

Jim: Ms. Whitaker's returned.

Jim: Ms. Whitaker —
Sarah: Yeah —

Jim: Okay.
Sarah: I gotta go.
Deacon: Hey, hey —
Sarah: Sorry —

[She kisses him goodbye.]

Sarah: It's fine, it's probably just a fire alarm or something small.
Deacon: Okay. Knock 'em dead.
Sarah: Love you. Um, just call me later.

[Deacon sees Jim glowering at him, so Deek flips him off. The flashback ends.]

Rikki: Look, Addy, I'm sorry.
Addy: Whatever.
Rikki: Addy —
Addy: Whatever¹ Rikki!
Rikki: I'm sorry. Goddamn.

[The girls storm off. Deacon suddenly has an epiphany.]

Deacon: Clearance. clearance¹! Uh, O'Brian, this is St. John, come back.
        O'Brian, this is St. — just answer your Goddamn radio!

O'Brian: St. John. Didn't think I'd hear from you again.

Deacon: Yeah, neither did I. Alright, listen — That night you bugged out, you
        told me that you didn't take any civilians, you just took, uh — NERO
        personnel, Feds, people with clearance.

O'Brian: I told you, there was nothing I could do, we didn't —

Deacon: Shut up, shut up, shut up, listen to me. Sarah, my wife, she had
        clearance. She had her ID badge with her the night that I put her on
        your chopper.

O'Brian: I don't think that they —

Deacon: So — Just do me a favor, look it up. Sarah Irene Whitaker. She worked
        at Cloverdale. She had federal clearance. She was doing, uh, I don't
        know, research, pharmaceutical — I don't know what she — the hell she
        was doin'. Just do me —

O'Brian: Okay. okay¹! I'll see what I can find.
Deacon: Okay, great. O'Brian, remember, you owe me.
O'Brian: Yeah, yeah. O'Brian out.

088) WHY AM I HERE?                                                      [M088]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[A while after Deacon contacts O'Brian, he hears back.]

        she — is she alive or isn't she?

O'Brian: I — have something to give you.

[Deek visits the mountain valley where O'Brian's chopper has already landed.]

         with what's goin' on.

Deacon: So why am I here?

         level.

Deacon: Clearance level —

O'Brian: No.
Deacon: No? Well, you got a ride. we're¹ all friends now.

Deacon: What?
O'Brian: Year ago — a local Militia group.
Deacon: Militia group? Where's their camp?
O'Brian: We don't know.

Deacon: How the hell can you not know? You got a helicopter, you got satellites
        —

O'Brian: Somewhere around Crater Lake. But it's a no-fly zone, okay? They got
         outposts, rockets, RPGs —

Deacon: Crater Lake.

O'Brian: Crater Lake. Look, I wanted to tell you about the work we're doing?
         Studying the infected — the Freaks? They're evolving. As bad as things
         are right now — They're gonna get worse. A lot worse.

[O'Brian climbs into the helo and it flies off.]

Deacon: Ah — go to hell, O'Brian. I don't — give a shit about any of that —
        Boozer — Boozerman, come back.

Boozer: Yeah, Deek.

Deacon: Hey, listen — listen to me, uh — a year ago, we were with Iron Mike,
        we were thinking about riding south, but the Santiam Pass was blocked
        — there was no way through — and he said that he knew another way —

Boozer: Deek — Iron Mike — he's — he's not too happy with us right now —
Deacon: Just listen to me — just listen to me — do you remember what he said?

Boozer: Iron Mike? Yeah — he was — braggin' about knowin' every goat trail in
        a hundred miles — said there was, uh — a trail that went around Mt.
        Thielsen? Mt. — Thielsen — I dunno, somethin' —

Deacon: Thielsen — Thielsen — yeah, that's it. The Thielsen Pass —

Boozer: Yeah. Well, why the hell're you — wait — NERO — shit. You've — you've
        talked to — she's alive? Sarah's alive? Deek?

Deacon: Okay, listen to me — O'Brian — they, uh — Boozer, he found her ID
        badge — yeah, Boozer, uh — I — I think that she's alive.

Boozer: Deek — well, you never lost hope. You always knew — you never gave up.
        So what're ya gonna do?

Deacon: I don't know, Boozer — I don't know. Uh — but — God, if there's even a

Boozer: Goddamn right. Um — shit — I — I gotta go. Uh — Rikki and Addy need —
        need help puttin' up a — shelf or some Goddamn thing. Look, I — I'll
        see you when you get back to camp. Boozer out.

Deacon: Okay, okay — see ya, Boozeman.

[A while afterwards, Rikki calls in.]

Rikki: Deacon — where are you?
Deacon: Hey¹ Rikki. Uh — I — I got some shit I gotta take care of —
Rikki: Are you coming back?
Deacon: Am I coming back? What — what do you — what do you mean?
Rikki: Boozer told us —
Deacon: Boozer told you — okay¹ look, there's nothing to tell.
Rikki: There's no way over the Santiam Pass, you know that.

Deacon: Yes, yes, I'm coming back. Listen, like I said — I got some shit to
        do. Deacon out.

[More truther jank plays after Rikki signs off.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. It has come
          to my attention that some of you are out there working with NERO. The
          very same NERO we saw cut down a group of survivors not long ago. The
          same NERO that abandoned us here in the shit two years past. Some
          would call these people fools, but I got a better name for 'em:
          traitors. And I assure you, I don't take treason lightly. But, I am
          a reasonable man, so you get one warning. Listen up! Stop what you're
          doin'. Now. Before we find you. 'Cause we will. And when we do, you
          will pay. I'll personally string you up on the biggest tree I find.
          And while you're breathing you're last, we'll quarter you and feed
          you to the Freaks you love. That is a promise. This is Mark Copeland
          for Radio Free Oregon. Don't believe the lies.

Deacon: Yeah, well — Cope — I gotta say, I don't like it any more than you. Do
        your worst.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
089) RIDING NOMAD AGAIN                                                  [M089]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deek rides back into town after meeting O'Brian.]

Deacon: Alright — let's see what the old man's got to say —

[Deacon goes up to speak with Iron Mike.]

Deacon: You know a way over the Thielsen Pass. You told me once that, uh —
Iron Mike: I told you nothin'. Go on! I can't help you, Deek.
Deacon: Oh c'mon. Just draw me a Goddamn map?
Iron Mike: After everything you've done?

Deacon: After everything that I've — What about what you've done, old man? Huh?
        Sherman's Camp —

Iron Mike: You go on —
Deacon: The things that you did —
Iron Mike: — you get out of here! You leave me be!

Deacon: — hey, no, listen to me, listen to me, listen to me — What if you could
        take it all back, huh? What if you could fix it.¹ That night I put
        Sarah on the chopper, I felt relieved. How fucked up is that? Huh? I
        was relieved, Mike. That's what I've been livin' with.

Iron Mike: And now you're chasin' ghosts. You think findin' your ol' lady — if
           she's alive — You think that's gonna fix it? Make you whole?

Deacon: I don't know, but I gotta try.

Iron Mike: Alright. If I do this — what you want, show you the way over the
           pass — You don't come back. Alright? You promise me — You don't
           come back.

Deacon: I gotcha.

[Mike walks off.]

Deacon: Oh, shit — now I gotta — talk to Boozer —

[He walks outside the lodge and hears two NPCs talking.]

Carl: It sounds like there's some kind of militia down there, they're takin'
      the fight to the Goddamn Freakers. While we're up here pissin' our pants
      about a buncha Rippers.

JT: Okay, so whaddya wanna do? Go down there? What's blockin' the road, snow
    and ice? We — we just wait for it to thaw.

Carl: There's a bunch of abandoned cars, would take forever to get past. No,
      no, no. That's the least of our worries. There's a Horde. The biggest
      one you ever saw. There must be over a thousand.

JT: Are you shittin' me?

Carl: It's down there, right off the road to the south. I saw it on my way
      back.

JT: Jesus — what the hell you doin' runnin' off where there's a Horde? And you
    don't even tell me?

Carl: I didn't know it was there. Makes you wonder why no one else told us
      shit.

[Deek goes over to his and Boozer's cabin.]

Boozer: Holy shit.
Deacon: Boozer, I — I —

Boozer: Last winter. We're up on Farewell Ridge. We're watchin' the Freaks.
        Thousands — thousands of 'em. I mean, too many to count.

Deacon: Yeah, I remember.

Boozer: All I could think was every one of us, man, woman, and child, are now
        homeless. Buncha Goddamn refugees. Yeah. The world belongs to them now.

Deacon: We'll survive.

Boozer: Yeah, we been doin' that all right. Survivin'. Isn't livin'. Somethin'
        Jack used to say — "Doesn't matter when you hit the road, where you're
        headin' out to — But you damn well better know where you're comin' home
        to."

Deacon: You know, we never talked about it. Why we still wore the colors — All
        this time out in the Freakshow, when shit like this didn't matter
        anymore.

Boozer: Yeah. Habit, I think. Last two Mongrels on earth. Farewell originals.
Deacon: The biker boys — most badass Drifters on the broken road.
Boozer: Damn straight.
Deacon: Yeah, I guess we did become a sort of a brand.
Boozer: We were a lotta things, but we were never a brand.

Deacon: When we rode outta Farewell — Without Sarah, without Jack, or anyone —
        I know that we were — leaving everything behind. Everything that
        mattered was gone. Except this.

[Deacon hands over his cut to Boozer.]

Boozer: You ridin' NOMAD again, huh?
Deacon: Yep, I guess I am.

[They give each other a hug.]

Boozer: Come on, Jack. Inside. Let's go. If she's out there — you'll find her.

[Boozer walks inside with his pup.]

Iron Mike: Deek, you ready?
Deacon: Yeah, Mike. I'm ready.
Iron Mike: Meet me at the gate. Don't keep me waiting.
Deacon: Yeah, sure, Mike. Whatever you say.

[Deek heads to the front gate. Rikki and Addy come over.]

Deacon: Hey.
Rikki: Heard Big Mike is taking you over the pass?
Deacon: Yep.

Rikki: You really think she's still alive? Billions of people are dead, but
       somehow she made it.

Deacon: Hey, we made it, didn't we? If I give up now, if I don't — if I don't
        do this. Hell, then I'm just gonna end up like, uh —

Rikki: Like us — right? Like Iron Mike? Like Boozer? What'd you call us —
       campers, yeah?

Addy: You go, and you find your woman.

[Addy walks by Rikki.]

Addy: You know where to find me.

[Addy leaves.]

Rikki: Hey, you know what? You know what I think, Deacon? I think that you're
       — you're afraid to be here. You're afraid to be a part of something. We
       need you here and that scares the hell outta you.

Deacon: I'm sorry.
Rikki: Yeah. Me too.

[She stomps off. Mike arrives soon after.]

Iron Mike: You ready?
Deacon: Yeah. I wanna get the hell outta here.
Iron Mike: Come on, this way.
Deacon: Okay, I'm following you.

[The pair leaves Lost Lake at night.]

Iron Mike: Took Jack out fishin' once — before, y'know?
Deacon: No shit —
Iron Mike: He caught one — didn't know what the hell to do with it.
Deacon: That sounds like Jack —

Iron Mike: He ran a pretty tight club. Oh, you boys raised some hell back in
           the day — but I don't think you murdered anyone. Not in cold blood.

Deacon: It's not murder if they shoot at you first.

[They keep riding.]

Iron Mike: You know how many tourists we used to get through here, come summer?

Deacon: A few.

Iron Mike: Thousands — too many to count. Highway'd be bumper-to-bumper with
           SUVS and campers chock full'a sunburned moms, beer-chuggin' dads,
           and their snot-nosed kids. Goddamn rainbow of floppy hats, Hawaiian
           shirts, and flippy flops. All summer long they'd come, like a trail
           of colorful ants, from LA to Farewell, to here. Non-stop.

Deacon: I'm glad I avoided road trips out here that time of year.

[They ride through the Rogue Camp tunnel into ex-Ripper territory.]

Iron Mike: We can use the help.

Deacon: I don't have a choice, Mike.

Iron Mike: Yeah. Fair enough. Come on, just follow me.

Deacon: Yeah, okay.

[They reach a frigid tunnel that leads to Mt. Thielsen.]

Iron Mike: This is it. This is as far as I go. Keep followin' the trail. It'll
           take you down the mountain, on into the Diamond Lake valley. I wish
           you luck. Hope you're right about your old lady still bein' alive.

Deacon: She is.

Iron Mike: Well maybe so. What you gotta ask yourself¹ Deek, is what does it
           matter if everyone else is dead.¹

[Mike rides off back home.]

092) WE'RE FIGHTING A WAR                                                [M092]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[The guards give them admittance into the camp. Captain Kouri stands nearby.]

       know what to do.

        for a long time. Your man, Russell, said you were recruiting?

        interested.

        mostly.

       here soon.

Deacon: Gettin' ready to ride out where?
Kouri: You said you had some tracking skills?
Deacon: Yeah, some.

Kouri: This isn't the life of a Drifter. We're fighting a war out here. You
       sure you're up for it?

[He gazes over at some recruits doing jumping jacks.]

Deacon: Is that the best you got?

Kouri: I can recruit you, but the Colonel is the only one who can swear you in.
       You stick around, give us a hand — I'll take you to him myself.

Deacon: I'll be here.
Kouri: Good.

[Kouri walks off.]

Deacon: Oh, Jesus — Jesus, motherfucker has my ring. He took it from Sarah. He
        had to take it from Sarah because she wouldn't have given it to him. So
        that means that she's gotta be here.

[He spies an odd recruit nearby.]

Deacon: Hmm — he doesn't look like Militia. Hey. Uh — you don't look very
        Militia to me. Um —

Taylor: Nah, man. Name's Wade — Wade Taylor. You can call me Wade.
Deacon: Deacon St. John. Listen —
Taylor: Holy shit — Deacon St. John? Is your old man a preacher or something?
Deacon: No.
Taylor: Man, that is a hell of a name.
Deacon: Alright, listen¹ Wade —
Taylor: You see this, man? This is some crazy shit.
Deacon: Yeah.

Taylor: Whew. So¹ what, you joinin' up? Becomin' an army man? You playin'
        soldier 'n' shit?

Deacon: I don't know — maybe. Listen — uh — You look like you just came in
        from out in the shit, right?

Taylor: Yeah, man. Yesterday, yesterday.
Deacon: Okay — I've been —
Taylor: Been waitin' to see the Colonel or whatever the hell that is —

Deacon: Traveling with some people, we got separated. You see anyone that
        looked like this around here?

[He shows the weird guy Sarah's picture.]

Taylor: Uh, nah¹ man — oooh, but she is a looker. I'd hit that, y'know? Ah, I
        gotta go, man. They're checkin' me for lice or some shit. Good luck to
        ya¹ Deacon St. John — Jesus, what a name.

[Taylor wanders off.]

Deacon: Jesus — that dude's fucked up. He wouldn't remember Sarah if she
        slapped him in the face. Come on¹ Sarah, c'mon — where the hell are
        you? You're here — somewhere. Maybe in these tents? Maybe in here?
        The infirmary. I mean, with her background, that's where she would be.

[Deacon keeps searching tents and wandering.]

Deacon: No, she wouldn't be in the mechanics area. She never knew a wrench from

        what am I thinkin'.¹ Even if she were here, she wouldn't be playing
        soldier with this bunch of assholes. She's not in the commissary. She's

        Check this one. Ah, dammit. She's not here either. That's gotta be the

        now could it.¹

Kouri: St. John. Are you on this channel? Corporal Russell said you had a
       radio.

Deacon: Yeah. Yeah, uh — I'm here.
Kouri: Meet me at the gate.
Deacon: On my way.

Deacon: Looks like the MREs weren't enough for your man — clean gunshot, right
        through the head.

Kouri: Yeah, the wolves must have heard the shot, decided they wanted it more
       than Vasquez.

Deacon: Yeah, the rest of the pack came at us from back that way, from the
        east.

Kouri: You think they chased off Vasquez, leaving one to guard the carcass.
Deacon: That's my guess.
Kouri: Come on. Let's see if you're right.

Deacon: You guys got a lot of wolves out here? Ones that aren't infected, I
        mean.

Kouri: We get reports almost every day.

Deacon: When I was a kid — growin' up — there were no wolves in Oregon. I mean,
        a few coyotes, but no wolves. They'd been driven to extinction by
        ranchers and farmers. Timber companies.

Kouri: Well, it looks like they're making a big comeback.

[Ahead is something pinned under a wolf carcass.]

Deacon: Hold up, hold up, hold up —
Kouri: Well, what is it?
Deacon: Uh, it's a backpack —
Kouri: It's one of ours —
Deacon: Looks like they almost got to him —
Kouri: — and he shrugged off the pack to get away —

Deacon: Nah, nah, nah — to buy time — He landed on his ass, tried to scramble
        away, but then the wolf lunged — Vasquez dropped 'em. Two shots.

Kouri: You can tell all that?
Deacon: Yeah.

[If Deacon tries taking some of the dropped supplies/ammo:]

Deacon: Mind if I take some of this shit?
Kouri: Not at all. We might need it when we catch up to him.
Deacon: Remind me to thank Vasquez once we find him.
Kouri: Yeah. Of course.

[Ahead, Kouri stops Deacon as they approach an overlook.]

Kouri: Wait — get down — a Swarm.
Deacon: A NERO grave site.

Kouri: I don't think this one's marked on our map. They're scattered all over
       the region.

Deacon: Yeah, well maybe that explains why, uh — Vasquez? Came through here.
        Let's go around.

Kouri: Exactly what I was thinking. St. John, this way.
Deacon: Yeah. Right there with you.

[If Deacon foolishly alerts the Horde:]

Kouri: Wait! We're not out here to fight Freaks. Goddammit¹ St. John!

[They continue on.]

Deacon: I gotta say, I'm gettin tired of runnin' and hidin' from these
        sonofbitches.

Kouri: You ever take on a Swarm?
Deacon: Yeah, I've done it before. You just gotta keep movin'.

Kouri: Well¹ look, if you're gonna join the Militia, you must stay focused on
       the mission. We're not out here to fight Freaks.

[The Horde starts leaving shortly afterward.]

Deacon: Bein' in the shit — killing Freaks — kinda goes hand-in-hand, doesn't
        it? Okay, um — put some distance between us and the graves. The cold
        weather's gonna bring out even more of 'em. I think they can smell a
        corpse from about a mile out.

Kouri: Part of our slash-and-burn strategy is to find these grave sites, dig
       'em up, and burn them along with everything else.

Deacon: Yeah, well, good luck with that. I've seen hundreds of 'em, just — in
        this part of the state alone.

Kouri: Well, we gotta start somewhere. Alright, where now?
Deacon: Keep headin' east. Hey, there's a road ahead. Hold up a second.
Kouri: What do you think?
Deacon: Is anyone else tracking him?
Kouri: Not that I know of.

Deacon: Ah — well, then he's either dead — Or he's got a lot of friends. See —
        see how his tracks have been overriden by bikes. A lot of bikes.

Kouri: Hmm — Okay. C'mon. Let's see where they're heading.

[They follow the bike tracks.]

Kouri: You said cold weather brings out the Freaks?
Deacon: Yeah, yeah, cold, snow, rain — hell, even clouds.

Kouri: Well like I said before — you know your Freaks. When we get to Command,
       there's some people who'll want to talk to you.

Deacon: People?
Kouri: The Colonel will fill you in — if he lets you join.
Deacon: Yeah, yeah — I think you said that already.

Kouri: Look, he runs a tight outfit. I just don't want you to get your hopes
       up.

Deacon: Hey, don't worry about me. I don't really give a damn either way.

[Further on...]

Deacon: Hey, wait — hear that?
Kouri: Yeah. It's coming from the logging camp, over there.
Deacon: Is that on your map?
Kouri: Yeah.
Deacon: Well, that means it's also on Vasquez's map.
Kouri: Come on. If Vasquez is there, what would your strategy be?

Deacon: Well, he's not alone. We know that from the tracks — Yeah, what's that
        Militia penalty for going AWOL?

Kouri: Hanging by the neck until dead. Why?
Deacon: Well, it means Vasquez isn't coming without a fight.

096) A TARGET ON THEIR BACKS                                             [M096]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

         back.

        kind of test.

       recruits isn't what it used to be.

Deacon: Yeah, sure. Why the hell not?

[The two start riding down Mt. Thielsen.]

       what an MRE looks like, you know how to recon an enemy position, you
       know "cover and advance" tactical maneuvers. So — where did you serve?
       Marines? Army?

Deacon: I try not to talk about it, you know? I mean, first year out here —

        Afghanistan. So how about you? Anyone who's ex-military has a — a
        certain bearing. None of your "soldiers" have it — but you do.

Kouri: Like I said — you've got a good eye. I was in the Air Force, ten years
       — part of SAC.

Deacon: There ain't no missile silos in Oregon.

       down, I got hourly reports from across the country — you think it was
       bad out here? Everything east of the Mississippi was overrun within two
       days.

[They reach a highway with a great view over the riverlands below.]

Kouri: Hold up. I want to show you something.

[Both disembark and hang out near the vista overlook.]

Kouri: So you familiar with this area?

Deacon: Yeah. I grew up in a town north from here, uh — It's called Farewell.
        You know it?

Kouri: No. Ah, it sounds like a fitting place to be living at the end of the
       world.

Deacon: Yeah, tell me about it.
Kouri: Well, maybe you have been here before.

Deacon: Yeah, I've been here. A few summers back, me and my ol' lady — or my
        wife — stopped by here on our honeymoon.

Kouri: You got a pic? Uh — of your wife, I mean.

[Deacon chuckles; Kouri fishes out his own pic.]

Kouri: Her name was Karie. We were married twelve years when — Anyway. It was
       a long time ago.

097) I PROMISE TO NEVER LEAVE YOU                                        [M097]
_______________________________________________________________________________

Deacon: Well, I thought you didn't want to talk about it —

Deacon: Nope.

        bear witness and support to the same — And to obey all orders without
        question, so do you swear.

Deacon: I swear.
Garret: Dismissed. Walked with me, son.

[The crowd disperses.]

Garret: Captain Kouri doesn't bring me many recruits these days — he must think
        highly of your combat skills.

Deacon: Uh — I've been in the shit a long time.
Garret: You know your way around the Freaks?
Deacon: Yes, sir. I¹ uh — I know as much as anyone. Sir.
Garret: Good, good. In here. We'll have the doc take a look at you.

[They enter Doc Jiminez's medical tent and he patches up Deacon's arm.]

Jiminez: Pulse is strong. Good heart rate. Got a pretty nasty burn there.
         How'd that happen?

Deacon: Uh — had a run-in with a wood stove.
Jiminez: Wood stove, huh? Who dressed this?
Deacon: I did.
Jiminez: No está mal. Not bad at all
Deacon: Thank you.
Jiminez: Keep it dressed or you're gonna lose that arm — you hear me, amigo?
Deacon: Yeah — yeah, I hear you.
Jiminez: I want you to check back with me in a few days.
Deacon: Got it.
Garret: Well, Doc?
Jiminez: Oh¹ he's fit to serve. Lo hará bien. You doing runs out in the shit?
Garret: Sorry¹ Doc, ya tiene novia. He's spoken for.
Jiminez: Let me guess. The Wizard Island Witch. Vaya con Dios. Good luck¹
         amigo.

Garret: Let's go¹ son.

[They exit the tent.]

Garret: I normally don't tolerate insubordination — referring to an officer
        as a "witch." But I make exceptions for some of my more — eccentric —
        officers.

Deacon: Yes¹ sir.

Garret: I make exceptions — because every man and woman still living has a role
        to play. Do you believe in God, St. John?

Deacon: Never gave it much thought — sir.

Garret: Well, it's high time that you did. He has a plan for us. All of us.
        And my part — is this.

Deacon: Sir?

Garret: This — place. I had a vision — oh, nothing so grand as those described
        in the Old Testament — no flaming chariots or burning bushes — I —
        simply woke up one morning — before God's plague had rained down upon
        the world — and knew that this was the place.

Deacon: Crater Lake — uh — Wizard Island?
Garret: I call it the ark. Are you familiar with the story of Noah's Ark?
Deacon: Yeah — I mean — yes¹ sir. I mean, everyone's — everyone's heard of it —

Garret: Indeed. You'd be surprised how few have read the Bible or the book of
        Revelations.

Deacon: You mean Genesis, Noah's story, I — I mean, um — that — it — it's the
        book of Genesis — sir.

Garret: Yes, of course.

[They walk into the mountain through a cave passage.]

Garret: Okay¹ son, let's get you squared away.
Deacon: Whatever you say.

Garret: Now, we don't have much in the way of uniforms, I'm sorry to say, but¹
        uh — I think that¹ uh — oh, here. Try this on.

[He hands him a militia cap to replace Deacon's old one.]

Deacon: Seems to fit.
Garret: I'll take that.
Deacon: Well, if you don't mind, this is a gift from an old friend.
Garret: An old friend. Not many of those left anymore, are there?
Deacon: No, there are not.

Garret: Okay¹ soldier. But I don't want to see you wearing it. You're one of us
        now. And normally, we start new recruits in the rank of private. But
        since Captain Kouri has vouched for your experience in the field —
        We're starting you out at the rank of corporal. Congratulations, son.

Deacon: Thank you — thank you, sir.
Garret: Now, let's get you some work. Alright, now what was I saying —
Deacon: Uh — you were tellin' me about the ark. Sir.

Garret: Yes — the ark. What you see here is only a small part of it. Behind us
        is a whole network of caves and vents that lead from here up to the
        cone's peak. When our work is complete they will be filled with
        thousands of seeds, plants, computer files, and books. The world may
        die, but our achievements in medicine, science, and technology will not
        die with it.

Deacon: No sir.

Garret: But the island is more than just an ark, Corporal. It is a stronghold
        — a fortress. Here at the North Gate, we are stockpiling enough
        munitions to take the fight to the Freaks. We have rifles, grenades,
        heavy machine guns, and RPGs. We have the equipment to make ammunition
        — every type, every caliber. 

[They walk by some outdoor tents and facilities.]

Garret: This is our mechanical engineering area. If you need your bike
        repaired, see the officer on duty. And as you can see here, courtesy
        of the old National Guard, we are building a fleet of trucks and other
        vehicles. Once the Hordes are cleared from the highways, we will begin
        to rebuild the roads and bridges.

Deacon: Your "slash and burn" strategy may stop Newts and Swarmers, but it
        won't clear the highway. It won't — it won't stop the Hordes. Sir.

Garret: We are aware, Corporal. The Hordes — the Hordes are a different beast
        entirely, aren't they. But we have a plan.

Deacon: Plan, sir?

Garret: Benjamin Franklin once said, "by failing to prepare, you are preparing
        to fail." We are not going to fail. The heart of the army lives here,
        at the gate, ready to move on my command. These tents house hundreds
        of women and men — just like yourself — who have pledged and sworn
        their lives to the fight. But I have something else in mind for you.
        An assignment that requires more than just the ability to survive in
        the shit, or use a gun. Are you up for it, son?

Deacon: Uh, yes¹ sir. Wherever you need me.
Garret: You asked how we were going to defeat the Horde? Let me show you.

[They enter another tent. A scientist's concoction sends up sudden sparks.]

Weaver: Whoa, now. Shit.
Garret: You okay¹ Lieutenant?
Weaver: Oh, hey¹ Colonel, sorry about that. Too much acetone in that batch.

Garret: Lieutenant Weaver is our chemical engineer,¹ he's working on new ways
        to —

Weaver: To blow shit up.
Garret: — defeat the enemy.
Weaver: Sorry. But yeah. Uh — name's Weaver. James.
Garret: St. John, Deacon.
Weaver: All this Militia shit's just for show, right¹ Colonel?

Garret: Corporal St. John is new to Kouri's unit. If you need anything from
        out in the shit, he's your man.

Weaver: Oh, shit yeah. Here, there's a couple of things I need.
Deacon: What are you working on?
Weaver: Oh, just the new gelling agent combining naphthenic and palmitic acid.
Deacon: You're working on napalm?
Weaver: Yeah, yeah — this dude knows his shit.
Deacon: Just a lucky guess. Uh —
Garret: Sorry to interrupt.
Weaver: Oh, anytime. Oh, Colonel. I'm getting real close, Colonel. Very close.
Garret: That's good. That's really good.
Weaver: Where're you going next, Colonel? Wizard Island Witch?
Garret: That'll be all¹ Lieutenant.

[They leave Weaver's tent.]

Garret: Again, let me apologize for my more — eccentric — officers.
Deacon: No need, sir.

Garret: We have one final stop. As much as I believe in Lieutenant Weaver's
        work, what you're about to see could be, I think, our path to victory.
        In here.

[They enter the "Witch's" tent and find her speaking to another soldier.]

Sarah: Alright, what is this?
Soldier: Ma'am? I got everything on the requisition form —
Sarah: Does this look like fabric softener?
Soldier: No¹ ma'am.
Sarah: Okay, why don't you read it.

Soldier: Active ingredients. Chlor — clor — oh — form — And uh, A-terp — terp
         — terp — in — Shit.

[She takes the bottle away from him.]

Sarah: Get out. Get out! Matt, I can't do this if I have to do my own supply
       runs.

Garret: I got it covered. Lieutenant Whitaker, this is Corporal St. John. He's
        a new member of Kouri's unit. He's got some experience out in the shit.

[Sarah doesn't acknowledge that she knows him.]

Sarah: Read this.
Deacon: What?
Sarah: Read this. I mean, you can read, can't you?

Deacon: Active ingredients. Chloroform, A-Terpineol, Benzyl Alcohol, Ethyl
        Acetate —

Sarah: Good enough. When can he start?
Garret: I'll leave you to it. Carry on, Lieutenant.

[The colonel leaves.]

Sarah: Leave us.

[The other soldier nearby does as well.]

Deacon: Sarah —
Sarah: Stand at attention.
Deacon: Sarah, I —
Sarah: Don't.

[She runs a hand over his face.]

Sarah: No¹ you're — you're — you're dead. You're — you're dead. You're — you're
       supposed to be dead.

Deacon: Hey — hey, hey, hey —
Sarah: You're dead. You're dead.
Deacon: It's okay. I'm right here.

[They share a brief kiss, but she pulls a way.]

Sarah: Wait — wait a — wait a second¹ I — I don't understand — I couldn't find
       you —

Deacon: I — I thought you had died and I¹ uh — Boozer and I —

Sarah: No — we were overrun and — We had to go south — NERO, they said that no
       one made it out — Farewell was overrun — They said that everybody was
       dead.

Deacon: We — yeah, NERO — no — I found O'Brien and I found a way — over the
        mountain —

Sarah: I never thought I would see you again —
Deacon: And I didn't think that I would ever see you again.

[He tries to kiss her again, but she pulls back.]

Sarah: No — no, I can't — I can't —

Deacon: Hey, hey listen. Now, we can ride outta here, we'll pick a direction,
        we won't look back. C'mon —

Sarah: No, you — wait a — No. No, Deacon. I can't —
Deacon: Are they — are they forcing you to stay here?

Sarah: No. You don't understand. We're fighting a war. Don't you see? This is
       a war that we can win.

Deacon: I didn't come here to fight a war.

Sarah: I can be helpful. I can make a difference, but I — I can't go with you.
       I have to stay here. Don't you get it, you — you can stay here with me.
       Help me. Look — afterwards, whatever you say — we — we — we can go
       wherever you want.

[A soldier comes back 'round.]

Soldier: Colonel's looking for you.
Deacon: Whatever you say, ma'am.
Sarah: Wait — wait a second. Your requisition form. Thank you, soldier.

[He leaves Sarah's tent. A RFO broadcast can be heard if outside city limits.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. The Feds
          were whining babies, suckling at the teat of us taxpayers. But dumb
          as they were, we can't underestimate 'em. You gotta know the chief
          muckety-mucks are hiding out there in some bunker, waiting for the
          Freaks to die off. They didn't save the hungry, or their precious
          constituents — you know, the real reason they're in power? They saved
          the elite, the men and women who played ball. They're sittin'
          underground probably drinkin' Champagne while they wait. Meanwhile,
          we're out here dyin' — sufferin' — all so the Feds can hit the damn
          reset button. But they didn't account for one thing: we're not as
          stupid as they thought we were. And once they emerge to "reclaim the
          world" when the Freaks are gone, we'll be waitin'. Oh, yes we will.
          And they'll be sorry they ever came out of hiding. This is Mark
          Copeland for Radio Free Oregon. Don't believe the lies.

Deacon: Ah, Jesus — even all the way down here, I can't get away from Goddamned
        Radio Free Oregon.

101) KEEPING SOUVENIRS                                                   [M101]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deek returns to Kouri's outpost later on.]

Kouri: Corporal. Good. I have a job that requires your — unique skills.
Deacon: Uh — sure. Yeah — uh — yes¹ sir.
Kouri: You remember Vasquez?

Deacon: The man who went AWOL — yeah, we tracked him to the logging camp. I
        remembered.

Kouri: Well this man — Sergeant Lee Anderson — was his partner. He was about
       to be arrested when he killed a guard and took off.

Deacon: Your men have quite the "code of honor" —

Kouri: Our men. You're one of us now. Remember? I've marked the location on
       where he was last seen on your map. Apparently, like Vasquez — he wasn't
       alone.

Deacon: Great.

[Deek rides out on Anderson's trail, coming to the Maclaughin Point suburb.]

Deacon: Captain Kouri — I'm at the site where Sergeant Anderson was last seen.

Kouri: Well if he still has it, take his Militia insignia. I won't have it
       soiled by the stench of a traitor.

Deacon: You got it. St. John out. Alright¹ Anderson — let's go take care of
        business. Oh — he's gotta be here somewhere — Where the hell is he —
        Okay — let's take a look around.

[Deek comes across an infected wolf's corpse near mauled bodies.]

Deacon: Which way — Oh shit — wolves — Gotta take a closer look. Oh my God —
        is that Anderson that they're dragging? Oh — how the hell am I gonna
        get my bounty?

[He follows the blood trail to a cave.]

Deacon: Dead Coyote Lava Cave — well — nothing bad can happen with a name like
        that, yeah?

[The trail leads further into the runners' den.]

Deacon: Squeeze through here — You still got your Militia arm band?

[He loots Anderson's wolf-chewed corpse and exits, only to find a bear nearby.]

Deacon: Oh shit — Rager. Dammit. Maybe — I can sneak around?

[Deek returns to Kouri later.]

Deacon: Captain. I found your man — Anderson. And — you were right — he still
        had his Militia insignia —

Kouri: He's dead?

Deacon: Let's just say that he had a run-in with a pack of wolves long before
        I got to him.

Kouri: That's a fitting end for a murderer and a thief.
Deacon: Yes¹ sir.
Kouri: Thank you, Corporal. Dismissed.

[Deek rides out of camp, and no sooner has he done so, than...]

Taylor: Corporal St. John — uh — Wade Taylor to Deacon St. John.

Deacon: Taylor. Uh — I hear a bike. Tell me you're not out in the shit trackin'
        down that drug trafficker.

Taylor: Okay, okay — I won't tell you that. But I am.
Deacon: Goddammit — Taylor — you're gonna get yourself killed —
Taylor: Nah¹ man, no, no — hey, I followed a bunch of 'em up the highway —
Deacon: Highway 97?

Taylor: Hey, hey, it was — no, it was — it was daylight — weather was clear —
        I didn't see a single Freak. Uh — but there is this — this group of —
        of men, ended up at the ski lodge — did you even know there was a ski
        lodge out here? I didn't know that.

Deacon: Taylor —

Taylor: It's a sweet¹ ass setup too. If I ever decide to bug out, that is where
        I'm goin' — oh, shit, I gotta run. They're — they're stoppin' at
        another camp. Taylor out.

Deacon: Taylor? Taylor? Oh — dammit — stupid kid's gonna get himself killed.

102) I KNOW THINGS ARE STRANGE                                           [M102]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deek radios into Kouri after Taylor's convo.]

Deacon: Deacon St. John to Captain Kouri — St. John to Kouri, come back.

Kouri: St. John, I've just spoken with the Colonel — he's assigned you to the
       research division.

Deacon: Captain, uh — research division — uh, I guess you could call it that —
        uh — I'm helping Lieutenant Weaver and Lieutenant Whitaker.

Kouri: Good. They can use all the help you can offer.

        boy for now. And actually — that's why I radioed in. Lieutenant
        Whitaker gave me a requisition form that says yeast.

Kouri: Yeast? Hold a second. We have patrols making supply runs throughout the
       region. When they come across anything of potential value they note it

       kitchen area of the Crater Lake Visitor's Center. You know where that
       is?

Deacon: Yeah, I can find it.

[Deek heads to the other side of Crater Lake to find the destination.]

Deacon: Visi - Visitor's Center. That's gotta be it. Now — just gotta find
        some yeast. Kitchen — yeah, well. It's gotta be in the kitchen. Oh,
        shit — Breakers. Had to be Breakers. It couldn't be fuckin' easy,
        could it?

[Deacon slays the Newts and Breakers in the parking lot.]

Deacon: That's the last of 'em. Okay — now where the hell's the yeast.¹

[He jimmies the lock on the kitchen building and infiltrates.]

Deacon: Yeast — yeast — Ah, here it is. Yes. I hope this is enough. St. John
        to, uh — Lieutenant — Whitaker. Reporting in.

Sarah: Deacon, uh — Corporal St. John. Yes.

Deacon: I, um — got the item on your requisition form. The yeast. There wasn't
        much.

Sarah: I — I'm sure that — whatever you have is gonna be fine.
Deacon: So, um — just curious, uh — why do you need —

Sarah: Sorry, I'm right in the middle of something, I gotta go. I'll talk to
       you when you bring it in. Whitaker Out¹.

Deacon: Okay. You're welcome —

[Later, Deacon delivers the yeast to Sarah personally. She's mad at something.]

Sarah: Oh, Goddammit.
Deacon: Ma'am.

[He salutes.]

Sarah: Look, would you stop doing that, please?
Deacon: I'm sorry?
Sarah: I know that things are strange, but I can't help that right now.

Deacon: Well, I live in a barracks with a dozen Militia assholes — While my
        wife lives in a private tent up on an officer's ridge. Nothing strange
        about that.

Sarah: Deacon —

Deacon: And the only time that I see her is when I'm done running one of her
        errands. Nothing strange about that either. Ma'am.

Sarah: My yeast. Thank you.

Deacon: Uh, are — are you baking something? I mean, if you need an oven, I
        know where to find one.

Sarah: No, no, I'm using it to create viral proteins, that they — they trigger
       these antibodies — But of course, you were being sarcastic.

Deacon: Bread — viral proteins, it's all the same to me.
Sarah: Hey, wait a second. Here.

[She hands him another requisition form.]

Sarah: Thank you.
Deacon: You already said that.
Sarah: I meant, for staying.
Deacon: Yes¹ ma'am.

[As Deek leaves, his radio crackles to life.]

Jiminez: No, no, set them over there. Thank you. Corporal St. John? This is
         Doctor Jiminez. St. John?

Deacon: Hey¹ Doc, this is Deacon. What can I do for you?
Jiminez: Oh, St. John. Good. I need you to stop by the infirmary.
Deacon: Uh — is something wrong? You need something?
Jiminez: No, no. Nothing like that. I want to check on that arm.
Deacon: My arm? My — my arm's fine, doc.

Jiminez: A burn like that — from a wood stove — is nothing to play around with.
         You want la infection? You come see me. That's an order.

Deacon: Alright¹ Doc. Alright, fine, whatever you say. St. John out.

[If Deacon heads outside town:]

Sarah: Deacon, are you there? Deacon —
Deacon: I'm here.
Sarah: Look, I know we have a lot to talk about.
Deacon: Ma'am?
Sarah: This is a private channel. Deek?
Deacon: Okay.

Sarah: I want you to know that I meant what I said about — about you staying
       and helping. I — I know this — can't be easy for you. Being here — like
       this.

Deacon: Hey, uh — where else am I gonna go? And if I leave, they're gonna make
        me give back this really cool hat, — so I'm startin' to like this hat.
        I mean, really.

Sarah: Oh, I bet. Okay, alright, I gotta get back to work. This yeast has
       already filled up like half a dozen petri dishes.

Deacon: Okay, save me some of the viral proteins — I got an appetite out here.
Sarah: I'll do that. Lieutenant Whitaker out.

104) I'VE HAD BETTER DAYS                                                [M104]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[As he leaves the tent, his "friend" radios in.]

Taylor: St. John. Come in. Taylor to Deacon St. John.

Taylor: No, man — no, no — I can't — please, man — don't let him — fuck —
Marauder: You better — better do it — you better do it. I'll — I'll kill him.

Deacon: Taylor! — dammit!

[Saving Taylor from his captor's the only way to move forward, however.]

Deacon: Sure — yeah. I'll see what I can do —

[Suddenly, Deacon can hear gunfire and Freaker noises.]

[Deacon starts pushing a car underneath the window and rushes through. It's
 eerily quiet as he searches around.]

        Sarah? Sarah! No — dammit — no — Sarah! Sarah! Where are you? Come on —
        answer me — If anything's happened to you — Sarah?! I'm gonna kill —
        every one of you fucking bastards — Sarah, answer me — Sarah — Sarah!

Deacon: Hey —

       coming — I couldn't —

Sarah: I'm fine. C'mon, we're almost there.

[They walk outside.]

Sarah: This is the science building.
Deacon: Yeah. Looks like this place has been shut up tight from the inside.
Sarah: C'mon. There's gotta be a way in.
Deacon: Hey, are you sure you're okay?
Sarah: Yeah. I've killed Freaks before —
Deacon: No, I know, I know — it's just —
Sarah: Deacon, I'm fine. Let's go. Let's check this door. Can you open it?
Deacon: No, it's jammed from the inside.
Sarah: Let's go around the building. There has to be a way in.

Sarah: Oh Goddammit!
Deacon: Hey, hey¹ it's okay.
Sarah: It's jammed. Like all the rest.
Deacon: I'm sure we can find another way —

[A noise inside startles them.]

Sarah: Oh shit —

Sarah: What the fuck?!
Deacon: Hold on — hold on a second — those are —

        be a way in from the roof.

Sarah: Yeah. Come on. C'mon — the roof's lower over there.
Deacon: Yep — we just have to — find a way up.

[They find a jeep nearby.]

Deacon: Sarah, here. Uh — help me push this. We can use it to climb up.
Sarah: Okay.

Sarah: Yeah.

Sarah: That far enough?

Sarah: They remind me of that little girl — the one in Farewell —
Deacon: The one that fuckin' stabbed you?
Sarah: She didn't know what she was doing.
Deacon: None of 'em know what they're doin' — won't stop 'em from killing you.

Deacon: There's more of 'em —
Sarah: I see 'em —
Deacon: Look out —
Sarah: I got 'em —

[Finally, all the li'l Freakers lie dead.]

Deacon: That's the last of 'em —
Sarah: You enjoyed that —

Deacon: What, killin' Newts? No, but — I mean, you gotta admit they're pretty
        Goddamn annoying —

Sarah: You're right about that —

[They find a high skylight to get through.]

Deacon: Here, give me your hand —
Sarah: Okay —

[Deek drops down into the building.]

Deacon: Careful — steady —
Sarah: I got this — alright —

[She falls into his arms.]

Sarah: Careful —
Deacon: Ugh — not only are they annoying, but they smell like shit —
Sarah: Yeah, well you try living like them — see how you smell after two years.
Deacon: No thanks — where — where — where're we goin'?

Sarah: Try these doors. Uh — one of these is gonna be a lab or a lecture room.
       Centrifuge has to be here somewhere.

[They enter a room filled with peaceful-looking corpses.]

Deacon: Hey, I don't — I don't get it. There's no, uh, bullet holes, no sign
        of violence or attack —

[Sarah smells some residue from a cup nearby.]

Sarah: Hemlock.
Deacon: Jesus.
Sarah: Over here.
Deacon: Is that the, uh, centrifuge you were looking for?
Sarah: Yep. This is it. C'mon.
Deacon: Okay.

111) YOU COULDN'T STOP SHAKING                                           [M111]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[They walk outside. At the gate, they hear yelling, explosions and gunfire.]

Sarah: Explain what, Deacon? Why everyone in the good ol' boys club calls me

Sarah: Nothing's "happened" to me that hasn't happened to every other fucking
       person on this planet.

Deacon: Yeah, okay. If you say so.
Sarah: C'mon, let's go.
Deacon: Right behind you.

[Back at the bike, they secure the centrifuge and ride home to Wizard Island.]

Sarah: Can I say thank you?
Deacon: No.
Sarah: Okay. You know, I just wanted to let you know how much I needed this.

[She walks off.]

Deacon: You're welcome.

[If Deacon goes outside town, he can hear a convo snippet from up north:]

Copeland: Manny, this is Copeland — come back —
Manny: Cope — I'm headin' out on a run — I thought I'd —
Copeland: I told you, Manny — you're gonna get yourself killed —
Manny: I can take care of myself, Cope — I'll be fine —
Deacon: Keep your nose down, Manny. They'll feed ya.

113) WHAT KEPT ME GOING                                                  [M113]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deek visits Sarah after his checkup.]

[She kisses him hard.]

        right now. I'd like to see what he's doing.

        advanced as you've been saying.

Deacon: What is that all about, anyway?
Sarah: What?

Deacon: All the yes sirs and no sirs, and the saluting and the ranks and the
        uniforms. It just seems kinda pointless, you know? Considering.

Sarah: Hey, you were in the army once. You should know.
Deacon: That was different.
Sarah: How?

Deacon: Well, there were more people in the world. I don't know. I mean —
        havin' a military made more sense.

Sarah: I think it makes more sense now.
Deacon: Why?

Sarah: It's utter fucking chaos out here. We need the order and discipline or
       we're not gonna make it.

Deacon: You know, I've been at plenty of camps that are doin' just fine without
        having a Colonel breathin' down their necks.

Sarah: You know what's funny? About uniforms and ranks seeming pointless, I
       mean?

Deacon: No, what?

Sarah: I used to think the same thing about the MC. I mean, you guys had ranks
       like "Road Captain," and "President," I mean — you wore badges and
       patches and — and tats like uniforms. And when you guys used to all ride
       together you looked like an army. Well, except for the beards and bikes.

Deacon: Now that you mention it — I — I can see your point.

Sarah: You know, I'm actually surprised you weren't wearing the cut when you
       came into the camp. I didn't think anything would make you give that up
       —  even the end of the world.

Deacon: Okay, so my cut, huh? I'm gonna have to see if the Colonel will let me
        switch uniforms.

Sarah: You know, there is that. Where are we heading?

Deacon: To Diamond Lake. There's an old forest service road that winds around
