A SCORE TO SETTLE                                                        [SD03]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon returns to Salome after "We've All Done Things."]

Tucker: Deek, we got a problem.
Deacon: Yeah¹ Tuck, what's up?
Tucker: You remember Alkai said that Rippers were spotted — heading our way?
Deacon: Yeah, I remember. He said he didn't try to stop them.

Tucker: Well, we've seen 'em scouting the Hot Springs. A couple of men followed
        'em back to their camp, in the cliffs south of the Twin Craters.

Deacon: Goddamn Rippers. Don't worry about it. I'll take care of 'em. I got a
        score to settle.

Tucker: A score? What are you talking about?
Deacon: Uh — never mind.

[He makes for the camp.]

Deacon: Goddamn Rippers. You fuck with my friend? I am going to fucking kill
        every Goddamn one of you.

[Deacon has various lines he can say when killing the Rippers. Examples:]

 • Rest. In. Peace. You sonofabitch.
 • Burn my friend's arm, you get low motherfucker!
 • Where's Carlos, motherfucker — huh? He send you?
 • What's your name, asshole? I wanna know who I'm killing!
 • Fuck you — you wanna Rest in Peace — let me help you out —

[After slaughtering the fiends:]

Deacon: Tucker, you there? You don't gotta worry about that Ripper Camp no
        more. I took care of 'em. Every last one of 'em.

Tucker: Nice job. Sounds like you did have a score to settle. Alkai said
        there's rumors going around, that the Rippers are after the biker
        boys.

Deacon: Let's just say they fucked with the wrong guy. Deacon out.

COMING INTO TOWN                                                         [SD04]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "Do You Have My Back?", Deacon returns to Tucker.]

Tucker: Deek, thanks for stopping by.
Deacon: What's going on?

Tucker: Remember Larsen, the guy who spotted that gal in Marion Forks? The one
        I told you about?

Deacon: Yeah. I remember.

Tucker: Well he went back out there. To see what else he could find. He hasn't
        come back. We think he's been taken by a group of Drifters who've been
        moving through the Belknap wilderness.

Deacon: Shit. Where was he last seen?
Tucker: A building on the east side of town. The Old Wagon Hotel.
Deacon: Yeah, I know the one.
Tucker: Thanks, Deek. I appreciate it.

[Deek goes to the neighboring town.]

Deacon: Tucker — I'm at the Old Wagon Hotel, and I'm heading in.
Tucker: Do you see Larsen? Is he there?
Deacon: I don't know, but if he is, I'm gonna find him. St. John out.

[As Deek approaches, he can hear the hostage yelping.]

Larsen: Help — I'm in here — Goddammit —

[Deek swiftly delivers death unto the captors.]

Deacon: Heya¹ Larsen, how're you holdin' up?

Larsen: St. John. You know, thought I'd come into town, find a drink, hang out
        with my buds —

Deacon: Soon as I cut you loose, you get the hell outta here.

Larsen: You don't gotta tell me twice. I don't know where the hell you came
        from, but Jesus¹ man.

Deacon: Go. Run.

Deacon: Tuck, you there? I found Larsen,¹ he should be on his way back to the
        Hot Springs.

Tucker: Nice job. I'll have Alkai keep a look out for him. More Rippers have
        been spotted moving north into Belknap. We need all the men we can get.
        Tucker out.

DIDN'T WANT TO JOIN UP?                                                  [SD05]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "I Tried to Hit That Once," Deacon visits Kouri for a job.]

Kouri: Corporal. Deacon. Good. Thank you for reporting in so quickly.
Deacon: It sounded urgent — sir.
Kouri: It is. We have another hostage situation.

Deacon: Hostage. Damn. It seems like every Squatter within a dozen miles has it
        in for us — or for the Militia — you know — I mean.

Kouri: It does seem that way. I've marked his last known position on your map.
       He's just a kid — St. John. Private Ross — Ethan. I sent him to track
       down a group of Marauders and he musta gotten in over his head.

Deacon: Private Ross — I don't know him — but, uh — I'll get him out alive,
        Captain.

Kouri: Good luck, St. John. Dismissed.

[Deek goes out in pursuit, entering the southern region's NE sector.]

Deacon: Where are you, Ethan — I'll find ya.

[Down the road...]

Deacon: Oh, Jesus — helluva camp they got going on here — Now just gotta —
        find a way in —

[He blows up a junk barricade.]

Deacon: Oh yeah — we're in business —

[He, and some Freaks, end up slaying the band.]

Deacon: Now that — that was a lotta Goddamn Marauders. Jesus.

[Deek goes over to the bound captive.]

Deacon: Hey, Ethan, I presume, uh, yeah? How ya doing, buddy?
Ethan: Corporal. Man, am I glad to see you.
Deacon: Yeah? You didn't wanna join up with those assholes?
Ethan: Hell no, and I had no idea what they were gonna do to me.

Deacon: Yeah, well, it wasn't gonna be good. Uh, are you good to get outta here
        on your own?

Ethan: Yeah. Yeah. Thanks, man.

[Ethan leaves. Later, on the ride back...]

Deacon: St. John to Captain Kouri, uh — it's done¹ sir, the kid is on his way
        back.

Kouri: Good work, St. John. You've been — a huge part of what makes us
       successful. The Deschutes County Militia would not be the same without
       you.

Deacon: Thank you, sir. Um — I will radio in later and make sure he made it.
        St. John out.

[Later...]

Deacon: Deacon St. John to Captain Kouri — uh — how's that kid doing?

Kouri: Good. A little dehydrated and — hungry. The cook tells me he's almost
       cleaned out the mess hall single-handed.

Deacon: Well, tell him to save some for me. St. John out.

DRIFTERS AT EDEN HILL                                                    [SD06]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Rikki calls Deek back to town after "Do You Have My Back?".]

Rikki: Deek, a group of men rode in, shot up the gate, and when we wouldn't let
       them in, they rode off.

Deacon: Shit, what direction?

Rikki: They headed west, but they didn't go far. They've set up camp just north
       of Eden Hill. I think they might be planning another attack — so I need
       you to take a look.

Deacon: Okay — right, yeah — I'll handle it.
Rikki: Thanks¹ Deek.

[He rides out to Eden Hill.]

Deacon: Okay — Rikki, I'm near Eden Hill — yeah — Drifters — still here.
Rikki: Can you handle it?
Deacon: Well, I guess we'll know soon enough. Deacon out.

[He creeps closer and starts picking them off.]

Deacon: Alright, gentlemen — thought you'd just swing by, shoot up the place?
        I just think it's time you move along. Oh, come on — let's do this —
        huh? Oh, come on, you can do better than that — How many ya got left?
        Oh, is that it? No — ah, shit — one more. Okay, I think that's all of
        'em. Okay, time to — radio in and — let Rikki know —

Rikki: Deacon — how'd it go?
Deacon: It's done. They won't be shootin' up any more camps.

Rikki: Whew — thank God. I'll let Iron Mike know. You know, keep this up and
       and you and Mike are gonna be best friends before you know it. Bye¹
       Deek.

[As Deek starts to leave, Mike radios in.]

Iron Mike: Deek — you track down those boys, shot up the gate and took off?
Deacon: Hey¹ Mike, yeah. Uh — I found 'em, and they won't be — comin' back.

Iron Mike: Seem like it's getting worse? Amount a' Squatters and Drifters we
           got comin' through? No offense to present company.

Deacon: None taken — uh — and yeah, Mike, it's getting worse. I don't know —
        Mike, I think it's like you were saying about tourists — always coming
        up here from California — well, I guess if I had the choice, yeah, I'd
        rather be here than down there.

Iron Mike: Yeah, I guess so. See ya¹ Deek. Iron Mike out.

DROWNED THEM LIKE RATS                                                   [SD07]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "I'm Good With That," Deacon rides up to Sarah's memorial stone.]

Deacon: Uh, hey. Me again. I know, I know. It's, uh — been a while since I've been up here. It's just, um — okay, we, uh — had a run-in — with the
        Rippers. With Carlos. See, um — turns out, "Carlos" is actually this
        two-bit hood we knew from before. Back in the day, he was a
        fully-patched member of the MC. Yeah, I know — what are the odds of
        him surviving —  Jessie Goddamn Williamson — when so many others —
        died. And, uh — I never told you what happened to Jessie, uh — well —
        you know, because you hate it when I talk about club shit, so — let's
        just say — that some bad shit went down, really bad shit — And Jack —
        he, uh — he — well, he kicked Jessie outta the club — but — you can't
        take your colors with you. See, that — that's a problem. So — problem
        is Jessie had a Mongrels — tat on his back — just like mine, you know?
        So — yeah — me and Boozer, Jersey Jim, we held him down — while Jack —
        uh — took a welding torch to, uh — to his back. Look, I'm not proud of
        it — I'm not proud of it. I — never told you because — um — because I
        knew that you would — never be with someone who could do something like
        that. And, uh — hey — you know — I would tell you that I've changed —
        but — at this point — there's — there's no reason to lie to you
        anymore. I killed him — Jessie — I had to, I mean — guy was a Goddamn
        psychopath. But, uh — we didn't stop with him — Boozer and I, we —
        we blew 'em up. The Rippers, we blew up their camp, we drowned 'em like
        a bunch of sorry rats. And you know what? I'm not sorry. I just thought
        you should know. Okay. I gotta go. Uh, I'll — I'll talk to you later.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
EVIL SURROUNDS US                                                        [SD08]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "How Far We Have Fallen," Deek attends a perfectly sane Garret rally.]

Garret: A short while ago, I stood here before you — And grieved for the loss
        of Captain Jiminez — Our only doctor — and my very dear friend. And for
        what great purpose did Captain Jiminez perish? So that a drug addict —
        a worthless excuse of a human being — could get high. Jiminez died
        because he stood between a junkie — and a bag full of narcotics. I have
        taken steps to see that this never happens again. For their own safety,
        I have moved Lieutenants Whitaker and Weaver into the ark — Where they
        will be under protective watch — twenty-four hours a day. The call is
        going out — any person who has highly trained knowledge and skills —
        skills that cannot be replaced — Mechanics, engineers, scientists,
        medical personnel — Are to be taken from active duty and removed to the
        ark — until this war is over. From now on, no one is allowed entrance
        into the ark unless they are on special assignment — And unless they
        are personally vetted by myself. There will be no exceptions. I am
        beginning to see — I'm afraid — that our enemy has never been the
        Freaks. They know not what they do. Mankind — in all his state of
        degradation and transgression — is our true enemy. Keep a watchful eye
        on your neighbors. Evil — surrounds us. Company dismissed.

GONE FISHING                                                             [SD09]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[A little before "Riding the Open Road," Deek visits Rikki in town.]

Rikki: Deek, I'm really worried.
Deacon: Rikki, what's up?
Rikki: The Butler twins — Abigail and Gabbi — you know them?

Deacon: No, but¹ uh — I've seen 'em around. What's — what's going on, what's
        wrong?

Rikki: They went out fishing yesterday and they didn't come back —
Deacon: The lakeshore's pretty safe so long as they stay out of the marsh —

Rikki: That's just it — they weren't at Lost Lake — they went east, over to
       the Metolius River —

Deacon: The hell were they thinking? Okay, alright, yeah. I'll¹ uh — I'll see
        if I can find 'em.

Rikki: Deacon, thank you so much.

[Deacon rides out into the wastes.]

Deacon: Hey¹ Rikki, what else can you tell me?

Rikki: Before everything went to hell, the girls' family had a fishing site
       that they always used to go to. I marked it on your map.

Deacon: Okay — I'll start there. Deacon out.

[Deacon nears the fishing hole and investigates the tracks.]

Deacon: Okay — fishing pole — it's just the one — it's gotta be the right
        place — Okay — the girls were fishing — oh, shit — Marauders — Jesus —
        Up this way —

[He tracks them nearby to a compound where Marauders contend with Freaks.]

Deacon: Inside here —

[He opens the cabin and kills those inside.]

Deacon: That did it — Inside here —

[After unlocking the bathroom, he finds a weeping girl.]

Deacon: Gabbi, it's okay. Hey, hey, hey, I'm not here to hurt you. Rikki sent
        me.

Gabbi: They killed my sister. They killed Abigail.

Deacon: No, I know, I know. I'm sorry, uh, we just have to get you back to
        camp — come on, come. With me —

Gabbi: No, no! I can make it myself. I can —
Deacon: Okay, go. Go!

[Deacon rides back for town after letting Gabbi return unaccompanied.]

Deacon: Rikki — I found her — alive —

Rikki: Deacon, thank God —

Deacon: Look, she wouldn't come with me, so — you gotta send someone who knows
        her — okay? She's on her way back to camp.

Rikki: Okay — alright, okay — Rikki out.

[Later on...]

Iron Mike: Deacon St. John — You there?
Deacon: Yeah, Mike. I'm here.

Iron Mike: Rikki told me what you done, savin' Gabbi and all. I just — I just
           wanted to thank ya. I've known that lil'¹ gal since she was in
           diapers.

Deacon: Sure¹ Mike — yeah — I, uh — just wish that I could have gotten to
        Abigail in time.

Iron Mike: Ya did what you could, and I'm grateful. See ya¹ Deek. I'm glad
           you're on our side. Mike out.

Deacon: Hey, did someone pick her up?

Rikki: Hey¹ Deek — yeah, she's fine. A little traumatized, but I guess no more
       than anyone else.

Deacon: Well, I guess we all know what it's like to lose someone.
Rikki: Yeah, I guess we do.
Deacon: Yeah. See ya, Rikki.

HARD TO MISS                                                             [SD10]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "Do You Have My Back?", Deacon returns to Copeland.]

Copeland: St. John—¹ I got a bounty job for you.
Deacon: I'm listening.

Copeland: You're looking for Ned Walker. Wears a red scarf. He and his crew
          came to the gate the other night. Wouldn't let him in. He killed one
          of my guards, then took off.

Deacon: You have someone follow 'em?

Copeland: He's holed up at a Marauder camp, just north of O'Leary Mountain. I
          think you know where that is.

Deacon: No. But I'll find him.

[He locates the camp on the other side of the mountain.]

Deacon: Cope — I'm at the camp.
Copeland: Copy that. Cope out.
Deacon: Hey¹ Cope, uh — the man he killed. Who was it?
Copeland: A young kid, everyone called him Gopher — never knew his real name.
Deacon: Gopher. How old was he?

Copeland: Like I said, a kid. Nineteen, twenty. No idea how he lasted this
          long. But he was a good kid. Why you askin'?

Deacon: No reason.

Copeland: If you spent more time at the camp, got to know folks, then maybe
          you'd find a reason. Cope out.

[Deek spies the bescarved Ned on an upper camp catwalk.]

Deacon: That's him — Ned Walker — motherfucker. Hello¹ Ned — I'd say it's good
        to see you, but it's not.

[Later, Deacon loots the headwear as a trophy.]

Deacon: Cope's gonna want this —

[He makes it back to his bike.]

Deacon: Cope — it's done. You won't be hearin' from Ned Walker again.
Copeland: Bring me his bandana. I wanna see it for myself. Cope out.
Deacon: Yeah. Of course you do.

[He returns to town.]

Copeland: Nice work. Lost more'n a few men tryin' to hunt down that
          sonofabitch.

Deacon: Next time, just come to me.
Copeland: You volunteerin'? Never thought I'd see the day.
Deacon: My bike —
Copeland: Go see Manny. If you got enough camp credits, he'll fix you right up.

HE NEVER CAME BACK                                                       [SD11]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "What Have They Done," Deacon returns to Copeland's Camp.]

Copeland: St. John — I got a job for you.
Deacon: Cope —

Copeland: You want Manny to work on your bike? Only one way that's gonna
          happen —

Deacon: — I gotta do runs for you. Yeah, I heard you.

Copeland: I need you to deal with a Marauder Camp near those burned out shacks
          along the Cascade Highway. You know where I'm talkin' about?

Deacon: Yeah, I know it.
Copeland: Radio me if you want to know more.

[Deacon begrudgingly sets out.]

Deacon: Cope, I'm headin' to that Drifter camp along the highway. What else
        can you tell me?

Copeland: Not much. They followed one of our supply runs — got a little too
          close. I sent a man to check 'em out. He never came back.

Deacon: You send anyone to find him?
Copeland: Yeah. Man named Deacon St. John. Cope out.

[Following their trail, Deacon spots multiple corpses.]

Deacon: Alright — where — Got ya. This is it — Alright — what've we got —
        Still got this — Okay — let's take a look around.

[Eventually the trail leads to a loud torturer and his victim.]

Hostage: No, no, no —
Torturer: Just tell us — what we want to know —
Hostage: I don't know nothin¹ — oh —
Torturer: oh¹ yeah? You don't know nothin' huh?
Hostage: no¹, no —
Torturer: The supply runs — where are you getting the shit for your camp?
Hostage: I don't —
Torturer: Tell me!
Hostage: I don't know — nothin'! All over — same as — anyone —

Torturer: The camp — Copeland's his name? How many people live there? In the
          camp? How many? How many?!

Hostage: I — I don't know — no —

Torturer: How do you like that? Huh? You havin' trouble breathin'? Makin' it
          hard to talk? Let's see if I can fix it!

Hostage: I don't know nothin' — no —

Torturer: You ready to talk yet? Huh? Don't be a dumbass. Why sacrifice
          yourself? Huh? What's Copeland ever done for you?

[Deacon makes quick work of the hostage-taking trio.]

Hostage: No more. No more.
Deacon: Just, shut up, I'm cuttin' you loose.
Hostage: What, what? You're not —
Deacon: Copeland sent me. Come on, get up.
Hostage: Oh, my God, thank you — thank you.
Deacon: Come on.
Hostage: They were following us — on a supply run. I didn't know what to do.
Deacon: Hey, shut up. Can you run?
Hostage: What? Yeah, yeah.
Deacon: Well then run. Go.
Hostage: Thank you. I'll tell Copeland — you saved my life.

[The two split up.]

Deacon: Cope, I found your man.
Copeland: Is he alive?

Deacon: Barely. He's headin' back to ya on foot. You might want to send
        someone.

Copeland: I'll do that. Thank you¹ St. John. Copeland out.

HE'S FEEDING THE FREAKS                                                  [SD12]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "You Got the Wrong Guy," Deacon is summoned to the colonel's post.]

Deacon: Colonel — you asked to see me?

Garret: Corporal. Yes. Yes¹ I did. Captain Kouri says that you've been helpful
        dealing with Marauders in the area.

Deacon: Just doing my duty — sir.

Garret: A curious group of Drifters has been spotted moving down Highway 97 —
        evidently, they came over the Thielsen Pass — which I thought to be —
        impassable. Our patrol reported that they were — scarred — the letters
        R.I.P. carved into their foreheads. Have you ever heard of anything
        like this?

Deacon: No, sir. Sounds like — sounds like another cult — like, uh — the
        Anarchists?

Garret: Perhaps. Regardless, I want you to track them down and deal with them.
        We have enough to deal with,¹ I don't need another cult springing up
        in our backyard.

Deacon: No, sir. Last thing we need is another crazy cult.
Garret: I've marked their last known position on your map. Dismissed, Corporal.

[Deacon goes out to hunt the Rippers.]

Deacon: Colonel — I've spotted that, uh — cult that you asked me to check out.
        I'm gonna deal with them.

Garret: Very good, Corporal. Keep me posted. Garret out.

[Deek sneaks into the camp to begin the slaughter, taunting all the while.]

Deacon: Rippers — oh — my Goddamn favorite — What is it, things get a little
        too hot for ya in Iron Butte? How the hell did you get over the pass?
        Remember me, assholes? Maybe head south, start all over again? Nah,
        nah — that ain't gonna happen. Where's your leader? Where's Carlos?
        Oh, that's right — he's dead. I killed him, huh? You hear me? It was
        me! Oh, but Carlos — he ain't resting in peace — he's feeding the
        fucking Freaks. And you're all gonna be feeding the fucking Freaks —

[Finally, the dozen Rippers lie dead.]

Deacon: That's all of 'em — fucking Rippers. Colonel — reporting in. That, uh —
        that cult — R.I.P. — they're no longer a threat.

Garret: Corporal — yes. It's a curious thing. I finally read the complete
        report filed by Captain Thompson — it seems they followed them for
        quite some time before engaging. Evidently, they called themselves
        Rest in Peace — seemed to worship the Freaks — strive to become just
        like them.

Deacon: Well that's pretty fucked — uh — that's pretty messed up¹ sir.

Garret: We're all soldiers here, Corporal. I'm not offended by coarse language.
        But men like that — Rest in Peace — they — offend me.

Deacon: Yes¹ sir.

Garret: They offend me because they show what the world has come to. We —
        Corporal St. John — are all that stand between the world — and the
        abyss.

Deacon: Uh — yes¹ sir. St. John out.

HE'S FULL OF CRAP                                                        [SD13]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "With Other Men's Blood," Deacon returns to Sarah's memorial stone.]

Deacon: Uh, hey. Me again. So uh, I took Boozer into the Lost Lake Camp, and
        — I know — I know, I told you I was never going back there with Iron
        Mike threatening to break my neck and all but — Didn't have a choice.
        See, Boozer — Boozer was gonna die. And¹ uh — well, he still didn't
        wanna go — hell, I didn't wanna go. But — Like I said, I didn't have
        a choice. Neither of us did. So, it didn't matter. He¹ um — He lost the
        arm anyway. And — and now he's stuck — I mean — we're stuck — Goddamn
        Skizzo — You know, I can't remember if I told you about this clown.
        But he's the kind of asshole who's glad all this shit went down. He
        says he was, uh — gang-bangin' — in Sacramento, Fresno, I don't
        remember. But he says he's not from around here. And he's — he's not.
        Claims he was dealing drugs and guns, from California to Oregon, and
        then everything went to hell — And you know what? I think he's full of
        shit. To me, he kinda looks like a frat boy, like he was on the
        lacrosse team, peddling sodas at a — mini-mart — Or — no, no, no, man,
        he would've — He would've had a cushy job at his old man's accounting
        firm, making copies, and getting everyone their morning coffee. You
        know? Making more in a day than I ever made in a week. You know, it's
        this game that Boozer and I used to play, before we rode outta Lost
        Lake for good — We used to call it, uh — "who you were." You know,
        we'd look at someone, we'd try to guess who they were before the shit
        went down, you know? You know, I met a few drug addicts, lotta ex-cons.
        Uh, no accountants. So. That makes sense, if ya think about it. First
        couple of weeks, after the shit went down — I mean, Jesus, that was a
        Freakshow. There's no way some accountant or pencil pusher lived
        through that shit. So I dunno, maybe Skizzo's tellin' the truth — I'm
        not sorry that you missed it. I'm not. Anyway, Boozer and I wanted to
        head north, and — get away from all this shit. But — that — that ain't
        happenin' anytime soon — or — or — Happenin' ever. Uh, hey — look on
        the bright side — Looks like you're¹ uh — stuck with me. Okay. I'll
        stop by later. See ya.

HE'S JUST A KID                                                          [SD14]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "They Will Never Stop," Deek stops by to see Rikki.]

Deacon: Hey¹ Rikki, what's up?

Rikki: Mitchell and a couple guys were on a run northwest of here, when they
       were hit by a group of Drifters. They tracked 'em back to a camp north
       of Melakwa Lake.

Deacon: Okay, so Mitchell — and the others — they didn't take 'em out?

Rikki: They're not Drifters, Deek — and Mitchell's just a kid. I don't even
       know if he can — if he can use a gun —

Deacon: Then what the hell are they doing out in the shit?
Rikki: Look, I need you to do this. Lost Lake needs you.
Deacon: Okay, okay. Great, I'll take care of it.
Rikki: Thank you¹ Deek.

[Deek heads up to the Drifter camp.]

Deacon: Rikki — I'm at Melakwa Lake — yeah, there's a camp full of Drifters
        here.

Rikki: Can you handle them.

Deacon: Uh — yeah, I got this. Deacon out. Alright¹ boys — what, you thought
        you'd just set up camp in Lost Lake territory — have the run of the

[Deek starts slayin'.]

Deacon: Oh, come on — time to clear this camp — Oh, please tell me that's all

        gotta let Rikki know it's done — Uh — Rikki, it's done. I cleared out

Rikki: Thanks¹ Deek — I'll let Iron Mike know.
Deacon: Uh — be sure to let Mitchell know it's safe to play outside again.
Rikki: He's just a kid, Deek.

Deacon: Yeah, well — if he wants to live long enough to become an adult, he

Rikki: Yeah, you're right. I'll start working with him. Thanks¹ Deek.

[A little while afterwards...]

Iron Mike: Deek, ya there? This is Lost Lake, come in.

Deacon: Hey¹ Mike, what's up?

Iron Mike: Rikki told me you took care a' that Drifter camp, north of Melakwa
           Lake.¹

Deacon: Yeah — they won't, uh — be bothering us anymore. Hey¹ Mike, that kid,
        Mitchell, he really shouldn't be goin' out on runs unless he can take
        care of himself —

Iron Mike: Yeah — Goddammit. I'll take care of it. Thanks¹ Deek. Iron Mike out.

HEAR ABOUT A RIPPER CAMP?                                                [SD15]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deek goes to Copeland's camp after being tipped off to a job opportunity.]

Copeland: Deek, good, got something you might be interested in.
Deacon: Yeah, don't be on it¹ Cope. I'm busy.

Copeland: Too busy to hear about a Ripper Camp? Here, in the Cascade
          Wilderness?

Deacon: Rippers, up here? Where?

Copeland: Thought you might be interested. I heard how you and Boozer got hit
          by 'em. In fact, I haven't seen Boozer around much, have I?

Deacon: Where, Cope?

Copeland: Up by Separation Meadow. Flack — you know her, don't you? Saw 'em
          first hand, passed their camp when she was out on a supply run.

Deacon: Don't worry — I'll take care of 'em.

[He rides out.]

Deacon: Boozeman, are you awake? Boozer?
Boozer: Yeah, Deek — just — feelin' a little out of it — y'know?

Deacon: Look, I'm on my way up to Separation Meadow, Cope says there's a Ripper
        camp, up here —

Boozer: Rippers? This far north?

Deacon: Yeah — Boozer, what the hell's going on with these guys? Alkai said the
        Rippers were looking for us, that we had a price on our head.

Boozer: What the hell? How's that possible? I mean, sure, I've killed my share
        of crazy bastards, but I never went outta my way — uh, not that I
        remember —

Deacon: Yeah, that's what I thought. Rippers — Deacon out.

[Deacon comes across the Rippers' camp and engages.]

Deacon: Rippers — this is it — Goddamn Rippers — You wanna get low? Huh? Get
        low! You hurt my brother — you know that? Now I'm gonna hurt you — You
        Ripper sonofabitch — here's your fucking Path — Buncha crazy assholes
        — what're ya doing up here? Huh?

[After the bloodbath, Deek radios in to Mark, then Boozer.]

Deacon: Cope — it's done. The Rippers up here won't bother anyone ever again.

Copeland: St. John — that's good news. I talked to Manny the other day — some
          of the others — I know you've been doing things for the Camp. I just
          wanted to say thank you. Mark Copeland out.

Boozer: Deek — you there? You find that Ripper camp?
Deacon: Yeah, Boozer. I found it.
Boozer: You think — you think they were up here, lookin' for us?

Deacon: I don't know, Boozeman — I was too busy stopping them from cutting my
        eyes out to ask.

Boozer: Sorry¹ brother. I — I wish I'd been there.
Deacon: Sure, man. Yeah, I know. Deacon out.

HERE'S A LITTLE CHAOS                                                    [SD16]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "Not Like I Got a Choice," Deacon returns to Copeland's camp.]

Copeland: Deek — oh — you're not gonna believe this one.

Deacon: I don't know¹ Cope, I seen a lot of unbelievable shit these past couple
        years, try me.

Copeland: You remember the Anarchists?

Deacon: Came through a year ago, maybe more? Killin' anyone in their path?
        Leavin' their little piles of stones everywhere they went?

Deacon: Anarchists — yeah, yeah. We had a couple of run-ins with 'em, back in
        the day.

Copeland: Well — they're back. Two of my people stumbled into their camp while
          out huntin' deer. Only Bender made it back,¹ she said it was
          Anarchists. Each of them had the symbol painted on their face.

Deacon: Jesus, where? Where did she see the camp?

Copeland: I'll mark it on your map. You find 'em and kill every last one of
          'em. We got enough crazy up here dealin' with Rippers — don't need
          Anarchists movin' back in.

Deacon: You got that right,¹ I'll find 'em.

[He eventually finds the Anarchists' hideaway.]

Deacon: Cope, you were right. It's¹ um — Anarchists.

Copeland: You found 'em? Good. Got another report — they hit one of our supply
          runs coming down from Tumalo. Now you go in there and kill 'em all
          like they were roaches hidin' under your bedroll. Let 'em know it
          ain't gonna be like it was last time, when they had the run of the
          place. Cope out.

[As Deacon picks them off, he rages quietly to himself.]

Deacon: Fucking Anarchist — how do ya like that? Things aren't messed up
        enough for ya, huh? Is that it? You thought you'd just ride down into
        our home — tear that shit up, yeah? Oh yeah, here's a little chaos for
        ya — How's this for a little Anarchy — huh?

[Eventually, all twelve are killed.]

Deacon: Cope, it's done. If there's any more of 'em, maybe they'll get the
        message, stay out of our land.

Copeland: I hope you're right — and you just said "our land." You're not
          careful, you might become one of us yet. Cope out.

Deacon: Yeah¹ don't hold your breath.

HOW DO I GET THEM?                                                       [SD17]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "You Can't Be Replaced," Deek visits the colonel on the island.]

Deacon: Colonel — reporting as ordered.

Garret: Corporal St. John. I'm hearing good things about you from Lieutenant
        Weaver and Sarah — Lieutenant Whitaker. They say you're doing a fine
        job.

Deacon: Well, thank you — sir. I'm just trying to be of service.

Garret: I've got another job for you. Drifters have set up camp southeast of
        here, along Highway 97. They are using hit and run tactics — they hit
        our supply runs, then run back to their camp — like the cowards they
        are. It appears they've created a defensive position on the rooftop of
        an old gas station. I've marked it on your map. I've consulted Captain
        Kouri and he feels it would be best to send in a single soldier —
        someone who works well alone, who might be able to use the element of
        surprise.

Deacon: Yes¹ sir — I can do that.

Garret: Very good, Corporal. Report to me when the mission is complete.
        Dismissed.

[Deek heads for the old gas station.]

Deacon: Colonel — St. John reporting. And I'm at that position.
Garret: Were my field reports accurate?
Deacon: Yes¹ sir, they were.
Garret: Do you need reinforcements?

Deacon: No sir. Like you said, I've got the element of surprise — uh — well,
        if I want to use it.

Garret: Carry on, Corporal. Garret out.

Deacon: Gas station rooftop — now, how the hell am I gonna get to 'em? Oh,¹ boy
        I oughta be careful — Surprise 'em? Oh, shit — heavy guns — Armor — 
        oh, great¹ they've got body armor —

[Deek slays the dozen Drifters, including the heavily equipped ones.]

Deacon: That — was the last of 'em — oh my God — Colonel — Corporal St. John
        reporting.

Garret: St. John. Yes. The Marauder Camp. It's been dealt with?
Deacon: Sir, yes¹ sir. As ordered.
Garret: Excellent work, Corporal. Carry on.

[After "No Beginning and No End," Deek goes to Rikki in town.]

       stop him.

        say.

       there?

Deacon: I'm at the sawmill. Goin' after him.

Rikki: Be careful¹ Deacon. Remember, there's —

        Alright¹ Two Dog — where ya hiding?

Deacon: Another MMU — wonder what NERO left behind this time?

[He enters the checkpoint's yard and inspects ripped-up corpses. Two Dog runs
 away as soon as he catches sight of Deacon.]

Deacon: Come on, you sonofabitch.

Two Dog: You're not takin' me — I'm not goin' back —

Deacon: There he is — Two Dog! You got nowhere to run, brother!

[Deacon pursues, eventually finding Two Dog's corpse after he ran into Freaks.]

Deacon: Here we go — guess you won't be turning in any more human ears as
        bounties, will ya? Okay — now I just gotta head back to Rikki.

[Deek returns to Lost Lake.]

Deacon: Here's his knife.

Rikki: Thank God. When Joe Haslin found out he came back, he was terrified. I
       am so relieved.

Deacon: Yeah. Okay — see ya, Rikki.

_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Deacon returns to Sarah's grave after "What Have They Done".]

Deacon: Uh, hey. Me again. I know it doesn't make any sense — me coming up

        Springs, and I know — I know you don't like Tucker, but — well — you

        — what would you think of me? I should've left her where I found her.

        he's getting any better. His arm's — it's pretty messed up — and I
        don't — I don't think that there's much more that I can do for him.

        Rick — don't try to run away —

[Deacon's cover is eventually blown.]

Marsdon: Whatcha doin' out here, St. John? Tucker send ya? They missin' some
         supplies, maybe? We got plenty to spare — Deek? Listen to me — we got
         shit to spare — whatever that old woman is payin' — I'll double it —
         Dammit¹ St. John — listen to me! You don't gotta do this —

[He kills Marsdon and takes a trophy for Tucker.]

Deacon: Hat like this, you deserve to die, Rick "the Prick" —

[Back at Salome...]

Deacon: Hey¹ Tuck, got you a new hat.
Tucker: Nice job. Did he put up much a fight?
Deacon: So, uh — do I get paid more if he did?
Tucker: No.
Deacon: Then why do you care?

Tucker: Just enjoying the thought of how much the sonofabitch suffered before
        he bled out.

Deacon: Well — Jesus, Tuck — I don't do this shit for your entertainment.

IT WAS ON ME                                                             [SD21]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "Lots of Sick People," Deacon returns to Sarah's NERO-site headstone.]

Deacon: Uh, hey. Me again. Boozer says that I shouldn't come up here anymore.
        He keeps — asking me what good's it do, and — and maybe he's right. I
        don't know. He got hurt pretty bad the other day. We ran into some
        Rippers who burned the hell out of his arm, and it looks pretty bad.
        I broke into one of those — uh, what the hell do you call them — the
        — Mobile Medical Units — and I got him sterile bandages. And I — hope
        it's enough, you know? But — Boozer, you know — he says he's fine. But
        I — I don't — I don't think so. Shit looks pretty bad to me. See the
        thing is — it was on me. I risked his life — for a bike part. A Goddamn
        bike part. Not that it mattered. Sonofabitch Copeland parted it out
        anyway. Took me a year to put that bike together. You would've liked
        it. It's not as nice as the one I taught you to ride on. But it got me
        around. Do you remember that — tank, that you had painted for me? Well,
        that was the only thing left of that old hog, and now it's — gone too.
        Soon as I get it back together — my bike, I mean — and get Boozer
        patched up, we're gonna ride north. Fresh start — you know, lotta
        memories around here. Too many. Anyway — I guess I'm just sayin' that,
        uh — I might not see you again, you know?

JUST CHECKING IN                                                         [SD23]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "We Couldn't Take the Risk," Deek rides out to the radio tower atop
 Applegate Peak. Deacon clears it of Marauders. As a reward, Cope's broadcast
 plays.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. It's the
          Wild West again, and some men are actin' like law and order are a
          thing of the past. But last I checked, this is still the United
          States of America! And in America, the right of property shall not
          be infringed. We have the right to claim territory, to hold it, and
          to defend it. Sure, we took this land from the Indians — no point in
          rewriting history — but we took it by force, and force is the only
          thing that will move us now. We're not gonna roll over for a bunch
          of bullies. If the Feds, or Rippers, or Marauders think they're gonna
          come rolling into my wilderness, they got another thing coming! The
          strongest survive, the strongest take, and the strongest will
          succeed. This is Mark Copeland for Radio Free Oregon. Don't believe
          the lies.

Deacon: Listen to Cope. Law and order are a thing of the past,¹ what the hell
        are you talking about? But¹ yeah — you got a point about force being
        the only thing that matters now. Force — and a lotta Goddamn ammo.

[With the foes gone, Deek climbs the tower to contact Boozer at Lost Lake.]

Deacon: I hope this is high enough — Boozer, it's Deacon. Come back. Lost Lake
        Camp, is anyone there?

Boozer: Deek? Deek, is that you? I can barely hear you. You're — you're cuttin'
        out. Where the hell are you?

Deacon: Crater Lake — believe it or not. Hey — uh, I — I —

Boozer: It's good to hear from you again, brother — uh — thought maybe, uh —
        thought maybe you were headin' back.

Deacon: No — Boozer — not yet — it's, uh — it's complicated. Look, uh — I'm
        just — I'm just sorta checkin' in, to see how — you know — how
        everything's going?

Boozer: Good — good, Deek. Things are goin' good. You will never guess who the
        old man put in charge of security —

Deacon: Wait, you?

Boozer: Yeah, you got it. Guess he figured — you know, with only one arm, I can
        only cause half as much trouble.

Deacon: Okay — yeah, like I said, I just — I just wanted to check in.
Boozer: Yeah, it was good to hear from you, brother.
Deacon: Yeah — you too.

JUST DOING MY JOB                                                        [SD24]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "You Can't Be Replaced," Deek is called into Kouri's camp.]

Kouri: Corporal St. John. I've got an important assignment for you.
Deacon: Yes¹ sir — whatever I can do to help.

Kouri: We sent a patrol north along Highway 97 to investigate a group of —
       Anarchists. Have you ever had a run-in with them before?

Deacon: Anarchists — the assholes who left those little fucking cairns all
        over the place? Yeah — yeah, I've met 'em once or twice — uh — way
        back in the day. I — I, uh — thought they were all killed off.

Kouri: Evidently not. I've marked their location on your map. I'm sending you
       in alone in case any of our men are being held —

Deacon: Yeah, I get it. I'll have a better chance of getting 'em out alive.
        Got it.

Kouri: The patrol commander — Sergeant Mitch Allen — is a personal friend of
       mine.

Deacon: Yes¹ sir. I'll — uh — I'll do what I can.
Kouri: I'm counting on you, Corporal. Dismissed.

[In the snowy Kerr Valley, Deacon searches for clues.]

Deacon: Militia tracks — Okay, Militia gear — looks like they got dragged
        off — More tracks — A cairn — yep — Goddamn Anarchists — This is it —
        Tracks lead this way — A mine — yeah, this is it — Hey¹ Captain. I've
        found 'em. Looks like they're holed up in a mine.

Kouri: Are they holding hostages? Are they alive?

Deacon: Uh — I don't know yet. But if they are, I'll get to 'em. Sir — um —
        if they have your friend, I'll find him.

Kouri: Thank you — Kouri out.

[A firefight soon ensues.]

Deacon: Anarchists — yeah — this is definitely it. Anarchist symbols — gotta
        be the place. Where they hiding ya? A mine — another Goddamn mine.
        Another Anarchist sign — You fuckin' Anarchists. Hate every Goddamn
        one of ya. Hey, why aren't ya guys just out, like, you know¹ stacking
        up little piles a' rocks — huh? So you boys just thought you'd set up
        camp and pick off Militia supply runs, is that it? A cairn — yep —
        Goddamn Anarchists. Hey — ya want some anarchy? How about this? Hey!
        Ya like chaos? Huh? Ya like shit being all fucked up?

[Deek heads further into the mine.]

Deacon: Alright¹ Allen — Allen, you gotta be in here somewhere — Another
        Anarchist sign — Where are they hiding ya? Goddamn big mine —

[He eventually comes upon a hostage being beaten severely.]

Deacon: That's the last of 'em. Good riddance. There he is — Heya¹ Sarge —
        you must be Mitch Allen?

Mitch: I was a goner — thank you — thank you, man — I thought it was over —
Deacon: I'll bet — are you — uh — good to get outta here on your own?

Mitch: Okay, alright — thanks, man, I owe you my life — I'm headin' back — I'll
       tell 'em what you did, I swear to ya —

Deacon: Just doing my job.

[Mitch leaves and Deacon soon follows. Freaks stream in following him.]

Deacon: Uh — hey — where'd you go? Or — oh — okay. Have I been down this
        tunnel? That's gotta be the way out — There — I see daylight —

[He finally makes it out, leaving the Anarchists to fight a gigantic horde.]

Deacon: Captain, I, uh, found your man. He should be on his way back to
        Diamond Lake.

Kouri: Good work, St. John.
Deacon: I'll radio back, check on him later. St. John out.

[Later...]

Deacon: Hey, Captain. Did¹ uh — Sarge make it back okay?

Kouri: He's in the infirmary now. I think he'll make a full recovery. Thanks
       to you.

Deacon: Well, just doing my job — sir.

Kouri: Well — that was one helluva job. Thank you — Corporal. From both Mitch
       and myself.

Deacon: Uh — yes¹ sir. St. John out.

LEAVE ALL THAT BY THE DOOR                                               [SD25]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "A War We Can Win," Deacon radios in to Weaver.]

Weaver: Yeah, sure. I should have written that shit down for you. It comes

Deacon: Yes¹ sir.

Weaver: Hey, between you and me? If the Colonel isn't around, stop with all
        the "yes sir, no sir" bullshit — alright? Makes me feel old.

[Deacon rides up toward the aforementioned mine.]
Taylor: St. John. Cor — por — al St. John — you got your ears on, man? Does
        this — does this thing even work? I don't think this radio's workin' —

Deacon: Taylor — yeah, your radio works. What's up?

Taylor: Deacon St. John! Hey — uh — I mean, you know, nothin' — just — just —
        just checkin' in on ya. I haven't — seen ya since the whole "swearin'
        in" thing — that was some shit, am I right?

Deacon: Taylor — you know — I'm kinda busy —

Taylor: What? Hey, hey — what — what the — what the hell — ya got — they got
        ya doin', huh? I'm — I'm — in the damn infantry or some shit. Spend
        all day burnin' out nests, choppin' down trees — haulin' wood. So,
        sorry — sorry, what're you doing?

Deacon: Research — they got me goin' out into the shit, finding supplies for
        the officers working on — what —

Taylor: Oh shit! Oh, I heard about that. Yeah, yeah — workin' on — uh — on,
        uh — bioweapons, uh — chemical weapons, shit like that. Burn them
        Freaks to the ground! Am I right?

Deacon: Yeah. Look, Taylor — I gotta go.

Taylor: Alright, alright. Hey, hey, um — hey — look, man — it's, uh — it's
        just — I'm — I'm — I'm havin' second thoughts about all this — military
        — shit, you know —

Deacon: Taylor — what radio are you on? Are you sure that you're — not being
        monitored?

Taylor: Oh, shit —
Deacon: Huh — that's what I thought. Gotta go. St. John out.

[There may be another Taylor convo if it isn't heard elsewhere first.]

Taylor: Corporal Deacon St. John — hey, you got your ears on, man? Hey —
Deacon: Taylor? Whaddya need?

Taylor: There you are — okay — uh — so I finally figured out how to use this
        damn thing. Alright, I got a secure channel and everything. So how's
        it going, man?

Deacon: Taylor, I'm kinda busy right now — so —

Taylor: Yeah — yeah, yeah, yeah. Sorry¹ man, sorry. Uh — hey, so — word's out
        in the camp that drugs are makin' their way in, right under the
        Colonel's nose. It's good stuff too. But — do you know anything about
        that?

Deacon: I don't do drugs, Taylor, so no, I don't know anything about it. Why?

Taylor: No, no, no, no, no — no, no, I don't — I don't either. I'm just — I
        saw this guy, you know, one of the new recruits, actin' all suspicious
        — he rides in and out of camp all the time. And so I thought — I
        thought I'd follow him, right? See what the hell he's about.

Deacon: Goddammit, Taylor — listen to me. You just go to Kouri, let him handle
        it. You got that?

Taylor: Yeah, yeah — yeah, yeah. That's a — good call. Yeah. Okay, Mr. — St.
        John. I'll, uh — I'll talk to you later, man. Uh — out.

Deacon: Oh, Jesus Christ, Taylor. What the hell are you doing?

[Deacon finally arrives in front of the mine and its abandoned buildings.]

Deacon: Lieutenant Weaver. You there? I'm at the mine.

Weaver: Good, good. Okay¹ man — you take a look around. The report I saw listed
        ore testing kits,¹ you're gonna need one.

Deacon: An ore testing kit. Copy that.

Weaver: Uh — cinnabar is kinda red, but not shiny — it'll have a dull luster
        to it. Gonna be hard to miss. Test the ore — it's gotta be at least
        60% pure or I can't use it.

Deacon: Alright, got it. Testing kit, testing kit — where the hell am I gonna
        find an ore testing kit? Maybe — one of these, uh — shacks? Nothin' in
        here.

[He checks another.]

Deacon: Fuel can. Huh. I need — a testing kit,¹ I don't need fuel.

[With some difficulty, Deacon enters the third shack.]

Deacon: Here we go. Ore testing kit. Yeah.

[He drops down to the vehicle-blocked entrance, clears the path, and enters.]

Deacon: Okay, okay — what did he say? Red rock, dull luster. Cinnabar. Yeah.
        And now I just gotta test it. Come on — yeah. You'll do.

[Deacon goes down a one-way shaft to find two more deposits.]

Deacon: Here we go. Cinnabar. And now I just gotta test it. Alright — Gotta
        find more ore. Mining pump. They musta had problems with flooding,
        even back in the day. I just gotta get it — uh — well — turned on.

[He kills some Freaks hiding by old machinery.]

Deacon: That's the last of 'em. Let's see if this pump is workin'. Genny's out
        of gas — genny's always out of gas — Here we go. Done.

[The roar of the generator is complemented by screaming Freaks nearby.]

Deacon: Oh shit. Okay — that's not good. And we got green lights. Green lights
        are good.

[He kills the attackers.]

Deacon: More Cinnabar. That's good. Good. Okay, good. Okay — let's test you
        out — Yeah — almost enough.

[He can hear water being sucked through the pipes.]

Deacon: Yeah — that's it. Water's goin' down. Gotta finish collecting this ore,
        and then I gotta get the hell outta here.

[Deek kills the Freaks hiding near the other cinnabar samples.]

Deacon: Here's some more. Okay — let's test you out — Come on — yeah. You'll
        do. One or two more samples is all I need. Cinnabar? Yeah — Testing —
        Alright — Just one more. Here's some more. Yes, you'll work. Come on,
        ore — let's see how pure you are —

[He realizes he's just short of his quota.]

Deacon: Okay, need more ore. Elevator shaft — oh, Goddammit — wonder where
        this goes. Only one way to find out.

[The lift goes up to a bloody detritus-filled tunnel system.]

Deacon: Huh — what's up here? Another tunnel. Looks like this one was abandoned
        a long time ago. Huh — haven't been up here before —

[In one area is a blinking red light.]

Deacon: A NERO beacon — in here?

[Deek exits into fresh air.]

Deacon: Lieutenant Weaver, this is St. John. I've got the cinnabar you asked
        for.

Weaver: St. John — good, good. I'm almost ready for it. Um — oh! Hold on a
        second. Can I help you¹ Lieutenant?

Sarah: Weaver, I ran out of isopropyl alcohol. Do you have any?
Weaver: Yeah, I got a bottle of vodka back in my tent — stop by later.
Sarah: Jesus, you never give up, do you?
Weaver: Don't be such a stranger!
Sarah: Fuck off!

[Sarah leaves.]

Weaver: St. John — yeah, sorry about that. Anyway, yeah, just drop off the ore
        as soon as you can. I got some more shit I need you to get. Weaver out.

[Back at Wizard Island, Deacon enters Weaver's tent and salutes.]

Deacon: Lieutenant — 

Weaver: Nah, man. Leave that shit by the door. No, no, no — no. I mean all that
        army shit.

Deacon: Oh — Okay. Uh —

[He puts the cinnabar on the table.]

Deacon: Think that's what you were looking for.
Weaver: Alright. Yeah — yeah, this is great. Hey, just wait a second — Here.

[He hands him another requisition form.]

Deacon: Polystyrene.

Weaver: Yeah, you know, like white, foam coffee cups — Packing peanuts, shit
        like that.

Deacon: Yeah, got it.
Weaver: Hey¹ man — by the way, how did it go? With the Wizard Island Witch?
Deacon: You mean Lieutenant Whitaker?
Weaver: Man, I thought you were gonna leave all that shit by the door?

[Deacon salutes.]

Weaver: That'll be all, Corporal. That'll be all.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "They Will Never Stop," Deek can taunt Skizzo outside the cabin where
 he's undergoing house arrest.]

Deacon: You know what? I think we're gonna do that whether they find you guilty

Skizzo: Deek! Deek! Dammit! Listen to me, Deek! I'm sorry, brother. I'm sorry!
        I didn't want to do it but I had to — and I didn't mean for it to go
        down this way. Deek! Listen to me! Deek!

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "I've Got a Plan," Deacon returns to the radio tower to chat up Boozer.]

Deacon: Boozer, you there? Lost Lake Camp, come in.

Deacon: It's¹ uh — everything's fine, Boozeman. It's, uh — I'm okay.

        brother?

        Okay — I'm gonna grab Iron Mike, uh — uh — Rikki, some men — look,

        — Drifters, Squatters, campers — makes no difference to them.

Deacon: Look, I got this — I got this figured out. Just — if anything happens

MY EYES HAVE BEEN OPENED                                                 [SD28]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "This One's on Me," Deek attents another of Garret's sermons.]

Garret: This day, as the sun sets on this island — It also sets on the life of
        a great man — Captain Arturo Jiminez — "Doc" to many of you — is gone.
        Taken from us on the eve — of our great victory. Captain Jiminez was
        murdered — slaughtered — his life ripped from him — His blood, even
        now — soaks the tent where he toiled — Hour after hour, tending our
        sick, our injured, our wounded. The great tragedy here is not that a
        good man needlessly lost his life — though for that I am indeed, very
        sorry. The great tragedy here is that he could not be replaced. Doctor
        Jiminez was the only trained physician in our ranks — perhaps — in all
        the world. My eyes have been opened. I see now the great mistake we
        have made. We have filled our ark with books and seeds and discs.
        Medical journals, medical books, and encyclopedia¹ — we have in spades.
        But who now — when this terrible war is over — will teach us how to use
        them? Journals can be replaced. Books and encyclopedia¹ can be
        replaced. Doctor Jiminez — our only doctor — cannot be replaced. I go
        now to grieve in private. I suggest you all do the same. Company
        dismissed.

NEVER GIVE UP HOPE                                                       [SD29]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "We Will Take Back This World," Deacon is assigned to hostage rescue.
 He goes out to the mountainous site.]

Deacon: Colonel, Corporal St. John reporting in, and I'm at the last location
        where Lieutenant Norwood was seen — uh, it seems pretty fortified, sir.
        Are you — are you sure you want me to tackle this alone?

Garret: Just — follow orders, Corporal. Garret out.

Deacon: Yes¹ sir. Fuckin' a¹ —

[He descends to the railroad tracks. An errant bike is nearby.]

Deacon: Okay, Militia bike — that's gotta be hers. Okay — come on, you assholes
        — let's do this —

[Deek starts gunning down the kidnappers in record time.]

Deacon: Lieutenant, you in here?
Justine: In here! I'm in here!
Deacon: Okay — hang on — I'm comin' —

[He finds the woman tied to a railroad stake in the ground.]

Deacon: Okay, hang on, I'm comin'. How the hell you doin', Lieutenant?
Justine: St. John. Thank God, I'd given up hope.

Deacon: Oh yeah? Well, a good friend a' mine once told me — never give up hope.
        Because you lose that, you may as well just pack it in.

Justine: Keep that in mind next time I'm ambushed by a dozen Squatters.

Deacon: You okay? Alright, listen. Camp's clear and your bike is still in one
        piece¹ so can you just get back alone, huh?

Justine: Yeah, I can handle it. Thank you, St. John.
Deacon: Sure, now get goin', go!

[Justine leaves and Deacon starts driving back to camp.]

Deacon: Colonel, sir. Reporting in. It's, uh — well, Jesus — it wasn't easy.
        But I got her out. Lieutenant Norwood is out.

Garret: Good work, Corporal. I'll send a patrol out now.

Deacon: She said she could make it on her own. So, uh — I'll radio in later,
        make sure she made it. St. John out.

[Later...]

Deacon: Colonel, sir. Just checkin' in on Lieutenant Norwood.

Garret: Corporal. I've just read her report. She claims that you — took out an
        entire Drifter camp — single-handedly?

Deacon: Well — uh — I wasn't about to leave her in there alone — sir.

Garret: Very good, Corporal. Captain Kouri has put your name in for a
        promotion. I'm beginning to see why.

NICE AND BLOODY                                                          [SD30]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Around the time of "What Did You Do?", Deacon gets asked to visit Salome Hot
 Springs again for a job.]

Tucker: Deek, you ever ride with a Drifter, scars all over his face, carries a
        tire iron, goes by the name of Limbo.

Deacon: Don't know him.

Tucker: He came into camp yesterday, to turn in some bounties, have a few
        drinks — seems like he didn't leave until early this morning.

Deacon: Well Tuck, I don't run security here, so why don't you just tell Alkai
        about that —

Tucker: He beat a man, Deek, and a woman, to death. Bowman and Hewitt. Her face
        was so smashed in, you couldn't tell it was her.

Deacon: Hewitt — Maria, right? Jesus. This asshole — Limbo — he's a local?

Tucker: Alkai says they've set up shop at the old Forest Service watch tower,
        on the east slope of Three Fingered Jack.

Deacon: Yeah, I know where it is, and uh — I'l handle it.

Tucker: I thought you might.

[Deacon rides out to the mountain and finds a medium-sized enemy encampment.]

Deacon: Hey Tuck, I'm here. And yeah, looks like Limbo and his crew are calling
        the place home, like nothin' ever happened. You said his face was
        scarred, so uh — I mean — more please. What else can you tell me?

Tucker: He wears a green coat. Looks like a Goddamn leprechaun. You bring me
        his tire iron, Deacon St. John — and I want it covered in what's left
        of the sonofabitch's face.

Deacon: I hear ya. Uh — St. John out.

[As Deacon infiltrates silently, he can hear the murderer's ongoing monologue.]

Limbo: See old "iron tooth" here? You wanna get all nice and cozy with him?
       Like — me puttin' him right up alongside your Goddamn face? That old
       bitch is gonna be sendin' some men out here and me an' "iron tooth"¹
       wanna be ready — You don't need no dentist with ol' "iron tooth" around,
       do ya? He'll just pop up and there and knock 'em all out at once, now
       won't he? Oh — "iron tooth" — he's gettin' kinda thirsty — oh? — Oh,
       what's that "iron tooth," you thirsty? You wanna drink somethin' warm,
       somethin' — red and thick and — gooey? Well, maybe I can help you with
       that — Come on, you sorry sonsofbitches — I want this camp locked down
       or you gonna answer to Limbo and his pal "iron tooth" —

Deacon: Huh — there you are — Okay — alright Limbo — where you at — Yeah —
        thought you'd stop by the Hot Springs — have a little fun, is that it?

[If alerted, Limbo flees upstairs.]

Deacon: He's gotta be up on that tower — Where the fuck are you?

[After looting the main enemy:]

Deacon: Still got old "iron tooth" on you, yeah?

[He returns to Salome afterwards.]

Tucker: You find that sonofabitch?
Deacon: Yeah. Here's old "iron tooth". Just like ya asked.

Tucker: Nice work. Deek? You were always the one person I could count on to
        get things done. You know, I have no idea where you and Boozer rode
        off to, but it's good to see you.

Deacon: Well, we're around, Tuck. And if you need anything, you know how to
        reach me.

Tucker: Go see Alkai,¹ I'll update your credits.

[Later, a new RFO broadcast plays.]

Copeland: This is Radio Free Oregon. The Truth Shall Set You Free. Back during
          the American Revolution, when we were fightin' for our freedoms, we
          gained the beautiful right to keep and bear arms. A right we used to
          protect ourselves, our families, our property. That is, until the
          evergrowin' Federal Government got scared of the people they swore
          to protect. Over the years, they stripped us of ever gun right they
          could, using a few mass shootings as an excuse to curtail the
          God-given rights of us, American Citizens. "Gun Control." And there
          went the Second Amedment, ladies and gentlemen. Let me ask you this:
          When all this shit went down, if every American was packin' heat, do
          you think we'd be in this mess? Hell. No. But this is how the Feds
          wanted it. Disarming the public was just the first step toward
          gettin' rid of us all. So who did those "gun laws" really protect?
          Sure as hell wasn't us, the American taxpayers. Someday, we ever dig
          outta this, I want to take a poll. I bet those who survived, were
          those who had guns. This is Mark Copeland for Radio Free Oregon.
          Don't believe the lies.

[After "That's His Mistake," Deacon goes to see Rikki in town.]

Iron Mike: Point well taken. See ya¹ Deek. Iron Mike out.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
PART OF THE FAMILY                                                       [SD34]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "Have It Your Way," Deek is called back to Salome.]

Tucker: Deek — I got a job for you — one only you can handle.
Deacon: Whaddya got?

Tucker: You remember the other day, I took you by the dig site? Food came up
        missing?

Deacon: Yeah. Wheeler was on watch.

Tucker: He was doing more than watching. He was robbing us blind. He and a few
        men took off, to a camp north of Patjens Lake. You know the one?

Deacon: Yeah. I know it.

Tucker: Find the bastard and kill him. He's got a pocket watch — still works.
        Bring it to me.

Deacon: Wheeler. Got it.

[He rides north, near the NERO checkpoint where Sarah's memorial stone is.]

Deacon: This is it — this has gotta be Wheeler's camp — Gotta go in on foot.
        Wheeler — there's that sonofabitch —

[If Deek reveals his presence somehow:]

Wheeler: Goddammit — Who is that? That you, St. John? That old bitch got you
         doin' her dirty work now? That it? You bein' the old hag's little
         errand boy? We rode together, brother! Deek — you sonofabitch — I
         tried, man — I tried — Deek — come on¹ man — it's me, Deek! Come on,
         man — don't gotta be like this. Uh — join up with us! Fuck Alkai and
         his bullshit, am I right? I know you don't like that sonofabitch —

[He kills Wheeler for his timepiece.]

Deacon: Pocket watch — here it is.

[Back at Salome...]

Deacon: Tucker, I got him.
Tucker: Nice job. I guess Wheeler's sorry he messed with Ada Tucker now.
Deacon: No — I'm guessin' he's not feeling a whole lot of anything.

Tucker: I've updated your credits. And you wait and see — I'm still gonna find
        a way to talk you and Boozer into joining us here — become a part of
        the family.

Deacon: Yeah — good luck with that.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
RIPPERS, REST IN HELL                                                    [SD35]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "Not Like I Got a Choice," Deacon returns to Salome at Tuck's behest.]

Tucker: Deacon, thank God.
Deacon: What's wrong, Tuck?
Tucker: It's Rippers. More Goddamned Rippers.
Deacon: Oh good, Rippers. Okay, where?

Tucker: They keep coming over the Iron Butte pass. Now they've set up a camp
        along Bear Creek, just south of here. I'm afraid, Deek. If we don't
        stop them, what's going to happen to the Hot Springs?

Deacon: I get it, I get it — don't worry about this, Tuck. I got this.

[Deek arrives at the streamside bivouac.]

Deacon: Hey¹ Tuck, I'm at that Ripper Camp and it doesn't look like there's
        too many of 'em, so — you know — must be a scouting party.

Tucker: Kill 'em — kill 'em all, Deek.

Deacon: Yeah, Tuck. You don't gotta tell me. St. John out. Goddamn Rippers. My
        friend — lost an arm because of you bastards — You wanna Rest in Peace?
        I can help you out with that — Come on you sonsofbitches — come on.
        You wanna get low, huh?

[All six lay dead soon enough.]

Deacon: Goddamn Rippers — rest — in hell — the lot of ya. Well, I better get
        back, so — okay — uh — okay, I gotta just turn this in to Tucker —
        Tucker, it's done.

Tucker: Did you get them all?

Deacon: Uh — yeah¹ Tuck, I got 'em all. Isn't that what you're paying me for?

Tucker: Sorry. It's just — this is the third time they've come up here —
        attacking our camp, taking and killing that poor girl, Lisa — we have
        to stop 'em¹ Deek, we have to.

Deacon: Uh — Tuck — sonofabitch — uh — listen — I've been to Iron Butte — and,
        uh — I've seen part of what they're building —

Tucker: What? When — how did you —

Deacon: No — it doesn't matter. But trust me on this — there's too many of 'em
        — hundreds, maybe — maybe thousands — and if they decide to come north,
        you ain't gonna stop 'em. You just ain't. Alright? So just keep doin'
        what you're doin' — you kill any that cross the border, and that's
        gonna let Carlos know that he ain't moving north without a fight. It's
        the best you can do. St. John out.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
SHE RODE WITH US                                                         [SD36]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[Shortly after "Smoke on the Mountain," Boozer radios in with a side job.]

Boozer: Deek? You there? Did — did you say you were headin' north?
Deacon: Boozeman — no. You know I wouldn't — ride north without you.
Boozer: Yeah, yeah — I know. I'm just — kinda — out of it.
Deacon: Well, third degree burns'll do that to ya.
Boozer: Yeah — so — take care of Alvarez. You know? Deek — it means a lot to
        me.

Deacon: I'll take care of her, Boozer — just, get some rest. Deacon out.

[He finds Alvarez's corpse still near the Old Pioneer Cemetery. He throws a
 molotov on it to keep anything from desecrating it.]

Deacon: Rest in peace. They can't get you now.

[Later, after "They're Not Sleeping," Deacon talks with Boozer about it.]

Deacon: Boozer, you there?
Boozer: Yeah, Deek —
Deacon: I took care of it. Alvarez, I mean.
Boozer: Thanks, brother. She'd do the same for us.
Deacon: Yeah, she would have. Deacon out.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
STILL BREATHING                                                          [SD37]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "This One's on Me," Deek is called back to Garret in town.]

Garret: Corporal St. John. We have a situation — that I think you can help us
        with.

Deacon: Okay — sir.

Garret: One of our soldiers has been taken hostage — Sergeant Melinda Foster —
        in charge of patrolling our eastern border, along the 97 corridor. Her
        squad was ambushed. Two men made it back — alive. Sergeant Foster was
        taken.

Deacon: Melinda Foster —
Garret: Do you know her?
Deacon: No¹ sir, I don't.

Garret: I've marked her last known location on your map. I have full confidence
        — Corporal — that you will return her safely.

Deacon: You can count on me, sir.
Garret: Dismissed, Corporal.

[Deek goes up onto the southern highway above Crater Lake's rim.]

Deacon: A Militia bike — it's gotta be hers —

[He tracks her captors to a nearby radio tower installation.]

Deacon: Colonel — Corporal St. John reporting in. Sir. I'm at that location —
        and the, uh — camp appears to be empty.

Garret: Sergeant Foster's life is in your hands, Corporal. Don't let me down.

Deacon: Nope — sir. I'll find her.

[He creeps in, only to find ambushers waiting. He lays 'em to rest soon after.]

Deacon: That's all of 'em? Looks like — just another day at the office —

[He jimmies the door to the main building, finding Foster and a captor.]

Torturer: I'll kill her — I swear —

[Deacon immediately puts him down.]

Deacon: How you doing, Sarge? How's your day going so far?
Foster: Jesus, Corporal. Thank you. It's going great. Just great.
Deacon: Do you need a lift back?
Foster: You see a Militia bike out front? Or did the bastards part it out?
Deacon: No, no. It's still there.

Foster: Okay, I'm good then. St. John, right? Thank you. I can get back on my
        own.

[Foster leaves.]

Deacon: Colonel — found Sergeant Foster. She's headin' back now.
Garret: Good work, Corporal.

Deacon: Thank you, sir. I'll, uh — I'll check back in later, see how she's
        doing. St. John out.

[Later...]

Deacon: Colonel — sir. Reporting in.
Garret: Yes?

Deacon: Corporal St. John, sir. I — I wanted to check to see how Sergeant
        Foster was doing.

Garret: Foster, yes, yes, uh — she'll be fine. Thank you, Corporal. Her report
        contained high praise for your actions and bravery. You are to be —
        commended.

Deacon: Well, thank you — sir. She's, um — she's a survivor.
Garret: We're all survivors, aren't we?
Deacon: Yes¹ sir. St. John out.

¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯
TAKE BACK WHAT'S MINE                                                    [SD38]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[During "I've Had Better Days," the colonel radios in.]

Garret: St. John — Corporal St. John. Come in. I need you to report to me ASAP.
Deacon: Hey¹ Colonel — uh — yes¹ sir. St. John out.

[If he reports in promptly, there's dialogue at Wizard Island.]

Deacon: Colonel, sir. Reporting in as ordered.

Garret: Corporal. Good. Good. How are things progressing with Lieutenant
        Weaver? Lieutenant Whitaker?

Deacon: Uh — good, Sir. I usually have a couple of requisition forms that I
        need to fill for them. Uh — they're — they are keeping me busy.

Garret: Good. I have another assignment — one that can use your tracking
        skills. One of our — workers — has escaped. Her name was — Adkins,
        Crystal. She's easy to identify — her face is covered with tattoos —
        prison tattoos.

Deacon: Mm-hmm. Yeah, the night I was sworn in — she was brought in with me
        and Private Taylor —

Garret: Exactly so. Apparently she didn't like her work assignment. Before
        dawn, she bribed a guard and stole a bike. Before she left, she broke
        into the ark and stole some jewellery.

Deacon: Jewellery, sir?

Garret: The rank and file are not allowed to wear jewellery of any kind,
        Corporal, as you well know. Her rings were — confiscated — when she
        arrived. I guess she wanted them back. I — want them returned.

Deacon: But she didn't enlist — she — um —

Garret: Don't question orders, soldier. She knows too much about our compound,
        our defences. She is a — problem — and we can't afford — problems. Am
        I understood, Corporal?

Deacon: Yes¹ sir.

Garret: I've marked her last known position on your map. Kouri tells me she was
        first seen at a logging camp, to the north. I'd start there — maybe she
        has — friends in the area who are helping her. Dismissed¹ Corporal.

[Deek heads northeast of Crater Lake and finds a smoldering bike nearby.]

Deacon: Colonel. I'm at the location where she was last spotted.
Garret: You found her?

Deacon: Not yet, but, uh — I see an abandoned Militia bike — so — she can't
        have gone far.

Garret: Very good, Corporal. Carry out your orders. Garret out.
Deacon: Militia bike — that's gotta be hers.

[Deek visits the logging camp and finds it occupied by brigands.]

Deacon: Oh, good, Marauders. Are these your friends, Crystal? Because they
        don't look too friendly —

[Deacon kills the dozen.]

Deacon: Oh, yeah — that's all of 'em — Uh — one of those shacks — In here —
        gotta be in here —

[He breaks in, finding Crystal battered and tied to a chair.]

Deacon: Oh, man, you keep pickin' the wrong friends.
Crystal: Screw you.
Deacon: Hey, hey. You — you don't remember me.¹

Crystal: Oh, I remember you. Standing up on that stage, kissing the Colonel's
         ass like a good little soldier.

Deacon: Well, Jesus Christ. Do you know why I'm here?

Crystal: I figure the sonofabitch Colonel put a bounty on my head. So do it
         already. I don't give a shit. What the hell are you doing?

[Deek unties her.]

Deacon: I'm not gonna kill ya. I just — I need the rings.

Crystal: Those are my Goddamn rings. The sonofabitches stole 'em from me,
         they're mine.

Deacon: Yeah, yeah they are. But it's either the rings or your life. So what's
        it gonna be?

Crystal: You can go to hell.
Deacon: You're welcome!

[He lets her run off and returns to Garret on the island.]

Deacon: Colonel, sir. Reporting in. I'm — uh — returning the stolen property.

Garret: Corporal. Yes. The worker — common thief and murderer. Did she put up
        a fight?

Deacon: Yes, sir. Yes — yes¹ she did, uh — she put up a hell of a fight. But
        it was nothing that I couldn't handle.

Garret: You fight on the side of righteousness, Corporal. Don't give it another
        thought. It is those like her — liars, thieves, murderers, drug
        addicts — criminals all — who brought this scourge down upon us. I
        will not weep to see them gone — every one. Dismissed¹ Corporal.

Deacon: Yes¹ sir. I'll — I'll get back to work.

THROW THEM INTO THE FURNACE                                              [SD39]
_______________________________________________________________________________
¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯¯

[After "You Couldn't Stop Shaking," Deacon attends another Garret soliloquy.]

Garret: My brothers and sisters in arms — I stand here before you — in
        celebration. The end — is nigh. Captain Kouri has been working nonstop,
        assembling and training our army. Lieutenant Whitaker — has been
        working tirelessly on a biological weapon — That will allow us to kill
        hundreds of Freaks at once. Lieutenant Weaver is working on a chemical
        weapon — that will allow us to burn down entire Hordes. Soon, slash and
        burn will be a thing of the past. We will go from fighting a defensive
        war — to an offensive war — As we take the fight to the Freaks, as we
        work to retake our world. And behold, He said — the enemy who sowed
        them is the devil, and the harvest is the end of the age; and the
        reapers are angels. And they will gather out of His kingdom all evil,
        and throw them into the furnace of fire — In that place, there will be
        weeping — and wailing — and gnashing of teeth. We — the Deschutes
        County Militia — are — those avenging angels. And — we are coming.
        Company dismissed.
